$$\begin{split} \bigg| \Pr \Big[ \mathcal{A}(i\mathcal{O}(1^{\lambda}, C_0), \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux}}) &= 1 : (C_0, C_1, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{B}(1^{\lambda}) \Big] - \\ \Pr \Big[ \mathcal{A}(i\mathcal{O}(1^{\lambda}, C_1), \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux}}) &= 1 : (C_0, C_1, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux}}) \leftarrow \mathcal{B}(1^{\lambda}) \Big] \bigg| \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda). \end{split}$$

### <span id="page-23-0"></span>3.5 Quantum Information

In this section, we recall some quantum information results.

We first recall the gentle measurement lemma, which says that if some measurement has a high probability of giving a particular outcome on some state, then the measurement can be implemented in a way so that the state will not be disturbed too much when that outcome occurs.

<span id="page-23-3"></span>**Lemma 1** (Gentle Measurement Lemma [Win99]). Let  $\rho$  be a mixed state acting on  $\mathbb{C}^d$ . Let U be a unitary and  $(\Pi_0, \Pi_1 = I - \Pi_0)$  be projectors all acting on  $\mathbb{C}^d \otimes \mathbb{C}^{d'}$ . We interpret  $(U, \Pi_0, \Pi_1)$  as a measurement performed by appending an ancillary system of dimension d' in the state  $|0\rangle\langle 0|$ , applying U and then performing the projective measurement  $\Pi_0, \Pi_1$  on the larger system. Assuming that the outcome corresponding to  $\Pi_0$  has probability  $1 - \epsilon$ , we have

$$|\rho - \rho'| \le \sqrt{\epsilon}$$

where  $\rho'$  is the state after performing the measurement, undoing the unitary U and tracing out the ancillary system.

We recall the *hybrid lemma* for reprogramming quantumly-accessible classical oracles.

<span id="page-23-1"></span>**Theorem 6** (Hybrid Lemma [BBBV97]). Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be a quantum algorithm making queries to an oracle  $\mathcal{O}$ . Let  $|\psi_t\rangle = \sum_{w,x,y,t} \alpha_{w,x,y,t} | w,x,y \rangle$  denote the joint state of the working register, the query input register and the query output register of the algorithm right before execution of the t-th query. For a subset S of the domain of  $\mathcal{O}$ , let  $q_S(|\psi_t\rangle) = \sum_{x \in S} |\alpha_{w,x,y,t}|^2$  and  $q_S = \sum_t q_s(|\psi_t\rangle)$ , and call  $q_S$  the query weight of S. Let  $\mathcal{O}'$  be another oracle whose output differs from  $\mathcal{O}$  only on points  $x \in S$ . Then, if  $\mathcal{A}$  makes T queries to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}$  and S is a subset such that  $q_S \leq \epsilon^2/T$ , we have  $||\psi\rangle\langle\psi| - |\psi'\rangle\langle\psi'||_1 \leq 2\epsilon$  where  $|\psi\rangle$ ,  $|\psi'\rangle$  denote the final state of the algorithm  $\mathcal{A}$  when given access to the oracles  $\mathcal{O}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}'$  respectively. In the case where  $\mathcal{O}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}'$ , S are distributional (along with some auxiliary information register  $R_{\mathsf{aux}}$ ) and possibly correlated, we have  $(|\psi\rangle\langle\psi|, \mathcal{O}, \mathcal{O}', S, R_{\mathsf{aux}}) \approx_{\epsilon} (|\psi'\rangle\langle\psi'|, \mathcal{O}, \mathcal{O}', S, R_{\mathsf{aux}})$  or equivalently  $(|\psi\rangle\langle\psi|, \mathcal{O}, \mathcal{O}', S, R_{\mathsf{aux}}) \approx_{\sqrt{q_S \cdot T}} (|\psi'\rangle\langle\psi'|, \mathcal{O}, \mathcal{O}', S, R_{\mathsf{aux}})$ .

We recall the following lemma about compressed oracle simulation technique for random oracles. We will use this technique in Section 7, thus, we refer the reader to [Zha19] for details of this technique. As a reminder of the notation, we have CStO = StdDecompoCStO'oStdDecompoIncrease.

<span id="page-23-2"></span>**Theorem 7** (Compressed Oracle Lemma [Zha19]). Consider a quantum algorithm  $\mathcal{A}$  making queries to a random oracle  $H: \{0,1\}^m \to \{0,1\}^n$  and outputting a tuple  $(x_1,\ldots,x_k,y_1,\ldots,y_k,z)$ . Let R be a collection of such tuples. Suppose with probability p,  $\mathcal{A}$  outputs a tuple such that (1) the tuple is in R and (2)  $H(x_i) = y_i$  for all i. Now consider running the compressed oracle simulation of  $\mathcal{A}$ , suppose the database D is measured after  $\mathcal{A}$  produces its output. Let p' be the probability that (1) the tuple is in R, and (2)  $D(x_i) = y_i$  for all i (and in particular  $D(x_i) \neq \bot$ ). Then  $\sqrt{p} \leq \sqrt{p'} + \sqrt{\frac{k}{2^n}}$ .

{24}------------------------------------------------

We recall the small-range distributions lemma.

<span id="page-24-0"></span>**Theorem 8** (Small Range Distributions [Zha12]). There is a universal constant  $C_{SRD} > 1$  such that, for any sets  $\mathcal{X}$  and  $\mathcal{Y}$ , distribution  $\mathcal{D}$  on  $\mathcal{Y}$ , any integer  $\ell$ , and any quantum algorithm  $\mathcal{A}$  that makes k queries, we have

$$\left| \Pr_{\mathcal{O} \leftarrow \mathfrak{O}_1} [\mathcal{A}^{\mathcal{O}}() = 1] - \Pr_{\mathcal{O} \leftarrow \mathfrak{O}_2} [\mathcal{A}^{\mathcal{O}}() = 1] \right| \le C_{\mathsf{SRD}} \frac{k^3}{\ell}$$

where the distributions  $\mathfrak{O}_1, \mathfrak{O}_2$  are defined as follows.

- For  $\mathfrak{O}_1$ , independently sample  $y_x \leftarrow \mathcal{D}$  for each  $x \in \mathcal{X}$  and set  $\mathcal{O}(x) = y_x$ .
- For  $\mathfrak{O}_2$ , sample a random function  $P: \mathcal{X} \to [\ell]$ , independently sample  $y_x \leftarrow \mathcal{D}$  for each  $x \in [\ell]$  and set  $\mathcal{O}(x) = y_{P(x)}$ .

{25}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-25-0"></span>Part I

# Definitions

# <span id="page-25-1"></span>4 Quantum Protection Definitions

In this section, we recall the definitions of various quantum protection ([\[C¸ G24,](#page-93-8) [C¸ G25\]](#page-93-1)) security notions, which is the question of encoding a key/functionality into a quantum state to obtain a classically-impossible security guarantee (such as copy-protection or unbounded leakage-resilience).

### <span id="page-25-2"></span>4.1 Quantum Protection

<span id="page-25-4"></span>We recall the notions of classically unlearnable functionalities and quantum protection schemes.

Definition 6 (Classically Unlearnable Functionalities [\[C¸ G24,](#page-93-8) [C¸ G25\]](#page-93-1)). A functionality F is a tuple (F, SampFunc, SampChal, Pred) whose elements are defined as follows.

- F: A sequence consisting of sets (for each λ ∈ N <sup>+</sup>) of classical circuits of polynomial size.
- SampFunc(1<sup>λ</sup> ) : An interactive efficient (quantum) algorithm that outputs a value f ∈ F at the end of the interaction.
- SampChal(f): An efficient (quantum) algorithm that takes as input a value f ∈ F and outputs a challenge input x and an answer key ak.
- Pred(f, ak, x, y): An efficient (quantum) algorithm that takes as input a value f ∈ F, an answer key ak, an input x and a value y, and outputs 1 or 0, denoting if y is a valid answer for input x with respect to f and ak or not.

Consider the following between a challenger and an adversary A.

#### LEARNING − GAMEA(1<sup>λ</sup> )

- 1. The challenger and the adversary interact where the challenger simply simulates SampFunc. Let f <sup>∗</sup> denote the output of SampFunc at the end of the interaction.
- 2. For any polynomial number of rounds: The adversary A submits the classical description of a oracular quantum circuit C with classical output, the challenger executes C with oracle access to f <sup>∗</sup> and submits the outcome to the adversary.
- 3. The challenger samples a challenge input x ∗ , ak<sup>∗</sup> ← SampChal(f ∗ ) and submits x ∗ to the adversary A.
- 4. A outputs y ∗ .
- 5. The challenger outputs 1 if and only if Pred(f ∗ , ak<sup>∗</sup> , x<sup>∗</sup> , y<sup>∗</sup> ) outputs 1.

A functionality F is said to satisfy ptriv-classical-unlearnability if for any QPT adversary A,

$$\Pr\left[\mathsf{LEARNING} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1\right] \leq p_{triv}(\lambda) + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

<span id="page-25-3"></span>Note that for any non-trivial game (i.e. ptriv is not close to 1), the size of the challenge x <sup>∗</sup> must be superlogarithmic.

{26}------------------------------------------------

Definition 7 (Quantum Protection Scheme [\[C¸ G24,](#page-93-8) [C¸ G25\]](#page-93-1)). Let F = (F, SampFunc, SampChal, Pred) be a functionality. A quantum protection scheme QuantumProtection for F consists of the following efficient algorithms.

- QuantumProtection.Protect(1<sup>λ</sup> , f): On input a circuit f ∈ F, outputs a quantum register Rkey.
- QuantumProtection.Eval(Rkey, x): On input a key register and a circuit input x, outputs an evaluation.

We require evaluation correctness: For each f ∈ F and input x to f,

$$\Pr \bigg[ y = f(x) : \begin{array}{c} \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QuantumProtection.Protect}(1^{\lambda}, f) \\ y \leftarrow \mathsf{QuantumProtection.Eval}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}, x) \end{array} \bigg] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

# <span id="page-26-0"></span>4.2 LOCC Leakage-Resilience

<span id="page-26-1"></span>We recall LOCC leakage-resilience security for general functionalities.

Definition 8 (LOCC Leakage-Resilience Security [\[C¸ GLZR24,](#page-94-1) [C¸ G24,](#page-93-8) [C¸ G25\]](#page-93-1)). Let F = (F, SampFunc, SampChal, Pred) be a functionality that is ptriv-classical-unlearnable and let QuantumProtection be a quantum protection scheme for F. Consider the following game between the challenger and an adversary A.

#### LEAK − GAMEA(1<sup>λ</sup> )

- 1. The challenger and the adversary A interact where the challenger simply simulates SampFunc. Let f <sup>∗</sup> denote the output of SampFunc at the end of the interaction.
- 2. The challenger samples R<sup>0</sup> ← QuantumProtection.Protect(1<sup>λ</sup> , f <sup>∗</sup> ).
- 3. Leakage Phase: Then, for any number[13](#page-26-2) of rounds, the following is executed (starting with i = 1).
  - 1. A specifies a quantum leakage circuit E<sup>i</sup> that takes as input a quantum register and outputs a classical string and the updated quantum register.
  - 2. The challenger executes L<sup>i</sup> , R<sup>i</sup> ← Ei(Ri−1) and submits the classical string L<sup>i</sup> to A. Then i is incremented.
- 4. The challenger samples a challenge input x <sup>∗</sup> ← SampChal(f ∗ ) and submits x ∗ to the adversary A.
- 5. A outputs y ∗ .
- 6. The challenger outputs 1 if and only if Pred(f ∗ , ak<sup>∗</sup> , x<sup>∗</sup> , y<sup>∗</sup> ) outputs 1.

A quantum protection scheme QuantumProtection is said to satisfy LOCC leakage-resilience for the functionality F if for any QPT adversary A,

$$\Pr\left[\mathsf{LEAK} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1\right] \leq p_{triv}(\lambda) + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

<span id="page-26-2"></span><sup>13</sup>Note that when A is QPT, implicitly this will be any polynomial number of rounds.

{27}------------------------------------------------

Note that previous works also define unbounded (i.e. 1-round) leakage-resilience. In this work, since we achieve the strongest notion, LOCC leakage-resilience, we will not define unbounded leakage-resilience.

In Section A, for ease of exposition, we also explicitly write out the special case of this definition for digital signatures and public-key encryption explicitly, since these are the two simplest and most natural use cases.

### <span id="page-27-0"></span>4.3 One-Shot Signatures

<span id="page-27-1"></span>We recall one-shot signatures.

**Definition 9** (One-Shot Signatures [AGKZ20]). A one-shot signature scheme OSS consists of the following efficient algorithms.

- OSS.Setup $(1^{\lambda})$ : Takes in a security parameter, outputs a common reference string crs.
- OSS.GenQKey(crs): Takes in the CRS value crs, outputs a verification key vk and a quantum signing key  $R_{kev}$ .
- OSS.Sign $(crs, vk, R_{key}, m)$ : Takes in the CRS value, a verification key, a signing key  $R_{key}$ , and a message m; outputs a classical signature sig.
- OSS.Ver(crs, vk, m, sig): Takes in the CRS value crs, a verification key vk, a message m and a signature sig; outputs 0 or 1.

Correctness: For any message  $m \in \mathcal{M}$ ,

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{aligned} crs &\leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Setup}(1^\lambda) \\ out_{\mathsf{Ver}} &= 1: \end{aligned} \begin{array}{c} vk, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}(crs) \\ sig &\leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}(crs, vk, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}, m) \\ out_{\mathsf{Ver}} &\leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Ver}(crs, vk, m, sig) \end{aligned} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

One-Shot Security: For any QPT adversary A,

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{array}{ccc} m_1 \neq m_2 & crs \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS.Setup}(1^\lambda) \\ \wedge & vk, sig_1, m_1, sig_2, m_2 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}(crs) \\ out_{1,\mathsf{Ver}} = 1 & out_{1,\mathsf{Ver}} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS.Ver}(crs, vk, m_1, sig_1) \\ \wedge & out_{2,\mathsf{Ver}} = 1 \end{array} \right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

In Section 6, we introduce a new security notion called incompressibility for one-shot signature in the classical oracle model. Thus, we also define OSS in the oracle model below 14.

<span id="page-27-2"></span>**Definition 10** (One-Shot Signatures in the Classical Oracle Model). A one-shot signature scheme OSS in the classical oracle model consists of the following efficient algorithms.

• OSS.GenOracles( $1^{\lambda}$ ): Takes in a security parameter, outputs a classical oracle  $\mathcal{O}$ .

<span id="page-27-3"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>14</sup>This is slightly different from the standard oracle model where there is a single global oracle (rather than an oracle being output for each instance of the scheme) that all the algorithms and adversaries query. We use this model for simplicity, and they are equivalent to each other.

{28}------------------------------------------------

- OSS.GenQKey<sup>(·)</sup>(1<sup> $\lambda$ </sup>): An oracle algorithm that takes in a security parameter, outputs a verification key vk and a quantum signing key R<sub>key</sub>.
- OSS.Sign<sup>(·)</sup> $(vk, R_{key}, m)$ : An oracle algorithm that takes in a verification key, a signing key  $R_{key}$ , and a message m; outputs a classical signature sig.
- OSS.Ver $^{(\cdot)}(vk, m, sig)$ : An oracle algorithm that takes in a verification key vk, a message m and a signature sig; outputs 0 or 1.

Correctness: For any message  $m \in \mathcal{M}$ ,

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{matrix} \mathcal{O} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenOracles}(1^\lambda) \\ \mathit{out}_\mathsf{Ver} = 1 : \begin{matrix} \mathit{vk}, \mathsf{R}_\mathsf{key} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}^\mathcal{O}.\mathsf{GenQKey}(1^\lambda) \\ \mathit{sig} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}^\mathcal{O}(\mathit{vk}, \mathsf{R}_\mathsf{key}, m) \\ \mathit{out}_\mathsf{Ver} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Ver}^\mathcal{O}(\mathit{vk}, m, \mathit{sig}) \end{matrix} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

One-Shot Security: For any query-bounded adversary A,

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{array}{ccc} m_1 \neq m_2 & \mathcal{O} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenOracles}(1^\lambda) \\ \wedge & vk, sig_1, m_1, sig_2, m_2 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathcal{O}}(1^\lambda) \\ out_{1,\mathsf{Ver}} = 1 & : \begin{array}{c} vk, sig_1, m_1, sig_2, m_2 \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathcal{O}}(1^\lambda) \\ out_{1,\mathsf{Ver}} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}^{\mathcal{O}}.\mathsf{Ver}(vk, m_1, sig_1) \\ \wedge & out_{2,\mathsf{Ver}} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}^{\mathcal{O}}.\mathsf{Ver}(vk, m_2, sig_2) \end{array} \right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

We define strong one-shot security similarly, with the difference that it is only required to have  $sig_1 \neq sig_2$  (and not necessarily  $m_1 \neq m_2$ ).

{29}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-29-0"></span>5 Definitional Work on Quantum Fire

In this section, we recall some existing definitions related to quantum fire, and also introduce definitions for new primitives and security notions.

### <span id="page-29-1"></span>5.1 Quantum Fire

We first recall quantum fire ([BNZ25]). Throughout the paper, we will only consider public-key quantum fire even when we ignore writing out public-key explicitly.

<span id="page-29-2"></span>**Definition 11** (Quantum Fire). A (public-key) quantum fire scheme QFire consists of the following efficient algorithms.

- QFire.Setup( $1^{\lambda}$ ): Takes in a security parameter, outputs a public key pk and a secret key sk.
- QFire.Spark(sk): Takes in the secret key, outputs a serial number sn, and a flame state in the register R<sub>flame</sub>.
- QFire.Clone(pk, sn, R<sub>flame</sub>): Takes in the public key, a serial number, a flame state register R<sub>flame</sub>, outputs a new flame register R<sub>clone</sub> (along with the input register R<sub>flame</sub>).
- QFire.Ver(pk, sn, R): Takes in the public key, a serial number, and an alleged flame state, outputs 0 or 1.

We require the following correctness guarantees.

### Verification Correctness:

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{matrix} pk, sk \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Setup}(1^\lambda) \\ out_{\mathsf{Ver}} = 1: & sn, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Spark}(sk) \\ out_{\mathsf{Ver}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Ver}(pk, sn, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}}) \end{matrix} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Cloning Correctness: For any polynomial  $p(\cdot)$ ,

$$\Pr\left[ \begin{aligned} pk, sk \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda}) \\ sn, \mathsf{R}_1 \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Spark}(sk) \\ For \ i = 2, \dots, p(\lambda) \ \mathsf{R}_i \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Clone}(pk, sn, \mathsf{R}_{i-1}) \\ For \ i = 1, \dots, p(\lambda) \ out_{i,\mathsf{Ver}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Ver}(pk, sn, \mathsf{R}_i) \end{aligned} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

We introduce a stronger correctness condition called *strong cloning correctness*.

**Definition 12** (Strong Cloning Correctness). A quantum fire scheme QFire is said to satisfy strong cloning correctness if the following are satisfied: There exists a collection of pure states  $|\psi_{sk,sn}\rangle$  such that with probability 1 the output of QFire.Spark(sk) is  $sn, |\psi_{sk,sn}\rangle$  for some sn. Let  $M_{sk,sn}$  denote the binary outcome projective measurement onto  $|\psi_{sk,sn}\rangle$ .

$$\Pr \left[ \begin{array}{c} pk, sk \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Setup}(1^{\lambda}) \\ sn, \mathsf{R}_{flame} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Spark}(sk) \\ b_1 = b_2 = 1: \ \mathsf{R}_{clone} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFire}.\mathsf{Clone}(pk, sn, \mathsf{R}_{flame}) \\ b_1 \leftarrow M_{sk,sn}(\mathsf{R}_{flame}) \\ b_2 \leftarrow M_{sk,sn}(\mathsf{R}_{clone}) \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

{30}------------------------------------------------

Note that in oracle-based constructions, the flame states also depend on the oracle itself[15](#page-30-2) in addition to sk, sn.

We now recall untelegraphability security for quantum fire. We slightly extend the definition of [\[BNZ25\]](#page-93-4) to consider collusion-resistant quantum fire, where the adversary gets multiple independent flame states.

<span id="page-30-1"></span>Definition 13 (Untelegraphability Security). Consider the following game between an adversary A = (A1, A2) and a challenger.

#### TELEGRAPH − GAMEA(1<sup>λ</sup> )

- 1. The challenger samples pk, sk ← QFire.Setup(1<sup>λ</sup> ) and submits pk to A<sup>1</sup> and A2.
- 2. For polynomially many number of rounds: The adversary sends an empty query, and the challenger samples sn, Rflame ← QFire.Spark(sk) and submits sn, Rflame to the adversary A1.
- 3. The adversary A<sup>2</sup> outputs a message T.
- 4. The adversary A<sup>1</sup> receives T and outputs a classical string L.
- 5. The adversary A<sup>2</sup> receives L, outputs sn<sup>∗</sup> , R ′ .
- 6. The challenger outputs 1 if b = 1 where b ← QFire.Ver(pk, sn<sup>∗</sup> , R ′ ) = 1, and otherwise it outputs 0.

We say that the quantum fire scheme QFire satisfies untelegraphability security if for any for any polynomial-time (or query-bounded, for unconditional oracle-based schemes) adversary A, we have

$$\Pr \Big[ \mathsf{TELEGRAPH} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1 \Big] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Note that the weaker notion of non-adaptive untelegraphability security can also be defined, where A<sup>1</sup> produces its output without receiving a message from A2.

Finally, we introduce the notion of mini-scheme for quantum fire, analogous to the notion of mini-scheme for quantum money. This definition makes proofs easier, and it is easy to see that any mini-scheme for quantum fire can generically be upgraded to a full scheme using digital signatures [\(Definition 4\)](#page-22-2), simply by signing the serial number (signature is made part of the new serial number) and verifying the signature on the serial number as part of verification - just like in the case of upgrading quantum money mini-schemes to full schemes ([\[AC12\]](#page-93-10)).

<span id="page-30-0"></span>Definition 14 (Quantum Fire Mini-Scheme). A public-key quantum fire mini-scheme QFireMini consists of the following efficient algorithms.

- QFireMini.Spark(1<sup>λ</sup> ): Takes in the security parameter, outputs a serial number sn, and a flame state Rflame.
- QFireMini.Clone(sn, Rflame): Takes in a serial number, a flame register, outputs a new flame register Rclone (along with the input register Rflame).
- QFireMini.Ver(sn, R): Takes in a serial number, and an alleged flame state, outputs 0 or 1.

<span id="page-30-2"></span><sup>15</sup>Equivalently, we can consider the whole oracle as part of the secret key for purposes of this definition.

{31}------------------------------------------------

### **Verification Correctness:**

$$\Pr\bigg[out_{\mathsf{Ver}} = 1: \begin{array}{c} sn, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFireMini.Spark}(1^{\lambda}) \\ out_{\mathsf{Ver}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFireMini.Ver}(sn, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}}) \end{array}\bigg] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Strong Cloning Correctness: We require that there exists a collection of pure states  $|\psi_k\rangle$  such that with probability 1 the output of QFireMini.Spark $(1^{\lambda})$  is  $sn, |\psi_k\rangle$  for some k, sn and

$$\Pr \left[ b_1 = b_2 = 1 : \begin{array}{c} sn, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFireMini.Spark}(1^{\lambda}) \\ \mathsf{R}_{clone} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFireMini.Clone}(sn, \mathsf{R}_{flame}) \\ b_1 \leftarrow M_k(\mathsf{R}_{flame}) \\ b_2 \leftarrow M_k(\mathsf{R}_{clone}) \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

where  $M_k$  denotes the binary outcome projective measurement onto  $|\psi_k\rangle$ .

Note that in oracle-based constructions, the flame states also depend on the oracle itself  $^{16}$  in addition to k.

<span id="page-31-1"></span>**Definition 15** (Untelegraphability Security for Quantum Fire Mini-Scheme). Consider the following game between an adversary  $A = (A_1, A_2)$  and a challenger.

# $\mathsf{MINI} - \mathsf{TELEGRAPH} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda})$

- 1. The challenger samples sn,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFireMini.Spark}(1^{\lambda})$  and  $submits\ sn$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}}$  to the adversary  $\mathcal{A}_1$ .
- 2. The adversary  $A_2$  receives sn and outputs a message T.
- 3. The adversary  $A_1$  receives T and outputs a classical string L.
- 4. The adversary  $A_2$  receives L, outputs R'.
- 5. The challenger executes QFireMini.Ver(sn, R') outputs if it outputs 1, otherwise it outputs 0.

We say that the quantum fire scheme QFireMini satisfies untelegraphability security if for any QPT (or query bounded, in case of unconditional oracle-based schemes) adversary A, we have

$$\Pr\Big[\mathsf{MINI} - \mathsf{TELEGRAPH} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1\Big] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

### <span id="page-31-0"></span>5.2 Interactive Untelegraphability Security

We introduce the notion of interactive telegraphing security, inspired by the notion of LOCC leakage-resilience (Definition 8) defined by [ÇGLZR24]. For simplicity, we will explicitly define it only for mini-schemes, but the collusion-resistant case is defined similarly to Definition 13 (where  $A_1$  receives multiple independent flame states).

<span id="page-31-2"></span>**Definition 16** (Interactive Untelegraphability Security). Consider the following game between an adversary  $A = (A_1, A_2)$  and a challenger.

<span id="page-31-3"></span>Equivalently, we can consider the whole oracle as part of the key k for purposes of this definition.

{32}------------------------------------------------

# $\mathsf{MINI} - \mathsf{INTERACTIVE} - \mathsf{TELEGRAPH} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda})$

- 1. The challenger samples sn,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QFireMini.Spark}(1^{\lambda})$  and  $submits\ sn$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}}$  to the adversary  $\mathcal{A}_1$ .
- 2. The adversaries  $A_1$  and  $A_2$  interact classically by exchanging classical messages for any number of rounds<sup>17</sup>.
- 3. The adversary  $A_2$  receives L, outputs R'.
- 4. The challenger executes QFireMini.Ver(sn, R') outputs if it outputs 1, otherwise it outputs 0.

We say that the quantum fire scheme QFireMini satisfies interactive untelegraphability security if for any QPT (or query bounded, in case of unconditional oracle-based schemes) adversary A, we have

$$\Pr\Big[\mathsf{MINI} - \mathsf{INTERACTIVE} - \mathsf{TELEGRAPH} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1\Big] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

### <span id="page-32-0"></span>5.3 Quantum Key-Fire

We now introduce a new notion called *quantum key-fire*. Quantum key-fire is the functional version of quantum fire, where the flame state can be used to evaluate a functionality, and we require *unbounded/LOCC leakage-resilience* ([ÇGLZR24]) as our security notion, which is a generalization of the notion of untelegraphability. Quantum key-fire is to quantum fire what copy-protection ([ALL+21, CLLZ21]) is to public-key quantum money. Just like the case of copy-protection and quantum money, it is easy to see that quantum key-fire implies quantum fire.

A quantum key-fire scheme is an *quantum protection scheme* (Definition 7) with unbounded/LOCC leakage-resilience, with the addition of a cloning algorithm. We write the full definition for reference.

**Definition 17** (Quantum Key-Fire). A public-key quantum key-fire scheme for a functionality  $\mathcal{F}$  (Definition 6) consists of the following efficient algorithms.

- QKeyFire.Protect $(1^{\lambda}, f)$ : Takes in a function  $f \in F$  and outputs a flame state  $R_{\text{key}}$ .
- QKeyFire.Clone( $R_{key}$ ): Takes in a flame register  $R_{key}$ , outputs a new register  $R_{clone}$  (along with the input register  $R_{key}$ ).
- QKeyFire.Eval( $R_{key}$ , x): Takes in a flame register  $R_{key}$ , and an input x, outputs a value.

Evaluation Correctness: For all  $f \in F$ , for all x,

$$\Pr \bigg[ y = f(x) : \begin{array}{c} \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFire}.\mathsf{Protect}(1^{\lambda}, f) \\ y \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFire}.\mathsf{Eval}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}, x) \end{array} \bigg] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

**Strong Cloning Correctness:** We require that there exists a collection of pure states  $|\psi_{k,f}\rangle$  such that for all  $f \in F$ , with probability 1 the output of QKeyFire.Protect $(1^{\lambda}, f)$  is  $|\psi_{k,f}\rangle$  for some k and

$$\Pr \left[ b_1 = b_2 = 1 : \begin{array}{c} k, sn, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFire.Protect}(1^\lambda, f) \\ \mathsf{R}_{clone} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFire.Clone}(\mathsf{R}_{flame}) \\ b_1 \leftarrow M_{k,f}(\mathsf{R}_{flame}) \\ b_2 \leftarrow M_{k,f}(\mathsf{R}_{clone}) \end{array} \right] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

<span id="page-32-1"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>17</sup>Note that when  $A_1, A_2$  are QPT, implicitly this will be any *polynomial* number of rounds.

{33}------------------------------------------------

where Mk,f denotes the binary outcome projective measurement onto |ψk,f ⟩.

Note that in oracle-based constructions, the flame states also depend on the oracle itself[18](#page-33-3) in addition to f, k.

Security: When QKeyFire is a key-fire scheme for some (classically-unlearnable) functionality F [\(Definition 6\)](#page-25-4), we will require that QKeyFire satisfies LOCC leakage-resilience [\(Definition 8\)](#page-26-1) for F.

### <span id="page-33-0"></span>5.3.1 Quantum Key-Fire for Signing

In this section, we provide the explicit definition of the special case of quantum-key fire for signing, since this the main functionality we consider in this work.

<span id="page-33-1"></span>Definition 18 (Quantum Key-Fire for Signing). A public-key quantum key-fire scheme for signing QKeyFireSign consists of the following efficient algorithms.

- QKeyFireSign.Setup(1<sup>λ</sup> ): Takes in a security parameter, outputs a verification key (also called serial number) vk, and a key state Rflame.
- QKeyFireSign.Clone(vk, Rkey): Takes in a key register Rkey, outputs a new register Rclone along with the input register Rkey.
- QKeyFireSign.Sign(vk, Rkey, m) : Takes in a key register and a message m, outputs a signature.
- QKeyFireSign.Ver(vk, m, sig): Takes in a verification key (also called serial number), a message and an alleged signature, outputs 1 or 0.

Evaluation Correctness: For all m ∈ M,

$$\Pr\bigg[\mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Ver}(vk,m,sig) = 1: \begin{array}{c} vk, \mathsf{R_{key}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda}) \\ sig \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Sign}(vk,\mathsf{R_{key}},m) \end{array}\bigg] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Strong cloning correctness: This is defined the same as before: We require that output of QKeyFireSign.Setup(1<sup>λ</sup> ) is a pure state |ψk⟩ and that clone on input |ψk⟩ outputs two copies, |ψk⟩ ⊗ |ψk⟩.

<span id="page-33-2"></span>Definition 19 (LOCC Leakage-Resilience Security for Quantum Key-Fire for Signing). Consider the following game between an adversary A and a challenger.

#### LR − SIGN − GAMEA(1<sup>λ</sup> )

- 1. The challenger samples vk, Rkey ← QKeyFireSign.Setup(1<sup>λ</sup> ) and submits vk to A.
- 2. Set R<sup>0</sup> = Rkey.
- 3. Leakage Phase: For any number[19](#page-33-4) of rounds, the following is executed (starting with i = 1).
  - 1. A specifies a quantum leakage circuit E<sup>i</sup> that takes as input a quantum register and outputs a classical string and the updated quantum register.

<span id="page-33-3"></span><sup>18</sup>Equivalently, we can consider the whole oracle as part of the key k for purposes of this definition.

<span id="page-33-4"></span><sup>19</sup>Note that when A is QPT, implicitly this will be any polynomial number of rounds.

{34}------------------------------------------------

- 2. The challenger executes L<sup>i</sup> , R<sup>i</sup> ← Ei(Ri−1) and submits the classical string L<sup>i</sup> to A. Then i is incremented.
- 4. The challenger samples a random message m<sup>∗</sup> ← M.
- 5. The adversary A receives m<sup>∗</sup> , outputs sig<sup>∗</sup> .
- 6. The challenger checks if QKeyFireSign.Ver(sn, m<sup>∗</sup> , sig<sup>∗</sup> ) = 1. If so, it outputs 1, otherwise it outputs 0.

We say that the quantum key-fire scheme QKeyFireSign satisfies LOCC leakage-resilience security if for any QPT (or query bounded, in case of unconditional oracle-based schemes) adversary A, we have

$$\Pr \Big[ \mathsf{LR} - \mathsf{SIGN} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1 \Big] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

{35}------------------------------------------------

## <span id="page-35-0"></span>Part II

# Technical Tools

# <span id="page-35-1"></span>6 One-Shot Signatures with Incompressibility Security

In this section, we introduce a new notion called *incompressibility* security for one-shot signatures in the classical oracle model, and then construct a scheme that satisfies it. The section is organized as follows. First we introduce our definition of incompressibility and give our theorem statement about existence of an incompressible OSS scheme. Then in Section 6.1, we introduce a technical tool called *operational incompressibility* that simplifies the proof of our incompressibility notion. Then we give our construction in Section 6.2 and prove its incompressibility property in Section 6.4. In Section 6.3, we show some technical results related to subspace oracles that will be used in our proof in Section 6.4 and might be of independent interest.

For our incompressibility notion, we consider a one-shot signature scheme OSS with *split oracles*.

<span id="page-35-4"></span>**Definition 20** (One-Shot Signature Scheme with Split Oracles). Let OSS be a one-shot signature scheme with classical oracles ( $Definition\ 10$ ). Write  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS}$  to denote its oracle. OSS is said to have split oracles if  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS}$  is a tuple of (correlated) oracles ( $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.GenQKey}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}$ ) =  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS}$ , where each algorithm of OSS uses only the corresponding oracle (e.g. OSS.GenQKey only uses  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.GenQKey}$ ). We also assume that the inputs to  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}$  and  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}$  are of the form vk, vk where vk denotes a verification key.

Note that any one-shot signature scheme can trivially be converted into a scheme with split oracles by setting all three oracles to be the full oracle, but this will not satisfy incompressibility. Now we define incompressibility.

<span id="page-35-2"></span>**Definition 21** (Incompressibility). OSS is said to satisfy incompressibility security for  $\mathcal{O} \in \{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}\}$  if the following is satisfied. There exists some c > 0 such that for any query-bounded adversary  $\mathcal{A}_1$  with unbounded length classical output, there exists a mapping  $\mathcal{M}$  (which outputs a list<sup>20</sup>  $\mathfrak{L}$  with at most  $s(\lambda)$  elements where  $s(\lambda) = (q(\lambda))^c$  and  $q(\lambda)$  is the number of  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.GenQKey}}$  queries made by  $\mathcal{A}_1$ ) such that for all query-bounded  $\mathcal{A}_2$ , we have

$$\mathbb{E}\left[\sum_{\substack{vk,x:\\\mathcal{O}(vk,x)\neq 0\\vk\not\in\mathcal{M}(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}},L,\mathcal{A}_2)}}\mathsf{QW}_{\mathcal{A}_2,L,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Ver}}}^{(vk,x)}: \begin{array}{c}\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}\leftarrow\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenOracles}(1^\lambda)\\L\leftarrow\mathcal{A}_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}}(1^\lambda)\end{array}\right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

where  $\mathsf{QW}_{\mathcal{A}_2,L,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}}^{(vk,x)}$  denotes the total query weight of  $\mathcal{A}_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}}(L)$  to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}$  on oracle input vk,x, and  $\mathcal{A}_1,\mathcal{A}_2$  are allowed to share an unbounded length classical randomness in advance (i.e. before oracles are sampled).

If incompressibility is satisfied for both  $\mathcal{O} \in \{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}, \mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}\}$ , then we will simply say that OSS satisfies incompressibility.

We define strong incompressibility similarly, where we require the list  $\mathcal{M}$  to output pairs (vk, z) and the summation above is taken over  $(vk, z) \notin \mathcal{M}(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}, L, \mathcal{A}_2)$ . It is easy to see that strong

<span id="page-35-3"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>20</sup>We will refer to this list as the incompressibility list.

{36}------------------------------------------------

incompressibility for  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}$  follows from incompressibility for  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}$  and strong one-shot security.

We claim that a one-shot signature scheme with incompressibility security exists.

<span id="page-36-2"></span>**Theorem 9.** Relative to a classical oracle, there exists a one-shot signature scheme for 1-bit messages that satisfies one-shot security and incompressibility security.

We give our construction in Section 6.2 and prove its incompressibility in Section 6.4.

### <span id="page-36-0"></span>6.1 Operational Incompressibility

As a technical tool for proving incompressibility, we define the notion of operational incompressibility.

<span id="page-36-1"></span>**Definition 22** (Operational Incompressibility). OSS is said to satisfy operational incompressibility security for  $\mathcal{O} \in \{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}, \mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}\}$  if the following is satisfied. There exists some c > 0 such that for any query-bounded adversary  $\mathcal{A}_1$  with unbounded-length classical output, for all query-bounded  $\mathcal{A}_2$ , we have

$$\Pr\left[\begin{array}{ccc} \forall i \in [s(\lambda)+1] \ \mathcal{O}(vk_i,x_i) \neq 0 & \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenOracles}(1^\lambda) \\ & \wedge & : & L \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}}(1^\lambda) \\ & (vk_i)_{i \in [s(\lambda)+1]} \ distinct & (vk_i,x_i)_{i \in [s(\lambda)+1]} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Ver}}}(L) \end{array}\right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

where  $s(\lambda) = (q(\lambda))^c$  and  $q(\lambda)$  is the number of  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.GenQKey}$  queries made by the adversary  $\mathcal{A}_1$  and  $\mathcal{A}_1, \mathcal{A}_2$  are allowed to share an unbounded length classical randomness in advance (i.e. before oracles are sampled).

<span id="page-36-3"></span>**Theorem 10.** If an OSS scheme satisfies operational incompressibility, then it also satisfies incompressibility.

Now we prove this theorem. Let OSS be a scheme that satisfies operational incompressibility. Fix  $\mathcal{O} \in \{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}\}$ . For any vk, define

$$q_{vk} = \sum_{x: \mathcal{O}(vk, x) \neq 0} \mathsf{QW}^{vk, x}_{\mathcal{A}_2, L, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}}$$

The dependence on  $A_2, L, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}$  are implicit.

Let  $vk_1, \ldots, vk_s, vk_{s+1}$  be the inputs such that

- $q_{vk_i} \ge q_{vk_{i+1}}$  for  $i \in [s]$
- $q_{vk_{s+1}} \ge q_{vk'}$  for any  $vk' \notin \{vk_i\}_{i \in [s+1]}$

That is,  $vk_i$  are the inputs with the highest valid query weights. Note that these all implicitly depend on  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}, L, \mathcal{A}_2$ .

We set  $\mathcal{M}(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}, L, \mathcal{A}_2)$  to be  $\{vk_1, \ldots, vk_s\}$ . Now suppose for a contradiction that incompressibility property is not satisfied, that is, there exists some  $\mathcal{A}_1, \mathcal{A}_2$  and polynomial  $t(\cdot)$  such that for infinitely many  $\lambda > 0$ ,

$$p_{out} = \mathbb{E}\left[\sum_{\substack{vk:\\vk \notin \mathcal{M}(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}, L, \mathcal{A}_2)}} q_{vk}: \begin{array}{c} \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}} \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenOracles}(1^\lambda)\\ L \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}}(1^\lambda) \end{array}\right] \geq \frac{1}{t(\lambda)}.$$

Let  $u(\lambda)$  denote the number of queries to  $\mathcal{O}$  by  $\mathcal{A}_2$ . Consider the following adversary  $\mathcal{A}'_2$  for the operational incompressibility game.

{37}------------------------------------------------

 $\underline{\mathcal{A}_2'}$ 

- 1. Set  $D = \emptyset$ .
- 2. For  $n(\lambda) = u(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot s(\lambda) \cdot \lambda^2 \cdot (s(\lambda) + 1)$  times (in s + 1 groups):
  - 1. Simulate  $A_2(L)$ , but measure a random query to  $\mathcal{O}$  to obtain vk, x.
  - 2. If  $\mathcal{O}(vk,x) \neq 0$  and  $vk \notin D^{21}$ , add (vk,x) to D and skip to the next group.
- 3. Output D.

We will show that we can violate operational incompressibility using  $\mathcal{A}'_2$ . We continue our proof by considering two cases/events. Define  $E_1$  to be the event that  $q_{vk_{s+1}} \geq \frac{1}{t(\lambda) \cdot s(\lambda) \cdot \lambda}$ , and  $E_2$  to be its complement. Thus we have either  $\Pr[E_1] \geq \frac{1}{4 \cdot t \cdot u - 2}$  or  $\Pr[E_2] \geq 1 - \frac{1}{4 \cdot t \cdot u - 2}$ .

Now we consider the case  $\Pr[E_1] \geq \frac{1}{4 \cdot t \cdot u - 2}$ . We claim that  $\mathcal{A}_1, \mathcal{A}'_2$  wins the operational incompressibility game with probability at least  $\frac{1}{8 \cdot t \cdot u - 4}$ . We condition on the event  $E_1$ , and we will show that the adversaries will win with probability  $\geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Observe that for each  $vk_i$  with  $i \in [s+1]$ , we have that the probability of  $vk_i \in D$  is  $1 - \exp\{-\frac{n}{u \cdot t \cdot s \cdot \lambda}\} \geq 1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$  since the weight of each  $vk_i$  is at least  $\frac{1}{t \cdot s \cdot \lambda}$ . Thus, by the union bound, we get that  $vk_1, \ldots, vk_{s+1} \in D$  with overwhelming probability, which indeed violates incompressibility security.

Now we consider the case  $\Pr[E_2] \geq 1 - \frac{1}{4 \cdot t \cdot u - 2}$ . Let GOOD be the event that

$$\sum_{vk:vk\notin\mathcal{M}(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}},L,\mathcal{A}_2)}q_{vk}\geq \frac{1}{2\cdot t}$$

Since expectation of this value  $(p_{out})$  is greater than  $\frac{1}{t(\lambda)}$  and since  $\Pr[E_2] \geq 1 - \frac{1}{4 \cdot t \cdot u - 2}$ , we get  $\Pr[E_2 \wedge \mathsf{GOOD}] \geq \frac{1}{4 \cdot t \cdot u - 2}$  by an application of Markov's inequality and union bound.

We claim that  $\mathcal{A}_1, \mathcal{A}'_2$  wins the operational incompressibility game with overwhelming probability conditioned on  $E_2 \wedge \mathsf{GOOD}$ , which happens with non-negligible probability. Let G denote the complement set of  $\mathcal{M}(\mathcal{A}_2, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}}, L)$ . Let  $vk_1^*, \ldots, vk_{s+1}^*$  be the values added to the database D during each group during execution of  $\mathcal{A}'_2$ , in the order of addition. In particular, if no item was added during a group, we set  $vk_i^* = \bot$ . We now claim that with overwhelming probability,  $vk_1^*, \ldots, vk_{s+1}^* \neq \bot$ . Note that once we establish this, we will have shown that we can violate operational incompressibility with non-negligible probability. Now to prove our claim, first observe that  $vk_1^* \in G$  with overwhelming probability since  $q_G := \sum_{vk \in G} q_{vk} \ge \frac{1}{2t}$  (since we conditioned on  $\mathsf{GOOD}$ ). Then, we claim that  $vk_2^* \neq \bot$  with overwhelming probability. To see this, observe that  $q_G \ge \frac{1}{2t}$  and for any possible value of  $vk_1^* \in G$ , we have  $q_{vk_1^*} \le \frac{1}{t \cdot s \cdot \lambda}$  (since we conditioned on  $E_2$ ) and thus  $q_G - q_{vk_1^*} \ge \frac{1}{2t}$ . Continuing like this, we can show that each  $vk_i^*$  is  $\in G$  with overwhelming probability, no matter what the previous values  $vk_1^*, \ldots, vk_{i-1}^*$  are. This completes case 2.

Observe that we showed violations of the operational incompressibility game in both cases. This completes the proof.

### <span id="page-37-0"></span>6.2 Construction and Proofs of Security

In this section, we prove Theorem 9: We show that there exists a one-shot signature scheme that satisfies incompressibility (Definition 21) relative to a classical oracle. Our construction will be a delicately modified version of the construction of [SZ25].

<span id="page-37-1"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>21</sup>Here we mean that there is no x such that  $(vk, x) \in D$ 

{38}------------------------------------------------

Now we move onto our construction.

Define the following parameters: Let q(λ) = 16λ, r(λ) = q(λ)·(λ−1), n(λ) = r(λ)+ <sup>3</sup> 2 q(λ), k(λ) = n(λ).

#### OSS.GenOracles(1<sup>λ</sup> )

- 1. Sample a random permutation π on {0, 1} n . Let H(x), J(x) denote the first r and last n − r bits of π(x).
- 2. For each y ∈ {0, 1} r , sample a random full column-rank matrix A<sup>y</sup> ∈ F k×(n−r) 2 and a random vector b<sup>y</sup> in F k 2 .
- 3. Set P(x) = (y, A<sup>y</sup> · J(x) + by) where y = H(x).
- 4. Set P −1 (y, v) = π −1 (y||z) if v = A<sup>y</sup> · z + b<sup>y</sup> for some z ∈ F n−r 2 , otherwise ⊥.
- 5. Set D(y, v) = 1 if v <sup>T</sup> A<sup>y</sup> = 0 and v ̸= 0, otherwise 0.
- 6. Set D0(y, m, v) = 1 if v = A<sup>y</sup> · z + b<sup>y</sup> for some z ∈ F n−r 2 and the first bit of v is m; otherwise 0.
- 7. The oracles: Set OVer = D0, OSign = D, OGenQKey = (P,P −1 , D, D0). Set the oracle OOSS to be (OVer, OSign, OGenQKey).

#### OSS.GenQKeyOGenQKey (1<sup>λ</sup> )

- 1. Parse OGenQKey = (P,P −1 , D, D0).
- 2. Prepare the states |0 n ⟩, |0 r ⟩, 0 k over the registers R1, R2, R3.
- 3. Apply H⊗<sup>n</sup> to R1.
- 4. Execute the oracle P with input register R<sup>1</sup> and output register (R2, R3).
- 5. Execute the oracle P <sup>−</sup><sup>1</sup> with input register (R2, R3) and output register R1.
- 6. Measure the register R2, let y be the measurement outcome.
- 7. Output y, R3.

# OSS.VerOVer(vk, sig, m)

- 1. Parse OVer = D0.
- 2. Output D0(vk, m, sig) = 1.

Our signing algorithm is the same as the signing algorithm of [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3) (which in turn is the same as the signing mechanism of [\[AGKZ20,](#page-93-9) [Shm22\]](#page-95-11)). For completeness, we recall it here.

{39}------------------------------------------------

# $\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Sign}}}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},m)$

- 1. Parse  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Sign}} = \mathcal{D}$ .
- 2. Parse  $(vk, \mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{key}}) = \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}$
- 3. For  $j = 1, \ldots, \lambda$ :
  - 1. Measure the first qubit of  $R'_{key}$ . In case the outcome is m, measure the rest of  $R'_{key}$  to obtain sig', and output m||sig'| and terminate.
  - 2. Apply  $H^{\otimes k}$  to  $\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{key}}$ , then apply the following mapping coherently (writing the outcome to a new output register) to  $\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{key}}$  and measure the output bit:  $(vk,z) \to 1$  if  $\mathcal{D}(vk,z) = 1$  or if  $z = 0^k$ , otherwise  $(vk,z) \to 0$ . Then, apply  $H^{\otimes k}$  again to  $\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{key}}$ . Proceed to the next iteration  $j \leftarrow j+1$ .
- 4. If all  $\lambda$  iterations failed, output  $\perp$ .

### Theorem 11. OSS satisfies correctness.

*Proof.* While the correctness of the scheme follows from previous work ([SZ25], which in turn uses the correctness proof of [AGKZ20, Shm22]), for ease of reference, we recall it below. Fix any  $m \in \{0,1\}$  for the rest of the proof.

First, we assume that for all but (at most)  $2 \cdot 2^{2r(\lambda)-n(\lambda)}$  many values of y, we have that  $A_y$  has at least a single column whose first entry is 1. Since the probability of this happening for any individual y value is  $1 - (1/2)^{n-r}$ , by a simple Chernoff bound it is easy to see that our assumption holds with probability at least  $1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$ .

It is easy to see that GenQKey outputs y,  $\sum_{u \in \mathsf{ColSpan}(A_y)} |v + b_y\rangle$  for a uniformly random y, thus we start with this state in the register  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}$ . We assume that  $A_y$  has at least a single column whose first entry is 1. Note that we had already assumed that this is already true for all but (at most)  $2 \cdot 2^{2r(\lambda)-n(\lambda)}$  many verification keys, and since y is chosen uniformly at random from  $2^r$  verification keys, our assumption holds with probability at least  $1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$ .

Note that by definition signatures for m correspond to vectors in  $\mathsf{ColSpan}(A_y) + b_y$  that start with the bit m. Since there is at least one column whose first entry is 1, it is easy to see that there is an equal number of vectors that start with either bit in  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y) + b_y$ . Thus, the probability of signing in the first iteration of the algorithm is accordingly 1/2. The algorithm makes  $\lambda$  tries and we would like to argue it succeeds with probability  $1-2^{\lambda}$ . We will prove that each try indeed succeeds with at least probability 1/2 (so far it is clear only for the first iteration), which will complete the proof.

Now let  $S := \mathsf{ColSpan}(A_y)$  and let  $S_0$  the set of vectors in S that start with 0, which is a subspace of S with one less dimension. Observe that after the failed first try, the state we have in  $\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{key}}$  is the state  $\sum_{u \in S_0} |b_y + x + u\rangle$ , for some value  $x \in S$  which will not matter for our proof (for the interested reader, x will be the zero vector if  $b_y$  starts with the bit  $\overline{m}$ , and otherwise it will be a vector that completes  $S_0$  to S). Now we claim that that if we have a state of the form  $\sum_{u \in S_0} (-1)^{\langle z, u \rangle} |b_y + x + u\rangle$ , for any  $z \in S_0^{\perp}$ , after performing the correction part of the signing algorithm, we obtain a state of the form  $\sum_{u \in S} (-1)^{\langle z', u \rangle} |b_y + x + u\rangle$  for some  $z' \in S_0^{\perp}$ . To see this, note that after executing  $H^{\otimes k}$  the state we get is  $\sum_{v \in S_0^{\perp}} (-1)^{\langle b_y + x, v \rangle} |z + v\rangle$ , and since  $S_0$  is a subspace of S with one less dimension, the subspace  $S^{\perp} := \mathsf{ColSpan}(A_y)^{\perp}$  is a subspace of  $S_0^{\perp}$  with one less dimension. Thus, when we measure the output qubit of  $\mathcal{D}$  (note that we are not using the output of  $\mathcal{D}$  and effectively discarding its answer) the state collapses to a state of the form

{40}------------------------------------------------

 $\sum_{v \in S^{\perp}} (-1)^{\langle b_y + x, v \rangle} |z' + v\rangle$  for some value  $z' \in S_0^{\perp}$ . When we execute the second Hadamard, we get a state of the form  $\sum_{u \in S} (-1)^{\langle z', u \rangle} |b_y + x + u\rangle$ , which is equal to  $\sum_{u \in S} (-1)^{\langle z', u \rangle} |b_y + u\rangle$  since  $x \in S$ . Thus, in summary, as long as we start an iteration with a state of this form, we end the iteration with a state of this form (even the signing attempt fails). With this, it is easy to see that each iteration succeeds with probability 1/2 independently. This finishes the proof.

### **Theorem 12.** OSS satisfies strong one-shot security.

*Proof.* Observe that the oracle  $\mathcal{D}_0$  in our construction can be implemented using  $\mathcal{P}^{-1}$ . Since strong one-shot security relative to  $\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}, \mathcal{D}$  has already been proven by [SZ25], the security of our scheme follows.

<span id="page-40-1"></span>**Theorem 13.** OSS satisfies incompressibility.

We prove this theorem in Section 6.4.

### <span id="page-40-0"></span>6.3 Properties of Subspace Oracles

In this section, we recall some results about subspace oracles and also prove some new technical results. Throughout the section, we will write  $\mathcal{O}_{S'}$  to denote the oracle that checks membership in S' (outputs 1 if and only if the input is inside S') where S' is a subspace.

First we recall the subspace-hiding oracles.

<span id="page-40-2"></span>**Lemma 2** (Subspace-Hiding Oracles [SZ25]). Let  $k, r, s \in \mathbb{N}$  be such that  $r + s \leq k$  and let S be a subspace of  $\mathbb{F}_2^k$  of dimension r. Let  $\mathcal{U}$  be the uniform distribution over superspaces T of S of dimension r + s.

Then, for any adversary A making at most q quantum queries, we have the following.

$$\{\mathcal{A}^{\mathcal{O}_S}()\} \approx_{O\left(\frac{q \cdot s}{\sqrt{2^{k-r-s}}}\right)} \{\mathcal{A}^{\mathcal{O}_T}() : T \leftarrow \mathcal{U}\} .$$

Now we prove the following theorem, which significantly improves upon a similar result of [SZ25].

<span id="page-40-3"></span>**Theorem 14.** Let  $d_2 \leq d_1 \leq n$ . Let S be a subspace of dimension  $d_1$  of  $\mathbb{F}_2^n$ , and let  $\mathcal{U}$  denote the uniform distribution of subspaces of S of dimension  $d_2$ . Then, for any adversary  $\mathcal{A}$  making at most q quantum queries, we have

$$\Pr\left[v \in T \setminus \{0\}: \begin{array}{c} T \leftarrow \mathcal{U} \\ v \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathcal{O}_{T^{\perp}}} \end{array}\right] \leq \frac{2^{d_1 - d_2} - 1}{2^{d_1} - 1} + q \cdot \sqrt{\frac{2^{d_1 - d_2} - 1}{2^{d_1} - 1}}$$

Proof. Let  $p_{\mathcal{A}} = \Pr\left[v \in T \setminus \{0\}: \frac{T \leftarrow \mathcal{U}}{v \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{\mathcal{O}_{T^{\perp}}}}\right]$ . We observe that for any adversary  $\mathcal{B}$  that is not given query access to  $\mathcal{O}_{T^{\perp}}$  (call such an adversary an oblivious adversary), the probability of outputting a vector  $v \in T^{\perp} \setminus S^{\perp}$  is  $p = \frac{2^{d_1 - d_2 - 1}}{2^{d_1 - 1}}$ . Thus, by Theorem 6, if we modify the first oracle call of  $\mathcal{A}$  to instead use  $\mathcal{O}_{S^{\perp}}$ , the probability of winning decreases by at most  $\sqrt{p}$ , since the part of the adversary before its first call to  $\mathcal{O}_{T^{\perp}}$  can be considered an oblivious adversary. Further, once we modify the first oracle call of the adversary to  $\mathcal{O}_{S^{\perp}}$ , now the part until the second oracle call is also an oblivious adversary. Continuing this argument for all q oracle calls, we can conclude that when  $\mathcal{A}$  is run with the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{S^{\perp}}$ , its probability of winning is at least  $p_{\mathcal{A}} - q \cdot \sqrt{p}$ . However, by the same oblivious algorithm argument as above, we have  $p_{\mathcal{A}} - q \cdot \sqrt{p} \leq p$ . Thus,  $p_{\mathcal{A}} \leq q \cdot \sqrt{p} + p$ .

{41}------------------------------------------------

### <span id="page-41-0"></span>6.4 Proof of Incompressibility

In this section, we prove Theorem 13. In the proof, instead of setting  $s(\lambda) = (q(\lambda))^c$  for some c > 0, we actually set  $s(\lambda) = 2q(\lambda)$ , which is even stronger.

Now, we move onto our proof. We will explicitly prove only the case of  $\mathcal{O} = \mathcal{O}_{\text{OSS.Ner}}$ , and the case of  $\mathcal{O} = \mathcal{O}_{\text{OSS.Sign}}$  follows essentially the same way (note the symmetry between  $A_y$  and  $A_y^{\perp}$  in our proof).

Suppose for a contradiction that incompressibility is not satisfied: There exists query-bounded  $\mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2$  and a polynomial  $p(\cdot)$  such that  $p_{win} \geq \frac{1}{p(\lambda)}$ , where we define

$$p_{win} = \Pr \left[ \begin{array}{ccc} \forall i \in [s(\lambda)+1] \ \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Ver}}(vk_i, m_i, sig_i) \neq 0 & (\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.GenQKey}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}) \leftarrow \mathsf{OSS.GenOracles}(1^{\lambda}) \\ & \land & : & L \leftarrow \mathcal{P}_1^{(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.GenQKey}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}})}(1^{\lambda}) \\ & & (vk_i)_{i \in [s(\lambda)+1]} \ \mathsf{distinct} & & (vk_i, m_i, sig_i)_{i \in [s(\lambda)+1]} \leftarrow \mathcal{P}_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}}(L) \end{array} \right]$$

where  $s(\lambda) = 2q(\lambda)$  and  $q(\lambda)$  is the number of queries to  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.GenQKey}$  made by  $\mathcal{P}_1$ .

Now define a sequence of hybrids for some adversaries  $A_1, A_2$ .

 $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$ : We define this hybrid as follows.

### $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$

- 1. Sample a random permutation  $\pi$  on  $\{0,1\}^n$ .
- 2. For each  $y \in \{0,1\}^r$ , sample a random full column-rank matrix  $A_y \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-r)}$  and a random vector  $b_y$  in  $\mathbb{F}_2^k$ .
- 3. Set  $\mathcal{P}(x) = (y, A_y \cdot J(x) + b_y)$  where y = H(x).
- 4. Set  $\mathcal{P}^{-1}(y,v) = \pi^{-1}(y||z)$  if  $v = A_y \cdot z + b_y$  for some  $z \in \mathbb{F}_2^{n-r}$ , otherwise  $\perp$ .
- 5. Set  $\mathcal{D}(y, v) = 1$  if  $v^T A_y = 0$  and  $v \neq 0$ , otherwise 0.
- 6. Set  $\mathcal{D}_0(y, m, v) = 1$  if  $v = A_y \cdot z + b_y$  for some  $z \in \mathbb{F}_2^{n-r}$  and the first bit of v is m; otherwise 0.
- 7. Set  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Ver}} = \mathcal{D}_0$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Sign}} = \mathcal{D}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{GenQKey}} = (\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}, \mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0)$ .
- 8. Sample  $L \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_1^{(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Ver}})}(1^{\lambda}).$
- 9. Sample  $(vk_i, m_i, v_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)+1]} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}}(L, (b_y)_{y \in \{0,1\}^r}).$
- 10. Check that  $vk_i$  are all distinct, and that  $v_i + b_{vk_i}$  starts with the bit  $m_i$  and that  $v_i \in \mathsf{Colspan}(A_{vk_i}) \setminus \{0\}$  for all  $i \in [q+1]$ . If so, output 1, otherwise output 0.

We set  $A_1$  to  $\mathcal{P}_1$  and  $A_2$  to be the following adversary. It first runs  $A_1$  to obtain  $(vk_i, m_i, sig_i)_{i \in [s(\lambda)+1]}$ , then it checks if there are at least q+1 values of  $i \in [s(\lambda)+1]$  such that  $sig_i \neq b_{vk_i}$ . If so, let  $I \subset [s(\lambda)+1]$  (with |I|=q+1) denote those values and  $A_2$  outputs  $(vk_i, m_i, sig_i - b_{vk_i})_{i \in I}$ . Otherwise, it outputs  $\bot$ .

Then, we claim that we have  $\Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_0 = 1] \ge \frac{1}{2p}$ . To see this, first define the event  $E_1$  to be the event in the definition of  $p_{win}$ . Define  $E_2$  to be the event that for at least q+1 values of  $i \in [s+1]$ , we have  $sig_i \ne b_{vk_i}$  (where the same sampling procedure is the same as in the definition

{42}------------------------------------------------

of  $p_{win}$ ). Now, observe that we have  $\Pr[E_1 \wedge E_2] + \Pr[E_1 \wedge \overline{E_2}] = p_{win} \geq \frac{1}{p}$ . Now we claim that  $\Pr[E_1 \wedge \overline{E_2}] \leq \operatorname{negl}(\lambda)$ . Observe that once we prove this,  $\Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_0 = 1] \geq \frac{1}{2p}$  follows easily for  $\mathcal{A}_1, \mathcal{A}_2$  we chose above.

Now we prove  $\Pr[E_1 \wedge \overline{E_2}] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Observe that once  $E_1 \wedge \overline{E_2}$  occurs, it means that we have recovered the value  $b_{vk}$  as part of the output  $\mathcal{P}_2$  for at least q+1 different vk values. Also note that each query to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}$  made by  $\mathcal{P}_2$  can be simulated by making  $2^{n-r}$  queries to an oracle that verifies equality for  $b_y$  values (i.e. the oracle that outputs 1 on  $b_y$ , y and 0 otherwise). Thus,  $\mathcal{P}_1$  makes q queries to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}(y) = b_y$  and  $\mathcal{P}_2$  makes  $\mathsf{poly}(\lambda) \cdot 2^{n-r}$  queries to the verification/equality check oracle for  $b_y$  values. Thus, by Theorem 15 and by the values of the parameters n, r, k, we get that (except with negligibly small probability)  $\mathcal{P}_2$  cannot output  $b_{vk}$  values for q+1 different vk values. Hence,  $\Pr[E_1 \wedge \overline{E_2}] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  as desired.

Hyb<sub>1</sub>: Let  $t(\lambda)$  denote the total number of queries in the experiment. Set  $\ell(\lambda) = 1024 \cdot C_{\mathsf{SRD}} \cdot p(\lambda) \cdot (t(\lambda))^3$  where  $C_{\mathsf{SRD}}$  is the constant from Theorem 8.

## $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$

- 1. Sample a random permutation  $\pi$  on  $\{0,1\}^n$ .
- 2. For each  $y \in \{0,1\}^r$ , sample a random full column-rank matrix  $A_y \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-r)}$  and a random vector  $b_y$  in  $\mathbb{F}_2^k$ .
- 3. Sample a random function  $SRD: \{0,1\}^r \to [\ell]$ .
- 4. Set  $\mathcal{P}(x) = (y, \mathbf{A}_{SRD(y)} \cdot J(x) + b_y)$  where y = H(x).
- 5. Set  $\mathcal{P}^{-1}(y,v) = \pi^{-1}(y||z)$  if  $v = A_{SRD(y)} \cdot z + b_y$  for some  $z \in \mathbb{F}_2^{n-r}$ , otherwise  $\perp$ .
- 6. Set  $\mathcal{D}(y,v)=1$  if  $v^T A_{SRD(y)}=0$  and  $v\neq 0$ , otherwise 0.
- 7. Set  $\mathcal{D}_0(y, m, v) = 1$  if  $v = A_{SRD(y)} \cdot z + b_y$  for some  $z \in \mathbb{F}_2^{n-r}$  and the first bit of v is m; otherwise 0.
- 8. Set  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Ver}} = \mathcal{D}_0$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Sign}} = \mathcal{D}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{GenQKey}} = (\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}, \mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0)$ .
- 9. Sample  $L \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_1^{(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Ver}})}(1^{\lambda}).$
- 10. Sample  $(vk_i, m_i, v_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)+1]} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_2^{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}, \mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}}(L, (b_y)_{y \in \{0,1\}^r}).$
- 11. Check that  $vk_i$  are all distinct, and that  $v_i + b_{vk_i}$  starts with the bit  $m_i$  and that  $v_i \in \mathsf{Colspan}(A_{SRD(vk_i)}) \setminus \{0\}$  for all  $i \in [q+1]$ . If so, output 1, otherwise output 0.

We have  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0 \approx_{1/16p} \mathsf{Hyb}_1$  by Theorem 8, since the whole experiment can be implemented with oracle access to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_A(y) = A_y$  (where each  $\mathcal{O}_A(y)$  is sampled independently from the full-column-rank matrix distribution as above)

Hyb<sub>2</sub>: We define this hybrid as follows.

{43}------------------------------------------------

### $\mathsf{Hyb}_2$

- 1. Sample a random permutation  $\pi$  on  $\{0,1\}^n$ .
- 2. For each  $y \in \{0,1\}^r$ , sample a random full column-rank matrix  $A_y \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-r)}$  and a random vector  $b_y$  in  $\mathbb{F}_2^k$ .
- 3. For each  $y \in \{0,1\}^r$ , sample  $A_y' \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-\frac{r}{2})}$  and  $A_y'' \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-\frac{r}{2})}$  so that  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y')$  is a random superspace of  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y)$  of dimension  $n-\frac{r}{2}$  and  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y'')^{\perp}$  is a random superspace of  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y)^{\perp}$  of dimension  $\frac{3r}{2}$ .
- 4. Sample a random function  $SRD: \{0,1\}^r \to [\ell]$ .
- 5. Set  $\mathcal{P}(x) = (y, A_{SRD(y)} \cdot J(x) + b_y)$  where y = H(x).
- 6. Set  $\mathcal{P}^{-1}(y,v) = \pi^{-1}(y||z)$  if  $v = A_{SRD(y)} \cdot z + b_y$  for some  $z \in \mathbb{F}_2^{n-r}$ , otherwise  $\perp$ .
- 7. Set  $\mathcal{D}(y, v) = 1$  if  $v^T A_{SRD(y)}^{"} = 0$  and  $v \neq 0$ , otherwise 0.
- 8. Set  $\mathcal{D}_0(y, m, v) = 1$  if  $v = A'_{SRD(y)} \cdot z + b_y$  for some  $z \in \mathbb{F}_2^{n-r}$  and the first bit of v is m; otherwise 0.
- 9. Set  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Ver}} = \mathcal{D}_0$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Sign}} = \mathcal{D}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{GenQKey}} = (\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}, \mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0)$ .
- 10. Sample  $L \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_1^{(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Ver}})}(1^{\lambda}).$
- 11. Sample  $(vk_i, m_i, v_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)+1]} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_2^{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}, \mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}}(L, (b_y)_{y \in \{0,1\}^r}).$
- 12. Check that  $vk_i$  are all distinct, and that  $v_i + b_{vk_i}$  starts with the bit  $m_i$  and that  $v_i \in \mathsf{Colspan}(A_{SRD(vk_i)}) \setminus \mathsf{Colspan}(A_{SRD(vk_i)}')$  for all  $i \in [q+1]$ . If so, output 1, otherwise output 0.

We have  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1 \approx \mathsf{Hyb}_2$  by the following argument. First, note that the changes to the oracles  $\mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0$  make negligible difference by Lemma 2 (since we only deal with  $\ell$ , which is polynomial, many subspaces). Also note that Lemma 2 allows the adversary to choose the base subspace, thus, the oracles  $\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}$  and so on do not preclude us from invoking the theorem. After we modify the oracles, the change to the winning condition also makes negligible difference by Theorem 14.

Hyb<sub>3</sub>: We define this hybrid as follows.

### $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$

- 1. Sample a random permutation  $\pi$  on  $\{0,1\}^n$ .
- 2. For each  $y \in \{0,1\}^r$ , sample a random full column-rank matrix  $A_y \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-r)}$  and a random vector  $b_y$  in  $\mathbb{F}_2^k$ .
- 3. For each  $y \in \{0,1\}^r$ , sample  $A_y' \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-\frac{r}{2})}$  and  $A_y'' \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-\frac{r}{2})}$  so that  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y')$  is a random superspace of  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y)$  of dimension  $n-\frac{r}{2}$  and  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y'')^{\perp}$  is a random

{44}------------------------------------------------

superspace of  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y)^{\perp}$  of dimension  $\frac{3r}{2}$  (or, equivalently,  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y'')$  is a random subspace of  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y)$  of dimension  $n-\frac{3r}{2}$ .)

- 4. Set  $\mathcal{P}(x) = (y, \mathbf{A}_y \cdot J(x) + b_y)$  where y = H(x).
- 5. Set  $\mathcal{P}^{-1}(y,v) = \pi^{-1}(y||z)$  if  $v = A_y \cdot z + b_y$  for some  $z \in \mathbb{F}_2^{n-r}$ , otherwise  $\perp$ .
- 6. Set  $\mathcal{D}(y,v) = 1$  if  $v^T A_y'' = 0$  and  $v \neq 0$ , otherwise 0.
- 7. Set  $\mathcal{D}_0(y, m, v) = 1$  if  $v = A'_y \cdot z + b_y$  for some  $z \in \mathbb{F}_2^{n-r}$  and the first bit of v is m; otherwise 0.
- 8. Set  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Ver}} = \mathcal{D}_0$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Sign}} = \mathcal{D}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{GenQKey}} = (\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}, \mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0)$ .
- 9. Sample  $L \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_1^{(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}},\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Ver}})}(1^{\lambda}).$
- 10. Sample  $(vk_i, m_i, v_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)+1]} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_2^{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}, \mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}}(L, (b_y)_{y \in \{0,1\}^r}).$
- 11. Check that  $vk_i$  are all distinct, and that  $v_i + b_{vk_i}$  starts with the bit  $m_i$  and that  $v_i \in \mathsf{Colspan}(A_{vk_i}) \setminus \mathsf{Colspan}(A_{vk_i}'')$  for all  $i \in [q+1]$ . If so, output 1, otherwise output 0.

We have  $\mathsf{Hyb}_2 \approx_{1/16p} \mathsf{Hyb}_3$  by Theorem 8, since the whole experiment can be implemented with oracle access to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_A(y) = A_y''|A_y||A_y'|$  (where each  $\mathcal{O}_A(y)$  is sampled independently as in the experiment).

Hyb<sub>final</sub>: We now define our final hybrid, for some adversaries  $\mathcal{A}'_1, \mathcal{A}'_2$ .

## $\mathsf{Hyb}_{final}$

- 1. Sample a random permutation  $\pi$  on  $\{0,1\}^n$ .
- 2. For each  $y \in \{0,1\}^r$ , sample a random vector  $b_y$  in  $\mathbb{F}_2^k$ .
- 3. For each  $y \in \{0,1\}^r$ , sample  $A'_y \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-\frac{r}{2})}$  and  $A''_y \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-\frac{r}{2})}$  so that  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A'_y)$  is a random subspace of  $\mathbb{F}_2^k$  of dimension  $n-\frac{r}{2}$  and so that  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A''_y)$  is a random subspace of  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A'_y)$  of dimension  $n-\frac{3r}{2}$ .
- 4. For each  $y \in \{0,1\}^r$ , sample  $A_y \in \mathbb{F}_2^{k \times (n-r)}$  so that  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y)$  is a random subspace from the set  $\mathcal{S}$  of subspaces of dimension n-r where each subspace in the set is a superspace of  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y'')$  and subspace of  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y'')$ .
- 5. Define the oracle  $\mathcal{O}(y)$  that outputs the index of  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_y)$  in the set  $\mathcal{S}$  when it is ordered in a canonical way. That is, each  $\mathcal{O}(y)$  is independently and uniformly sampled from  $[|\mathcal{S}|]$  (we will refer to the elements of  $[|\mathcal{S}|]$  and the subspaces  $A_y$  in an interchangeable way).
- 6. Sample  $L \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_1^{\mathcal{O}}(1^{\lambda}, \pi, (b_y, A'_y, A''_y)_{y \in \{0,1\}^r})$ .
- 7. Sample  $(vk_i, m_i, v_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)+1]} \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_2(L, \pi, (b_y, A'_y, A''_y)_{y \in \{0,1\}^r}).$

{45}------------------------------------------------

8. Winning Condition Check: Check that  $vk_i$  are all distinct, and that  $v_i + b_{vk_i}$  starts with the bit  $m_i$  and that  $v_i \in \mathsf{Colspan}(A_{vk_i}) \setminus \mathsf{Colspan}(A_{vk_i}'')$  for all  $i \in [q+1]$ . If so, output 1, otherwise output 0.

Since  $\Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_3 = 1] \ge \frac{1}{2p}$ , it is easy to see that there exists  $\mathcal{A}_1'$ ,  $\mathcal{A}_2'$  such that  $\mathcal{A}_1'$  makes q queries to  $\mathcal{O}$  and  $\Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_{final} = 1] \geq \frac{1}{2p}$ . Now we will show that this is a contradiction. Moving forward, without loss of generality, we will assume that  $A_2$  never outputs (i)  $v_i \notin \mathsf{Colspan}(A'_{vk_i}) \setminus \mathsf{Colspan}(A''_{vk_i})$ , (ii) it never outputs non-distinct  $vk_i$  values and (iii) it never outputs  $\perp$  (e.g. at worst, it can output random vectors in  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A'_{vk_i}) \setminus \mathsf{Colspan}(A''_{vk_i})$ ). Now, first, consider the compressed oracle simulation, Exp of the hybrid  $Hyb_{final}$ . In particular, we also execute the final part of the experiment (i.e. winning condition check) using queries to  $\mathcal{O}$ : For  $i \in [q+1]$ , we first query the oracle  $\mathcal{O}$  on  $vk_i$  and write the output to an empty register, and then we perform the membership check for  $v_i$  by reading from this register. We assume that the output (win or lose bit) is also written to a new register (call it the experiment outcome register). Since compressed oracle simulation is a perfect simulation, we have  $\Pr[\mathsf{Exp}=1] = \Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_{final}=1]$ . Now we define the experiment Exp' where we modify the execution of the compressed oracle simulation during the winning condition check as follows. Instead of applying StdDecomp o CStO' o StdDecomp (we assume that Increase has been applied for sufficiently many times in advance), we instead apply  $\mathsf{StdDecomp} \circ \mathsf{CStO}' \circ \mathsf{StdDecomp}'$  where  $\mathsf{StdDecomp}'$  is a linear mapping defined as  $\mathsf{StdDecomp}'$ :  $|vk\rangle\,|v\rangle\,|D\rangle \to |vk\rangle\,|v\rangle\,\sum_{A\in[|S|]:v\not\in\mathsf{Colspan}(A)\setminus\mathsf{Colspan}(A''_{vk})}\frac{1}{\sqrt{a}}\,|D\cup(vk,A)\rangle \text{ for }D,vk \text{ such that }D(vk)=0$  $\perp$  (and defined the same as StdDecomp for other basis elements), where  $a = \begin{bmatrix} r \\ r/2 \end{bmatrix}_2 - \begin{bmatrix} r-1 \\ r/2-1 \end{bmatrix}_2$ . We will call the case of D, vk such that  $D(vk) = \bot$  a good case. Since the original mapping StdDecomp maps  $|vk\rangle\,|v\rangle\,|D\rangle\,\rightarrow\,|vk\rangle\,|v\rangle\,\sum_{A\in[|S|]}\frac{1}{\sqrt{|S|}}\,|D\cup(vk,A)\rangle$  for D such that  $D(vk)=\perp$ , and since  $|S| = \left| \frac{r}{r/2} \right|_2$ , it is easy to see that  $\mathsf{Exp'} \approx \mathsf{Exp}$ . Finally, observe that  $\Pr[\mathsf{Exp'} = 1] = 0$ : For any output  $(vk_i, m_i, v_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)+1]}$  (of  $A_2$ ) and any compressed oracle database D that is in the support of the system when  $A_2$  yields its output, it will be the case that there is at least one value  $i \in [q+1]$  such that  $vk_i \notin D$  since D contains q valid pairs (also recall that when the good case does not apply, the number of valid pairs in the database does not increase). Thus, while applying the winning condition check, there will be a point where the good case of StdDecomp' applies, and after that it is easy to see that verification for that index fails. Thus, any  $(vk_i, m_i, v_i)_{i \in [q(\lambda)+1]}$ and any compressed oracle database D in the support of the system will map to a state where the experiment outcome register will have the state  $|0\rangle$ . Thus,  $\Pr[\mathsf{Exp'}=1]=0$ . However, we had  $\mathsf{Exp}' \approx \mathsf{Exp}$  and  $\Pr[\mathsf{Exp} = 1] = \Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_{final} = 1]$  and  $\Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_{final} = 1] \geq \frac{1}{2p}$ . Thus, this is a contradiction, as desired.

{46}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-46-0"></span>7 Incompressibility of Random Oracles

In this section, we show that random oracles satisfy a natural notion of incompressibility. First we give our theorem statement regarding this property, then we prove a technical lemma that will help us in our proof of the incompressibility theorem, and finally we prove our incompressibility theorem.

<span id="page-46-1"></span>**Theorem 15** (Incompressibility of Random Oracles). Let  $H : \{0,1\}^{g_1(\lambda)} \to \{0,1\}^{g_2(\lambda)}$  be a random oracle and define  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{ImageVer}}$  to be the following oracle (called (image) verification oracle).

 $\frac{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{ImageVer}}(x,y)}{\mathbf{Hardcoded:}} H$ 

1. Check if y = H(x). If so, output 1. Otherwise, output 0.

For a predicate  $P: \{0,1\}^{g_1(\lambda)} \to \{0,1\}$ , define  $\mathcal{O}_P$  as follows.

 $\mathcal{O}(x)$ 

 $\overline{\mathbf{H}}$ ardcoded: H, P

- 1. Check if P(x) = 0. If so, output  $\perp$  and terminate.
- 2. Output H(x).

Define the following experiment  $Exp_H$ .

## $\mathsf{Exp}_H$

- 1. Set i = 1.
- 2. For any polynomial number of rounds (denote this by  $u(\lambda)$ ):
  - 1.  $A_1$  makes polynomial number of queries (denote the number by  $s_i(\lambda)$ ) to H and unbounded number of queries to  $\mathcal{O}_{\bigcup_{j=1}^{i-1}P_j}$  where  $\bigcup_{j=1}^{i-1}P_j$  denotes the union of the predicates  $P_1, \ldots, P_{i-1}$  (i.e.  $\bigcup_{j=1}^{i-1}P_j(x) = 1$  if  $P_j(x) = 1$  for some  $j = 1, \ldots, i-1$ ).
  - 2.  $A_1$  outputs a predicate  $P_i$ .
  - 3. Increase i by one.
- 3. A outputs an unbounded length message L.

For any  $g_1(\lambda)$ ,  $g_2(\lambda)$  such that  $g_2(\lambda)$  is superlogarithmic, for an adversary  $\mathcal{A}_1$  as described above, there exists a mapping  $\mathcal{M}$  (which outputs a list<sup>22</sup>  $\mathfrak{L}$  of size at most  $\sum_{j\in[u(\lambda)]} s_j(\lambda)$ ) such that for all  $\mathcal{A}_2$  that makes at most  $q(\lambda)$  queries to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{ImageVer}}$  such that  $\frac{q(\lambda)}{\sqrt{2^{g_2(\lambda)}}}$  is negligible (but can make any number of queries to  $\mathcal{O}_{P^*}$ ), we have

<span id="page-46-2"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>22</sup>We will refer to this as the incompressibility list.

{47}------------------------------------------------

$$\mathbb{E}\left[\sum_{\substack{x,y:\\ \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{ImageVer}}(x,y)\neq 0\\ x\not\in\mathcal{M}(H,L,(P_j)_j,\mathcal{A}_2)\\ P^*(x)=0}}\mathsf{QW}_{\mathcal{A}_2,L,H,(P_j)_j}^{x,y}: \begin{array}{c} H\leftarrow\{0,1\}^{g_1(\lambda)}\rightarrow\{0,1\}^{g_2(\lambda)}\\ L,(P_j)_{j\in[u(\lambda)]}\leftarrow\mathcal{A}_1^{H(\cdot)}(1^{\lambda}) \end{array}\right] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

where  $P^* = \bigcup_{j \in [u(\lambda)]} P_j$  and  $QW_{\mathcal{A}_2, L, H, (P_j)_j}^{x, y}$  denotes the total query weight of  $\mathcal{A}_2^{\mathcal{O}_{P^*}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{ImageVer}}}(L)$  to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{ImageVer}}$  on oracle input x, y.

We will refer to the queries to  $\mathcal{O}_{P^*}$  (for  $\mathcal{A}_2$ ) and  $\mathcal{O}_{\bigcup_{j=1}^{i-1}P_j}$  (for  $\mathcal{A}_1$ ) as section queries (and to these oracles as section oracles), and queries to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{ImageVer}}$  as verification queries. A normal query will mean a query to H.

Before proving our theorem, we will prove a different technical lemma that will be useful in our proof. This lemma roughly says that, for a compressed random oracle adversary with additional verification oracle access to the random oracle; if at any point, the weight of databases that contain at most i inputs that satisfy a certain predicate is negligible, then this still holds after a verification query.

<span id="page-47-1"></span>**Lemma 3.** Let  $\mathcal{A}$  be an adversary with access to a random oracle  $H: \{0,1\}^{m(\lambda)} \to \{0,1\}^{n(\lambda)}$  and the verification oracle for the random oracle that outputs 1 on input x, y if H(x) = y, and outputs 0 otherwise. Define the registers

- X, Y, the input registers to the verification oracle,
- Q, the 1-qubit phase register for the verification oracle output,
- W, the internal workspace register of the adversary,
- P, the register containing a predicate<sup>23</sup>, chosen by the adversary,
- D compressed oracle database register,
- T, the register used for implementing the verification oracle queries (initialized at the beginning to zeroes and is not accessed by the adversary).

Consider the following simulation of execution of A:

- The random oracle queries are implemented as a standard oracle (i.e. the output XORed into the output register) using a compressed oracle simulation,
- The verification oracle queries are implemented as a phase oracle as follows:
  - 1. Query the random oracle with input and output registers X and the output register T.
  - 2. Apply a controlled phase gate that maps  $|x\rangle |y\rangle |q\rangle |t\rangle$  to  $(-1)^{b \cdot q} |x\rangle |y\rangle |q\rangle |t\rangle$  where b=1 if and only if y=t (and otherwise b=0).
  - 3. Query the random oracle with input and output registers X and the output register T.

Then,

<span id="page-47-0"></span>We will write P to both mean the predicate function, and to mean the set of inputs x such that P(x) = 1. Similarly,  $\overline{P}$  means the complement of the set P

{48}------------------------------------------------

- This is a perfect simulation of execution of A,
- Let  $|\phi\rangle = \sum_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} |x\rangle |y\rangle |q\rangle |w\rangle |P\rangle |D\rangle |0^{n(\lambda)}\rangle$  be the state of the system right before executing one of the verification oracle queries, respectively over the registers X, Y, Q, W, P, D, T. Let  $i \in \mathbb{N}$  and let  $\mathsf{Inp}(D)$  denote the set consisting of all a such that  $(a,b_a) \in D$  for some  $b_a \neq \bot$ . Let let  $|\psi\rangle = \sum_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \beta_{x,y,q,w,P,D} |x\rangle |y\rangle |q\rangle |w\rangle |P\rangle |D\rangle |0^{n(\lambda)}\rangle$  be the state right after executing the verification oracle query on  $|\phi\rangle$ .

Then, 
$$\sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\text{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|>i}} |\beta_{x,y,q,w,P,D}|^2 \le \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\text{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|>i}} |\alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D}|^2 + \frac{6}{\sqrt{2^{n(\lambda)}}}$$
.

Proof. The fact this simulation is a perfect simulation follows easily from the fact that compressed oracle simulation is a perfect simulation for the random oracle ([Zha19]). Now we prove the second part. Let CtPh denote the unitary for the controlled phase described above that is used in the implementation of the verification queries. Let  $U = \text{CStO} \circ \text{CtPh} \circ \text{CStO}$  (where CStO is the compressed oracle query unitary with input register X and output register T). Note that U is an isometry. Thus,  $|\psi\rangle = U\,|\phi\rangle$  (here our notation means applying the isometry U to the state  $|\phi\rangle$ ). We also let  $\pi$  denote<sup>24</sup> the projection onto  $|P\rangle\,|D\rangle$  such that  $|\text{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|>i$ . Thus, we have  $\sum_{x,y,q,w,P,D:} |\beta_{x,y,q,w,P,D}|^2 = ||\pi U\,|\phi\rangle||^2$ .  $||\text{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|>i$ 

We write

$$\begin{split} |\phi\rangle &= \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\mathsf{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|>i}} \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \, |x\rangle \, |y\rangle \, |q\rangle \, |w\rangle \, |P\rangle \, |D\rangle
