\, \left|0^{n(\lambda)}\right\rangle + \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\mathsf{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|\leq i\\ x\in D}} \alpha_{x,y,w,P,D} \, |x\rangle \, |y\rangle \, |q\rangle \, |w\rangle \, |P\rangle \, |D\rangle \, \left|0^{n(\lambda)}\right\rangle + \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\mathsf{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|\leq i\\ x\not\in D\\ P(x)=1}} \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \, |x\rangle \, |y\rangle \, |q\rangle \, |w\rangle \, |P\rangle \, |D\rangle \, \left|0^{n(\lambda)}\right\rangle + \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\mathsf{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|\leq i\\ x\not\in D\\ P(x)=0}} \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \, |x\rangle \, |y\rangle \, |q\rangle \, |w\rangle \, |P\rangle \, |D\rangle \, \left|0^{n(\lambda)}\right\rangle + \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\mathsf{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|\leq i\\ x\not\in D\\ P(x)=0}} \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \, |x\rangle \, |y\rangle \, |q\rangle \, |w\rangle \, |P\rangle \, |D\rangle \, \left|0^{n(\lambda)}\right\rangle + \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\mathsf{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|\leq i\\ x\not\in D\\ P(x)=0}} \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \, |x\rangle \, |y\rangle \, |q\rangle \, |w\rangle \, |P\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |D\rangle \, |$$

Let  $|\phi_1\rangle$ ,  $|\phi_2\rangle$ ,  $|\phi_3\rangle$ ,  $|\phi_4\rangle$  denote each unnormalized state in the summation above in the order they are written. Observe that when executing a verification query on  $|x\rangle|y\rangle|q\rangle|w\rangle|P\rangle|D\rangle$ , only x can be added to the database (if not already in the database), and the other entries in the database do not change. Thus, we get  $\pi U |\phi_2\rangle = 0$ . By the same argument, we get  $\pi U |\phi_3\rangle = 0$ . We also have  $||\pi U |\phi_1\rangle||^2 \le ||\phi_1\rangle||^2 = \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\|\text{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|>i}} |\alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D}|^2$ .

Now we claim  $\|\pi U\|\phi_4\rangle\|^2 \leq \frac{4}{2^n}$  will prove our claim. Observe that once we prove this, the theorem follows. To see this, first observe that  $\sum_{x,y,q,w,P,D:} |\beta_{x,y,q,w,P,D}|^2 = \|\pi U\|\phi\rangle\|^2 \leq \|\pi U\|\phi_1\rangle\|^2 + |\operatorname{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|>i$ 

 $\|\pi U |\phi_4\rangle\|^2 + 2 \cdot \|\pi U |\phi_1\rangle\| \cdot \|\pi U |\phi_4\rangle\| \text{ by triangle inequality and since } \pi U |\phi_2\rangle = \pi U |\phi_3\rangle = 0. \text{ Finally, note that } \|\pi U |\phi_1\rangle\|^2 + \|\pi U |\phi_4\rangle\|^2 + 2 \cdot \|\pi U |\phi_1\rangle\| \cdot \|\pi U |\phi_4\rangle\| = \|\pi U |\phi_1\rangle\|^2 + \|\pi U |\phi_4\rangle\| (\|\pi U |\phi_4\rangle\| + 2\|\pi U |\phi_1\rangle\|) \text{ and } (\|\pi U |\phi_4\rangle\| + 2\|\pi U |\phi_1\rangle\|) \le 3.$ 

Now we move onto proving  $\|\pi U\|\phi_4\rangle\|^2 \leq \frac{4}{2^n}$ . For all valid states (i.e. states where compressed oracle invariants are kept)  $|\tau\rangle$ , we have  $U|\tau\rangle = \mathsf{StdDecomp} \circ \mathsf{CStO'} \circ \mathsf{CPh} \circ \mathsf{CStO'} \circ \mathsf{StdDecomp} \circ (\mathsf{Inc})^2 |\tau\rangle$ . This follows from the fact that unitaries on different registers commute, that Increase can be moved to the beginning, and that  $\mathsf{StdDecomp}$  is an involution. Write  $U_1 = \mathsf{CStO'} \circ \mathsf{StdDecomp} \circ (\mathsf{Inc})^2$  and  $U_3 = \mathsf{StdDecomp} \circ \mathsf{CStO'}$ ; and thus  $U = U_3 \circ \mathsf{CPh} \circ U_1$ .

<span id="page-48-0"></span><sup>&</sup>lt;sup>24</sup>By abuse of notation, we will also write  $\pi$  to denote the measurement  $\pi \otimes I$  where the identity I is over the remaining registers.

{49}------------------------------------------------

After applying  $U_1$  to  $|\phi_4\rangle$ , the state becomes

$$\sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D,z:\\z\in\{0,1\}^{n(\lambda)}\\|\ln p(D)\cap\overline{P}|\leq i\\x\not\in D\\P(x)=0}}\alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D}\frac{1}{\sqrt{2^{n(\lambda)}}}\left|x\right\rangle\left|y\right\rangle\left|q\right\rangle\left|w\right\rangle\left|P\right\rangle\left|D\cup(x,z)\cup(\bot,0^n)\right\rangle\left|z\right\rangle$$

Once we apply the controlled phase based on the verification, the state becomes

$$\sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\operatorname{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|\leq i\\ x\not\in D\\ P(x)=0}} (-1)^q \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \frac{1}{\sqrt{2^{n(\lambda)}}} \left|x\right\rangle \left|y\right\rangle \left|q\right\rangle \left|w\right\rangle \left|P\right\rangle \left|D\cup(x,y)\cup(\bot,0^n)\right\rangle \left|y\right\rangle + \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ x\in D\\ |\operatorname{Inp}(D)\cap \overline{P}|\leq i\\ x\not\in D\\ P(x)=0}} \sum_{z\neq y} \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \frac{1}{\sqrt{2^{n(\lambda)}}} \left|x\right\rangle \left|y\right\rangle \left|q\right\rangle \left|w\right\rangle \left|P\right\rangle \left|D\cup(x,z)\cup(\bot,0^n)\right\rangle \left|z\right\rangle$$

which is equal to

$$\sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ |\operatorname{Inp}(D)\cap\overline{P}|\leq i\\ x\not\in D\\ P(x)=0}} ((-1)^q-1)\alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \frac{1}{\sqrt{2^{n(\lambda)}}} \left|x\right\rangle \left|y\right\rangle \left|q\right\rangle \left|w\right\rangle \left|P\right\rangle \left|D\cup(x,y)\cup(\bot,0^n)\right\rangle \left|y\right\rangle + \sum_{\substack{x,y,q,w,P,D:\\ x\not\in D\\ P(x)=0}} \sum_{x} \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \frac{1}{\sqrt{2^{n(\lambda)}}} \left|x\right\rangle \left|y\right\rangle \left|q\right\rangle \left|w\right\rangle \left|P\right\rangle \left|D\cup(x,z)\cup(\bot,0^n)\right\rangle \left|z\right\rangle$$

Denote the two unnormalized states in the summation as  $|\eta_1\rangle$ ,  $|\eta_2\rangle$  respectively. Since  $\sum_{x,y,q,w,P,D} |\alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D}|^2 = 1$ , we get  $||\eta_1\rangle||^2 \le \frac{4}{2^n}$  and thus  $||\pi \circ U_3||\eta_1\rangle||^2 \le \frac{4}{2^n}$ . Now, we show  $\pi \circ U_3|\eta_2\rangle = 0$ . Observe that once we apply  $U_3$  to  $|\eta_2\rangle$ , we get

$$\sum_{\substack{x,y,w,P,D:\\ |\mathsf{Inp}(D)\cap\overline{P}|\leq i\\ x\not\in D\\ P(x)=0}} \alpha_{x,y,q,w,P,D} \left|x\right\rangle \left|y\right\rangle \left|q\right\rangle \left|w\right\rangle \left|P\right\rangle \left|D\cup\left\{(\bot,0^n),(\bot,0^n)\right\}\right\rangle \left|0^{n(\lambda)}\right\rangle$$

Hence,  $\pi \circ U_3 |\eta_2\rangle = 0$ , which completes the proof.

Now we prove Theorem 15.

*Proof.* We will prove the operational version of the lemma (similar to Definition 22) and the actual incompressibility theorem directly follows (as in Theorem 10).

We will consider the compressed oracle simulation of the operational game, as in Lemma 3. Note that this simulation is purified: The output of  $A_1$  is measured at the very end. Let  $P_1, \ldots, P_{u(\lambda)}$  denote the registers on which the predicates will appear - without loss of generality, we can assume

{50}------------------------------------------------

that these registers exist from the beginning, and are initialized to zeroes (which will be interpreted as a predicate that rejects all inputs).

For any j ∈ N, let π<sup>j</sup> denote the projection onto database states (over the database register D) and predicate states (over the registers P1, . . . , Pu(λ) ) such that |Inp(D) ∩ (∪ u(λ) <sup>j</sup>=1 P<sup>j</sup> )| > j. Let |τ ⟩ be the state right before some query to the verification oracle, or the random oracle, or the section oracle, or right before updating a predicate register; and let |τ ′ ⟩ denote the state right after the execution of the query. We observe the following.

- If the query is a verification query, then ∥π<sup>j</sup> |τ ′ ⟩∥<sup>2</sup> ≤ ∥π<sup>j</sup> |τ ⟩∥<sup>2</sup> + <sup>√</sup> 6 2 g2(λ) . This follows directly from [Lemma 3.](#page-47-1)
- If the query is a section query, then ∥π<sup>j</sup> |τ ′ ⟩∥<sup>2</sup> ≤ ∥π<sup>j</sup> |τ ⟩∥<sup>2</sup> . This follows since when a compressed oracle query is executed on the state |x⟩ |D⟩, only x can be added to the database, no other values.
- If the query is a normal query, then ∥πj+1 |τ ′ ⟩∥<sup>2</sup> ≤ ∥π<sup>j</sup> |τ ⟩∥<sup>2</sup> . This is because a single query can add at most one input to the database, and cannot change the other entries (other than deleting an entry).
- If we are considering a point where a predicate register is being updated, then ∥π<sup>j</sup> |τ ′ ⟩∥<sup>2</sup> ≤ ∥π<sup>j</sup> |τ ⟩∥<sup>2</sup> . This is because we are considering the union of the predicates in the definition of π<sup>j</sup> , and adding more predicates makes the good set (Inp(D) ∩ (∪P<sup>j</sup> )) smaller.

Applying this to each query of the adversaries A1, A2, it is easy to see that πu(λ) |η⟩ ≤ negl(λ) where |η⟩ is the state of the system right before A<sup>2</sup> produces its output in the operational incompressibility game, since there is a total of u(λ) normal queries. By [Theorem 7,](#page-23-2) this means that except with negligibly small probability, A<sup>2</sup> can output at most u(λ) different valid input output pairs such that the input satisfies P ∗ (x) = 0, which completes the proof of operational incompressibility.

{51}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-51-0"></span>Part III

# Quantum-Key Fire

# <span id="page-51-1"></span>8 Quantum Key-Fire for Signing in the Classical Oracle Model

In this section, we define quantum key-fire for signing in the classical oracle model.

For simplicity, we work with an oracle model where the oracle is sampled by QKeyFireSign.Setup (i.e. there is an independent oracle for each instance) and output as the serial number. However, we note that, through elementary tricks, constructions in this model can also be easily converted to the standard classical oracle model where there is a single global classical oracle  $\mathcal{O}$  (that is sampled from some distribution) that everyone (adversaries and the construction) has quantum-query access to, and QKeyFireSign.Setup  $^{\mathcal{O}}$  simply outputs a classical string as the verification key/serial number instead of outputting oracles. Again for simplicity, we consider the leakage phase as two adversaries communicating over a classical channel: note that this is equivalent to the leakage phase from the original game.

<span id="page-51-3"></span>**Definition 23** (Quantum Key-Fire for Signing in the Classical Oracle Model). A public-key quantum key-fire scheme for signing QKeyFireSign in the classical oracle model consists of the following efficient algorithms.

- QKeyFireSign.Setup( $1^{\lambda}$ ): Takes in a security parameter, outputs an oracle  $\mathcal{O}$  as the verification key/serial number and a key state  $R_{\mathsf{flame}}$ .
- QKeyFireSign.Clone $^{\mathcal{O}}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}})$ : Takes in a key register  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}$ , outputs a new register  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{clone}}$  along with the input register  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}$ .
- QKeyFireSign.Sign $^{\mathcal{O}}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}, m)$ : Takes in a key register and a message m, outputs a signature.
- QKeyFireSign.Ver $^{\mathcal{O}}(m, sig)$ : Takes in a message and an alleged signature, outputs 1 or 0.

Evaluation Correctness: For all  $m \in \mathcal{M}$ ,

$$\Pr \bigg[ \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Ver}^{\mathcal{O}^*}(m,sig) = 1 : \begin{array}{c} \mathcal{O}^*, \mathsf{R_{key}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda}) \\ sig \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Sign}^{\mathcal{O}^*}(\mathsf{R_{kev}},m) \end{array} \bigg] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

**Strong cloning correctness:** This is defined the same as before: We require that output of QKeyFireSign.Setup( $1^{\lambda}$ ) is a pure state  $|\psi_{\mathcal{O}^*}\rangle$  and that clone on input  $|\psi_{\mathcal{O}^*}\rangle$  outputs two copies,  $|\psi_{\mathcal{O}^*}\rangle \otimes |\psi_{\mathcal{O}^*}\rangle$ .

<span id="page-51-2"></span>**Definition 24** (LOCC Leakage-Resilience Security for Quantum Key-Fire for Signing in the Classical Oracle Model). Let QKeyFireSign be a quantum key-fire scheme with classical oracles. Consider the following game between an adversary  $\mathcal{A} = (\mathcal{A}_1, \mathcal{A}_2)$  and a challenger.

# $\underline{\mathsf{LR}-\mathsf{SIGN}-\mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda})}$

- 1. The challenger samples sn,  $R_{key} \leftarrow QKeyFireSign.Setup(1^{\lambda})$  and submits  $R_{key}$  to the adversary  $A_1$ .
- 2. Parse  $\mathcal{O} = sn$ .

{52}------------------------------------------------

- 3. Leakage Phase:The adversaries A<sup>O</sup> 1 and A<sup>O</sup> 2 interact classically by exchanging classical messages for any number of rounds.
- 4. The challenger samples a random message m<sup>∗</sup> ← M.
- 5. The adversary A<sup>O</sup> 2 receives m<sup>∗</sup> , outputs sig<sup>∗</sup> .
- 6. The challenger checks if QKeyFireSign.VerO(m<sup>∗</sup> , sig<sup>∗</sup> ) = 1. If so, it outputs 1, otherwise it outputs 0.

We say that the quantum key-fire scheme QKeyFireSign satisfies LOCC leakage-resilience security if for any QPT (or query bounded, in case of unconditional oracle-based schemes) adversary A, we have

$$\Pr \Big[ \mathsf{LR} - \mathsf{SIGN} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1 \Big] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Note that this model also gives us the following conclusion. If the oracles of the scheme can be efficiently implemented (which is the case for our construction in [Section 9,](#page-53-0) assuming oneway functions), our oracle security proof will also imply that our scheme is secure assuming virtual black-box obfuscation in the plain model and thus heuristically secure assuming indistinguishability obfuscation. Separately, as discussed, through elementary tricks our model also can be converted to the standard classical oracle model with unconditional security.

{53}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-53-0"></span>9 Construction

In this section, we give a quantum key-fire construction relative to a quantumly-accessible classical oracle (Definition 23) for signing  $\nu(\lambda)$ -bit messages (where  $\nu(\lambda)$  is superlogarithmic), then prove its signing and cloning correctness. The security is proven in Section 10.

In Section 9.1, we describe our building block: incompressible one-shot signatures (OSS). Then, in Section 9.2, we give our construction.

Before moving onto the building block and construction, we introduce some notation.

**Oracle Algorithms** For a classical oracle  $\mathcal{O}$ , let  $U_{\mathcal{O}}$  denote its query execution unitary, that is, the unitary that maps  $|x\rangle |w\rangle |z\rangle$  to  $|x\rangle |w\rangle |z\oplus \mathcal{O}(x)\rangle$  where the registers respectively are the query input, workspace and query output registers. For a quantum query algorithm  $\mathcal{B}$ , there is an associated algorithm unitary  $U_{\mathcal{B}}$ , and the execution of  $\mathcal{B}$  with input R and oracle access to  $\mathcal{O}$  is simply applying  $(\mathcal{U}_{\mathcal{O}} \cdot U_{\mathcal{B}})^{p(\lambda)}$  to  $(\mathsf{R}, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux}})$  (where  $p(\lambda)$  is some polynomial and  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux}}$  is initialized to zeroes), and outputting (the whole or part of) the resulting register (after possibly measuring some parts of it in the computational basis)

### <span id="page-53-1"></span>9.1 Building Block: Incompressible One-Shot Signature Scheme

We will use an incompressible one-shot signature scheme OSS for 1-bit messages relative to a classical oracle (Definition 21) as a building block.

We make the following assumptions about OSS for presentation clarity, and all of these are without loss of generality.

Let  $t_1(\cdot), t_2(\cdot), t_3(\cdot), t_4(\cdot)$  be some polynomials.

- Since OSS is an incompressible OSS, it has split oracles (Definition 20): write ( $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.GenQKey}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Ver}$ ) =  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS}$  to denote its oracles. Let  $U_{OSS.GenQKey}$  be the algorithm unitary and let  $U_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.GenQKey}}$  be the query execution unitary for OSS.GenQKey, and similarly define  $U_{OSS.Sign}$ ,  $U_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}}$  for OSS.Sign.
- OSS.GenQKey $^{\mathcal{O}_{\text{OSS.GenQKey}}}(1^{\lambda})$ : Define  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{\text{OSS.GenQKey}},\text{OSS.GenQKey}} = (U_{\mathcal{O}_{\text{OSS.GenQKey}}} \cdot U_{\text{OSS.GenQKey}})^{t_2(\lambda)}$ . Then, this algorithm proceeds as follows:
  - 1. Introduce the auxiliary input register  $R_{\mathsf{inp-aux}}$  initialized to  $|0^{t_4(\lambda)}\rangle$ .
  - 2. Apply  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.GenQKey}},\mathsf{OSS.GenQKey}}$  to  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{inp-aux}}$  and parse the output into the registers:  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux}}$ .
  - 3. Measure  $R_{vk}$  to obtain the verification key vk.
  - 4. Output  $R_{kev}$  as the signing key and vk as the verification key.
- OSS.Sign<sup> $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}(vk, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{sk}}, m)$ </sup>: Define  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},OSS.Sign} = (U_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}} \cdot U_{OSS.Sign})^{t_1(\lambda)}$ . Then, this algorithm proceeds as follows:
  - 1. Introduce the auxiliary input register  $R_{\mathsf{inp-aux}}$  initialized to  $|0^{t_3(\lambda)}\rangle$ .
  - 2. Introduce the message register  $R_{msg}$  initialized to  $|m\rangle$ .
  - 3. Introduce the verification key register  $R_{vk}$  initialized to  $|vk\rangle$ .
  - 4. Apply  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},OSS.Sign}$  to  $(R_{vk}, R_{msg}, R_{sk}, R_{inp-aux})$  and parse the output into the registers:  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{out-aux}$  (registers  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$  are unmodified).
  - 5. Measure  $R_{sig}$  to obtain the signature sig.

{54}------------------------------------------------

- 6. Output sig.
- OSS.VerOOSS.Ver(vk, m, sig): Applies the oracle OOSS.Ver to obtain the output OOSS.Ver(vk, m, sig). If the output is 1, the algorithm outputs 1, otherwise it outputs 0[25](#page-54-1) .

# <span id="page-54-0"></span>9.2 Construction

Let ν(λ) be any polynomially bounded function. We now give our public-key quantum key-fire construction for signing ν(λ)-bit messages, with the classical oracle OQKeyFireSign = (O0, O1, O2, OOSS.Sign, O3, O4).

Let OSS be a one-shot signature scheme for 1-bit messages as described in [Section 9.1.](#page-53-1) Let p1(λ) denote the length of verification keys of OSS, p2(λ) denote the input length of the oracle OOSS.GenQKey.

#### QKeyFireSign.Setup(1<sup>λ</sup> )

- 1. Sample random functions H0, H1, Hsig where H<sup>0</sup> : {0, 1} <sup>p</sup>1(λ)+p2(λ) → {0, 1} λ , H<sup>1</sup> : {0, 1} <sup>p</sup>1(λ)+p2(λ) → {0, 1} λ .
- 2. Sample random function Hsig : {0, 1} <sup>ν</sup>(λ) → {0, 1} λ .
- 3. Sample (OOSS.GenQKey, OOSS.Sign, OOSS.Ver) ← OSS.GenOracles(1<sup>λ</sup> ).
- 4. Construct the oracle O0.

O0(ivk, isig, z)

Hardcoded: OOSS.Ver, H<sup>0</sup>

- 1. Check if OOSS.Ver(ivk, 0, isig) = 1. If not, output ⊥ and terminate.
- 2. Output H0(ivk||z).
- 5. Construct the oracle O1.

O1(ivk, isig, z)

Hardcoded: OOSS.Ver, H<sup>1</sup>

- 1. Check if OOSS.Ver(ivk, 1, isig) = 1. If not, output ⊥ and terminate.
- 2. Output H1(ivk||z).
- 6. Construct the oracle O2.

<span id="page-54-1"></span><sup>25</sup>The assumption about OSS.Ver is essentially that the signature verification procedure is classical and deterministic. It is easy to see that deterministic verification assumption is without loss of generality due to correctness with overwhelming probability. When we do not require the oracles to be efficiently implementable, classical verification assumption is also without loss of generality since any classical input - classical output quantum algorithm can be simulated by a classical oracle. However, in the efficient oracle case, the assumption about OSS.Ver might not be without loss of generality, but it is nevertheless true for our OSS construction in [Section 6.](#page-35-1) The assumptions about OSS.GenQKey and OSS.Sign are indeed without loss of generality in all cases.

{55}------------------------------------------------

## O2(ivk, y0, y1, z)

Hardcoded: H0, H1, OOSS.GenQKey

- 1. Check if y<sup>0</sup> = H0(ivk||z) and if y<sup>1</sup> = H1(ivk||z). If not, output ⊥ and terminate.
- 2. Output OOSS.GenQKey(z).
- 7. Construct the oracle O3.

## O3(ivk, y0, y1, m)

Hardcoded: H0, H1, Hsig

- 1. Check if y<sup>0</sup> = H0(ivk||m) and if y<sup>1</sup> = H1(ivk||m). If not, output ⊥ and terminate.
- 2. Output Hsig(m).
- 8. Construct the oracle O4.

# O4(m, y)

Hardcoded: Hsig

- 1. Output 1 if Hsig(m) = y, and output 0 otherwise.
- 9. Set sn = (O0, O1, O2, OOSS.Sign, O3, O4).
- 10. Simulate the purified version of OSS.GenQKeyOOSS.GenQKey (1<sup>λ</sup> ) and let (Rvk, Rkey, Rout−aux) be the output registers.
- 11. Output sn,(Rvk, Rkey, Rout−aux).

# QKeyFireSign.SignO(Rflame, m)

- 1. Parse (O0, O1, O2, OOSS.Sign, OOSS.Ver, O3, O4) = O.
- 2. Parse (Rvk, Rkey, Rout−aux) = Rflame.
- 3. Measure Rvk to obtain ivk.
- 4. Coherently run the following to obtain y<sup>0</sup> and then rewind (as in [Lemma 1\)](#page-23-3):
  - 1. Simulate OSS.SignOOSS.Sign (ivk, Rkey, 0), let isig be the output. Run O0(ivk, isig, m) and let y<sup>0</sup> be the output.
- 5. Coherently run the following to obtain y<sup>1</sup> and then rewind (as in [Lemma 1\)](#page-23-3):
  - 1. Simulate OSS.SignOOSS.Sign (ivk, Rkey, 0), let isig be the output. Run O1(ivk, isig, m) and let y<sup>1</sup> be the output.
- 6. Output O3(ivk, y0, y1, m).

{56}------------------------------------------------

# $\mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Ver}^{\mathcal{O}}(m,sig)$

- 1. Parse  $(\mathcal{O}_0, \mathcal{O}_1, \mathcal{O}_2, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_3, \mathcal{O}_4) = \mathcal{O}$ .
- 2. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4(m, sig)$ .

# $\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}.\mathsf{Clone}^{\mathcal{O}}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$

- 1. Parse  $(\mathcal{O}_0, \mathcal{O}_1, \mathcal{O}_2, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_3, \mathcal{O}_4) = \mathcal{O}$ .
- 2. Parse  $(R_{vk}, R_{key}, R_{out-aux,1}) = R_{flame}$ .
- 3. Create the registers  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{aux,2}$ ,  $R_{aux,3}$ ,  $R_{ora-out,4}$ ,  $R_{ora-out,5}$ . Initialize  $R_{aux,2}$  and  $R_{aux,3}$  to  $|0^{t_3(\lambda)}\rangle$  and  $|0^{t_4(\lambda)}\rangle$ . Initialize  $R_{ora-out,4}$  and  $R_{ora-out,5}$  to  $|0^{\lambda}\rangle$ . Initialize  $R_{msg}$  to  $|0\rangle$ . At some steps, we will parse  $R_{aux,3}$  as  $R_{ora-inp,3}$ ,  $R_{ora-out,3}$ ,  $R'_{aux,3}$ , as in the oracle query step of OSS.GenQKey, where  $U_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.GenQKey}}$  reads the oracle input input from  $R_{ora-inp,3}$  and writes the oracle output onto  $R_{ora-out,3}$ .
- 4. For  $t_2(\lambda)$  steps, execute the following.
  - 1. Apply  $U_{OSS.GenQKey}$  to  $R_{aux,3}$ .
  - 2. Execute the following (which essentially simulates the oracle call to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}}$ ):
    - 1. Apply  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},OSS.Sign}$  to  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{key}$ ,  $R_{aux,2}$ . Parse the output as  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{out-aux,2}$  as in OSS.Sign.
    - 2. Apply  $U_{\mathcal{O}_0}$  with input registers  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{ora-inp,3}$  and the output register  $R_{ora-out,4}$ .
    - 3. Apply  $(U'_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},OSS.Sign})^{-1}$  to  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{aux,2}$ , parse the output as  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{key}$ ,  $R_{aux,2}$ .
    - 4. Set  $R_{msg}$  to  $|1\rangle$ .
    - 5. Apply  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},OSS.Sign}$  to  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{key}$ ,  $R_{aux,2}$ . Parse the output as  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{out-aux,2}$  as in OSS.Sign.
    - 6. Apply  $U_{\mathcal{O}_1}$  with input registers  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{sig}}, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}$  and the output register  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}$ .
    - 7. Apply  $U_{\mathcal{O}_2}$  with input registers  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{ora-out,4}$ ,  $R_{ora-out,5}$  and the output register  $R_{ora-out,3}$ .
    - 8. Apply  $U_{\mathcal{O}_1}$  with input registers  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{ora-inp,3}$  and the output register  $R_{ora-out,5}$ .
    - 9. Apply  $(U'_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},OSS.Sign})^{-1}$  to  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{aux,2}$ , parse the output as  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{key}$ ,  $R_{aux,2}$ .
    - 10. Set  $R_{msg}$  to  $|0\rangle$ .
    - 11. Apply  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}$  to  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\;\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}$ .
    - 12. Apply  $U_{\mathcal{O}_0}$  with input registers  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{ora-inp,3}$  and the output register  $R_{ora-out,4}$ .
    - 13. Apply  $(U'_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},OSS.Sign})^{-1}$  to  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{aux,2}$ , parse the output as  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{msg}$ ,  $R_{key}$ ,  $R_{aux,2}$ .
- 5. Parse  $R_{aux,3}$  as  $R_{vk}^*$ ,  $R_{key}^*$ ,  $R_{out-aux}^*$  as in OSS.GenQKey.
- $6. \ \operatorname{Set} \ \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{clone}} = (\mathsf{R}^*_{\mathsf{vk}}, \mathsf{R}^*_{\mathsf{key}}, \mathsf{R}^*_{\mathsf{out-aux}}).$
- 7. Output  $R_{flame}$ ,  $R_{clone}$ .

{57}------------------------------------------------

Remark 1. As described above, the signing algorithm QKeyFireSign.Sign of our scheme consumes the flame state given to it. Note that thanks to the strong clonability correctness of the scheme, this is not a issue since one can clone the flame state before signing a message. However, if one insists on not consuming/altering the flame state while signing, this is also possible: Using the gentle measurement technique [\(Lemma 1\)](#page-23-3) it is also easy to see that the signing algorithm can be made so that it does not alter the state of the flame register (except up to negligible trace distance), since the output is pseudodeterministic (it is equal to Hsig(m) with overwhelming probability).

Remark 2. Aside from the conversion from quantum protection schemes for signing to quantum protection schemes for general unlearnable functionalities shown by the previous work, we can also slightly modify our construction above to achieve key-fire for unlearnable functionalities directly: Instead of O3, O4, we will just have a new O<sup>3</sup> which outputs f ∗ (x) after verifying y0, y1. The proof also follows the same, with the difference that at the final hybrid, instead of invoking [Theorem 21,](#page-83-1) we simply invoke the unlearnability of the functionality.

We claim that the construction satisfies correctness and security.

Theorem 16. QKeyFireSign satisfies quantum key-fire signing correctness, strong cloning correctness [\(Definition 18\)](#page-33-1). Let ν(λ) be superlogarithmic. Suppose OSS satisfies OOSS.Ver incompressibility and one-shot security, then QKeyFireSign satisfies unbounded (i.e. non-interactive) leakageresilience for signing unconditionally. Suppose OSS satisfies strong incompressibility and one-shot security, then QKeyFireSign satisfies LOCC leakage-resilience for signing [\(Definition 24\)](#page-51-2) unconditionally. Further, the oracles of QKeyFireSign can be implemented efficiently using a one-way function while preserving security (in which case, the security becomes computational rather than information-theoretic).

We prove the signing correctness and cloning correctness in [Sections 9.3](#page-58-0) and [9.4,](#page-58-1) and we prove security in [Section 10.](#page-63-0)

By implementing our construction using the incompressible one-shot signature we construct in [Theorem 9,](#page-36-2) we get the following corollary.

Theorem 17. Relative to a classical oracle, there exists a quantum key-fire scheme that satisfies LOCC leakage-resilience for signing functionality.

Theorem 18. Relative to a classical oracle, there exists a quantum key-fire scheme that satisfies LOCC leakage-resilience for any unlearnable functionality.

{58}------------------------------------------------

### <span id="page-58-0"></span>9.3 Proof of Signing Correctness

In this section, we prove the signing correctness of our scheme.

For simplicity, we will assume that OSS satisfies perfect correctness, and we will show that QKeyFireSign satisfies perfect signing correctness. Through elementary lemmas, this implies that if OSS satisfies correctness with overwhelming probability, then QKeyFireSign also satisfies signing correctness with overwhelming probability.

We first observe that the flame states of our scheme  $(sn, |\psi\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux}}})$  output by  $\mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda})$  are the same as the purified output of  $\mathsf{OSS.GenQKey}$  (whose original version traces out  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux}}$  and measures  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}$ , but  $\mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}$  does neither since it is purified). Then,  $\mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Sign}$  first measures  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}$  to obtain some value ivk and (effectively) traces out  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux}}$ . This collapses the state to the one-shot signature key with the serial number ivk. By signing correctness of  $\mathsf{OSS}$  and definition of  $\mathcal{O}_0$ , we get  $y_0 = H_0(ivk||m)$  with probability 1. Thus, by Lemma 1, the signing key is indeed not altered since we are rewinding. Then again by signing correctness of  $\mathsf{OSS}$  and definition of  $\mathcal{O}_1$ , we get  $y_1 = H_1(ivk||m)$  with probability 1. Hence, the output of the signing algorithm is  $\mathcal{O}_3(ivk, H_0(ivk||m), H_1(ivk||m), m)$  which is equal to  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}(m)$ . Due to the definition of the verification algorithm, this completes the proof of signing correctness.

### <span id="page-58-1"></span>9.4 Proof of Strong Cloning Correctness

In this section, we prove the strong cloning correctness of our scheme.

First, we note that the flame states of our scheme are indeed pure states as required for strong cloning correctness. Observe that the state output by QKeyFireSign.Setup is simply  $|\psi_{flame}\rangle = (U_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.GenQKey}} \cdot U_{OSS.GenQKey})^{t_2(\lambda)} |0^{t_4(\lambda)}\rangle$ . This is also the same as the purified output of OSS.GenQKey (whose not-purified version traces out  $R_{out-aux}$  and measures  $R_{vk}$ , but QKeyFireSign.Setup does neither).

For simplicity, we will assume that OSS satisfies perfect correctness, and we will show that QKeyFireSign satisfies perfect strong cloning correctness. Through elementary lemmas, this implies that if OSS satisfies correctness with overwhelming probability, then QKeyFireSign also satisfies strong cloning correctness with overwhelming probability.

We first prove the following lemma.

**Lemma 4.** During the loop in QKeyFireSign.Clone, if the state over the registers R<sub>vk</sub>, R<sub>key</sub>, R<sub>out-aux,1</sub>, R<sub>msg</sub>, R<sub>aux,2</sub>, R<sub>aux,3</sub>, R<sub>ora-out,4</sub>, R<sub>ora-out,5</sub> is

$$\left|\psi_{flame}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux},1}}\otimes\left|0\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\otimes\left|\zeta\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}$$

at the beginning of an iteration, then the state at the end of that iteration is

$$|\psi_{flame}\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux},1}} \otimes |0\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}} \otimes \left|0^{p_2(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}} \otimes (U_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}}} \cdot U_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}} \left|\zeta\right\rangle) \otimes \left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}} \otimes \left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}.$$

*Proof.* We will show the result by writing the state of the registers after each step of the iteration. The actual order of the registers will stay the same throughout, however, when writing the state we will reorder some registers for convenience of notation.

We also introduce the following notation for conciseness.

• 
$$|\psi_{flame}\rangle = \sum_{vk,w} \beta_{vk,w} |vk\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}} \otimes |\phi_{vk,w}\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{kev}}} \otimes |w\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux}}}$$

• 
$$U_1 = U_{\text{OSS.GenQKey}}$$
,

{59}------------------------------------------------

• 
$$U_2 = U_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.GenQKey}}}$$
,

$$\bullet \ U = U_2 \cdot U_1,$$

• 
$$U_1 |\zeta\rangle = \sum_{z,o,w'} \gamma_{z,o,w'} |z\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}} \otimes |o\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}} \otimes |w'\rangle_{\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{aux},3}}.$$

Now we show the evolution of the state during the loop.

1. After applying  $U_{OSS.GenQKey}$  to  $R_{aux,3}$ , we get

$$\left|\psi_{flame}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux},1}}\otimes\left|0\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\otimes\left(U_{1}\left|\zeta\right\rangle\right)_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}$$

2. After applying  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}$  to  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2},$  we get

$$|0\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}} \otimes \left(\sum_{vk,w} \beta_{vk,w} \, |vk\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}} \otimes \sum_{sig} \alpha_{vk,w,sig} \, |sig\rangle\right) \otimes (U_1 \, |\zeta\rangle)_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}} \otimes \left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}} \otimes \left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}$$

where for each vk, w, sig with  $\beta_{vk,w} \neq 0$  and  $\alpha_{vk,w,sig} \neq 0$  we have that  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}^*(vk, sig, 0) = 1$  by correctness of OSS.Sign.

3. After applying  $U_{\mathcal{O}_0}$  with input registers  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{ora-inp,3}$  and the output register  $R_{ora-out,4}$ , we get

$$\begin{split} |0\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}} \otimes \bigg( \sum_{\substack{vk,w\\z,o,w'}} \beta_{vk,w} \, |vk\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}} \otimes (\sum_{sig} \alpha_{vk,w,sig}) \gamma_{z,o,w'} \, |z\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}} \otimes \\ |o\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}} \otimes |\mathcal{O}_0(vk,sig_{vk,w},z)\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}} \otimes |w'\rangle_{\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{aux},3}} \bigg) \otimes \Big|0^\lambda \Big\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}} \end{split}$$

which is equal to

$$\left( \sum_{vk,w} \beta_{vk,w} \left( |vk\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}} \otimes \left( \sum_{z,o,w'} \gamma_{z,o,w'} |z\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}} |o\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}} |H_0(vk,z)\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}} \otimes |w'\rangle_{\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{aux},3}} \right) \right) \otimes \\ |sig_{vk,w}\rangle \right) \otimes \left| 0^{\lambda} \right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}$$

4. After applying  $(U'_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}},\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{Sign}})^{-1}$  to  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{crs}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{sig}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2},$  we get

$$\begin{split} &\left(\sum_{vk,w}\beta_{vk,w}\left(|vk\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}}\otimes\left(\sum_{z,o,w'}\gamma_{z,o,w'}|z\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}}|o\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}}|H_{0}(vk,z)\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\otimes\left|w'\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{aux},3}}\right)\right)\otimes\\ &\left|\phi_{vk,w}\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}}\otimes|w\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux}}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\right)\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}} \end{split}$$

{60}------------------------------------------------

- 5. After applying X to  $R_{msg}$ , this register changes from  $|0\rangle$  to  $|1\rangle$ , and the others are unaffected.
- 6. After applying  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}},\mathsf{Sign}},\mathsf{OSS},\mathsf{Sign}$  to  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}$  we get

$$\begin{split} &\left(\sum_{vk,w}\beta_{vk,w}\left(|vk\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}}\otimes\left(\sum_{z,o,w'}\gamma_{z,o,w'}|z\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}}|o\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}}|H_{0}(vk,z)\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\otimes|w'\rangle_{\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{aux},3}}\right)\right)\otimes\\ &\sum_{sig}\alpha'_{vk,w,sig}\left|sig\rangle\right)\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}} \end{split}$$

where for each vk, w, sig with  $\beta_{vk,w} \neq 0$  and  $\alpha'_{vk,w,sig} \neq 0$  we have that  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}(vk,sig,1) = 1$  by correctness of OSS.Sign.

7. After applying  $U_{\mathcal{O}_1}$  with input registers  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}$ ,  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{sig}}$ ,  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora}-\mathsf{inp},3}$  and the output register  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora}-\mathsf{out},5}$ , we get

$$\begin{split} &\left(\sum_{vk,w}\beta_{vk,w}\bigg(\left.|vk\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}}\otimes \big(\sum_{z,o,w'}\gamma_{z,o,w'}\left|z\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}}\left|o\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}}\left|H_{0}(vk,z)\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\left|H_{1}(vk,z)\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}\otimes \\ &\left.|w'\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}'}\big)\right)\otimes\sum_{sig}\alpha'_{vk,w,sig}\left|sig\right\rangle\bigg) \end{split}$$

8. After applying  $U_{\mathcal{O}_2}$  with input registers  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{ora-out,4}$ ,  $R_{ora-out,5}$  and the output register  $R_{ora-out,3}$ , we get

$$\begin{split} &\left(\sum_{vk,w}\beta_{vk,w}\left(\left.|vk\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}}\otimes\left(\sum_{z,o,w'}\gamma_{z,o,w'}\left|z\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}}\left|o\oplus\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}(z)}^{*}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}}\left|H_{0}(vk,z)\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\\ &\left.|H_{1}(vk,z)\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}\otimes\left|w'\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{dux},3}^{\prime}}\right)\right)\otimes\sum_{sig}\alpha'_{vk,w,sig}\left|sig\right\rangle\right) \end{split}$$

9. After applying  $U_{\mathcal{O}_1}$  with input registers  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{sig}}, \mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}$  and the output register  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}$ , we get

$$\begin{split} &\left(\sum_{vk,w}\beta_{vk,w}\bigg(\left|vk\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}}\otimes \big(\sum_{z,o,w'}\gamma_{z,o,w'}\left|z\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}}\Big|o\oplus\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}(z)}^*\right)_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}}\left|H_0(vk,z)\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\\ &\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}\otimes \left|w'\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}'}\big)\bigg)\otimes\sum_{sig}\alpha'_{vk,w,sig}\left|sig\right\rangle\bigg) \end{split}$$

{61}------------------------------------------------

10. After applying  $(U'_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},OSS.Sign})^{-1}$  to  $R_{vk}, R_{msg}, R_{sig}, R_{aux,2}$ , we get

$$\begin{split} &\left(\sum_{vk,w}\beta_{vk,w}\left(\left.\left|vk\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}}\otimes\left(\sum_{z,o,w'}\gamma_{z,o,w'}\left|z\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}}\left|o\oplus\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}(z)}^{*}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}}\left|H_{0}(vk,z)\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\right.\\ &\left.\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}\otimes\left|w'\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{dux},3}^{*}}\right)\right)\otimes\left|\phi_{vk,w}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}}\otimes\left|w\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux},1}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\right) \end{split}$$

- 11. After applying X to  $R_{msg}$ , this register changes from  $|1\rangle$  to  $|0\rangle$ , and the others are unaffected.
- 12. After applying  $U'_{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},OSS.Sign}$  to  $R_{crs}, R_{vk}, R_{key}, R_{msg}, R_{aux,2}$ , we get

$$\begin{split} &\left(\sum_{vk,w}\beta_{vk,w}\left(\left.|vk\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}}\otimes\left(\sum_{z,o,w'}\gamma_{z,o,w'}\left|z\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}}\left|o\oplus\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}(z)}^{*}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}}\left|H_{0}(vk,z)\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\\ &\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}\otimes\left|w'\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}^{\prime}}\right)\right)\otimes\sum_{sig}\alpha_{vk,w,sig}\left|sig\right\rangle\right) \end{split}$$

where for each vk, w, sig with  $\beta_{vk,w} \neq 0$  and  $\alpha_{vk,w,sig} \neq 0$  we have that  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}^*(crs^*, vk, sig, 0) = 1$  by correctness of OSS.Sign.

13. After applying  $U_{\mathcal{O}_0}$  with input registers  $R_{vk}$ ,  $R_{sig}$ ,  $R_{ora-inp,3}$  and the output register  $R_{ora-out,4}$ , we get

$$\begin{split} &\left(\sum_{vk,w}\beta_{vk,w}\left(\left.\left|vk\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}}\otimes\left(\sum_{z,o,w'}\gamma_{z,o,w'}\left|z\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}}\left|o\oplus\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}(z)}^{*}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\right|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}\right|0^{\lambda}$$

14. After applying  $(U'_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathsf{OSS.Sign}})^{-1}$  to  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{sig}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}$ , we get

$$\begin{split} &\left(\sum_{vk,w}\beta_{vk,w}\left(\left.\left|vk\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}}}\otimes\left(\sum_{z,o,w'}\gamma_{z,o,w'}\left|z\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-inp},3}}\left|o\oplus\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}(z)}^{*}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},3}}\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\right.\\ &\left.\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}\otimes\left|w'\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}^{\prime}}\right)\right)\otimes\left|\phi_{vk,w}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}}}\otimes\left|w\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux},1}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\right) \end{split}$$

which is equal to

$$\begin{split} &|\psi_{flame}\rangle\otimes|0\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\otimes U_{2}(U_{1}\left|\zeta\right\rangle)\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}} = \\ &|\psi_{flame}\rangle\otimes|0\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\otimes U\left|\zeta\right\rangle\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}} \end{split}$$

as claimed.

{62}------------------------------------------------

It is easy to see that the strong cloning correctness follows easily with this lemma: The loop starts with the state

$$\left|\psi\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux},1}}\otimes\left|0\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}},$$

thus, at the end, we get the state

$$\begin{split} &|\psi_{flame}\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux},1}}\otimes|0\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\otimes(U^{p_{1}(\lambda)}\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle)_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}}\otimes\\ &\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}=\\ &|\psi_{flame}\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{vk}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{key}},\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{out-aux},1}}\otimes|0\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{msg}}}\otimes\left|0^{p_{2}(\lambda)}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},2}}\otimes(|\psi\rangle)_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{aux},3}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},4}}\otimes\left|0^{\lambda}\right\rangle_{\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{ora-out},5}}. \end{split}$$

Hence, the algorithm outputs  $|\psi_{flame}\rangle \otimes |\psi_{flame}\rangle$ .

{63}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-63-0"></span>10 Proof of Security of the Main Construction

In this section, we prove the security of our scheme. Throughout the proof, we will refer to the adversary that gets the flame state  $(A_1)$  as the sender adversary and to the adversary that outputs the forged signature as the receiver adversary  $(A_2)$ .

Suppose for a contradiction that there exists a query-bounded adversary  $\mathcal{A} = (\mathcal{A}_1, \mathcal{A}_2)$  such that  $\Pr[\mathsf{LR} - \mathsf{SIGN} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1] > \frac{1}{q^*(\lambda)}$  for some polynomial  $q^*(\cdot)$  and infinitely many values  $\lambda > 0$ . Note that  $\mathcal{A}_1, \mathcal{A}_2$  will have query access to the oracles  $\mathcal{O}_0, \mathcal{O}_1, \mathcal{O}_2, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}, \mathcal{O}_3, \mathcal{O}_4$  of the construction.

**Adversary Assumptions** Without loss of generality, we make the following assumptions about the adversaries  $A_1, A_2$  (where  $u(\lambda), t(\lambda)$  are some polynomials), and we also define some notation.

- $(A_1, A_2)$  runs for exactly  $u(\lambda)$  rounds with probability 1, where each round consists of a message from  $A_1$  to  $A_2$  and then a message from  $A_2$  to  $A_1$  (except for the last round where  $A_2$  outputs  $\bot$  as its message).
- We will denote the *i*-round of  $\mathcal{A}_1$  as  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}$ , for  $i \in [u(\lambda)]$ . That is, at round i,  $\mathcal{A}_1$  simply executes  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}$  on its internal state register to obtain its message and the updated internal state register.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}$  makes a total of  $t(\lambda)$  queries to the oracles.
- Similar to above, we will denote the *i*-th round of  $\mathcal{A}_2$  as  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}$  for  $i \in [u(\lambda)]$ . Note that for  $\mathcal{A}_{2,u(\lambda)}$ , the message output by it is  $\bot$  since there is no message from  $\mathcal{A}_2$  to  $\mathcal{A}_1$ . Finally, we will write  $\mathcal{A}_{2,\text{final}}$  to denote the challenge phase of the adversary  $\mathcal{A}_2$ : It receives the internal state register produced by  $\mathcal{A}_{2,u(\lambda)}$  and the challenge message to be signed from the challenger and outputs a signature.
- Every round (i.e. for all  $\ell \in [u(\lambda)]$ ), queries of  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}$  to the oracles  $\mathcal{O}_0, \mathcal{O}_1, \mathcal{O}_2$  proceeds in triples: It first makes one query to  $\mathcal{O}_0$ , then to  $\mathcal{O}_1$ , and then to  $\mathcal{O}_2$ . We will call these groups of three queries a query-triplet. Further, we assume that each round,  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}$  has exactly  $t(\lambda)$  query-triplets, with any (polynomial) number of queries to the other oracles in between the triplets but with a total of exactly  $t(\lambda)$  queries to each of the oracles  $\mathcal{O}_3, \mathcal{O}_4, \mathcal{O}_{\text{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_{\text{OSS.Ver}}$  during the round. Note that this means that  $\mathcal{A}_2$  has a total of  $u(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda)$  query-triplets and a total of  $2u(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda)$  over the leakage protocol.

Note that without loss of generality, we can take  $t(\lambda) = 1$  by modifying our adversaries, since we do not impose an a-priori bound on the number of rounds. Similarly, without loss of generality, we can assume that each round, queries of  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}$  to  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_3$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_4$  occur in this order, after its queries to  $\mathcal{O}_0$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_1$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_2$ .

Organization of the proof Our proof will be done through a sequence of hybrids,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$  (which is the original game  $\mathsf{LR} - \mathsf{SIGN} - \mathsf{GAME}_\mathcal{A}(1^\lambda)$ ) through  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$  (with some additional subhybrids in between). In the remainder of this section, we simply state our main theorems: We state our theorem about the indistinguishability of the first and the last hybrid (Theorem 19), and about the security in the final hybrid  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$  (Theorem 20). Then, combining these main theorems simply proves the security of our scheme. The main theorems then are then proven in the subsequent subsections. In more detail, our proof is organized as follows.

In Section 10.1, we define various modified adversaries that we use in our hybrids. Then, in Section 10.2, we give the definitions of our hybrids. Then in Section 10.3, we prove Theorem 19,

{64}------------------------------------------------

that is, we show the indistinguishability of our hybrids (except for  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,0}, \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,1}$  which we prove in Section 11). Finally, in Section 10.4, we prove Theorem 20, that is, we show the security in the final hybrid.

We now give our main theorem statements about the hybrids (which are defined in Section 10.2).

<span id="page-64-1"></span>Theorem 19. 
$$|\mathsf{Hyb}_0 - \mathsf{Hyb}_3| \leq \frac{1}{2 \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$$

We prove this theorem in Section 10.3.

<span id="page-64-2"></span>**Theorem 20.** 
$$Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_3 = 1] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$$
.

We prove this theorem in Section 10.4.

Now we complete the proof of security assuming these two theorems. We had assumed for a contradiction that  $\Pr[\mathsf{LR} - \mathsf{SIGN} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1] = \Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_0 = 1] > \frac{1}{q^*(\lambda)}$  for some polynomial  $q^*(\cdot)$  and infinitely many values  $\lambda > 0$ . Combining this with Theorem 19, we get that  $\Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_3 = 1] > \frac{1}{2q^*(\lambda)}$  for infinitely many  $\lambda > 0$ . However, this is a contradiction by Theorem 20. Therefore, our contradiction hypothesis is wrong, and thus we get  $\Pr[\mathsf{LR} - \mathsf{SIGN} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , completing the proof of security.

### <span id="page-64-0"></span>10.1 Defining Modified Adversaries

In this section, we define the modified adversaries we will be using in the hybrids. We will explicitly denote the section queries to the oracles  $H_0, H_1$ .

We define  $A_{1,u(\lambda)+1}$  and  $A_{2,u(\lambda)+1}$  as follows.

$$\underline{\mathcal{A}_{1,u(\lambda)+1}^{\mathcal{O}}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}},S)}$$

1. Output  $\perp$ .

$$\mathcal{A}_{2,u(\lambda)+1}^{\mathcal{O}}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}},L)$$

- 1. Sample  $m' \leftarrow \mathcal{M}$ .
- 2.  $sig \leftarrow \mathcal{A}_{2,\mathsf{final}}^{\mathcal{O}}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}}, m').$
- 3. Output  $\perp$ , (m', siq).

We define  $\mathcal{B}_{1,0}, \mathcal{B}_{2,0}$ .

$$\underline{\mathcal{B}_{1,0}^{(\mathcal{O}_0,\mathcal{O}_1,\mathcal{O}_2,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4)}(\mathsf{R})}$$

1. Output  $R, \perp$ .

{65}------------------------------------------------

$$\mathcal{B}_{2,0}^{(\mathcal{O}_0,\mathcal{O}_1,\mathcal{O}_2,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4)}(T)$$

1. Output  $\perp$ .

For  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 2]$ , we define the adversaries  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell}, \mathcal{B}_{2,\ell}$ .

$$\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell}^{(\mathcal{O}_0,\mathcal{O}_1,\mathcal{O}_2,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4)}(\mathsf{R})$$

- 1.  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}}, (T, S) \leftarrow \mathcal{B}_{1, \ell-1}^{(\mathcal{O}_0, \mathcal{O}_1, \mathcal{O}_2, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_3, \mathcal{O}_4)}(\mathsf{R}).$
- 2.  $\mathsf{R}'_{\mathsf{internal}}, L \leftarrow \mathcal{A}^{(\mathcal{O}_0, \mathcal{O}_1, \mathcal{O}_2, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}_3, \mathcal{O}_4)}_{1,\ell}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}}, S).$
- 3.  $V \leftarrow \mathcal{Q}_{1,\ell}^{(\mathcal{O}_0,\mathcal{O}_1,\mathcal{O}_2,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4)}(T,L).$
- 4. Set  $X_4$  to be the empty set.
- 5. For  $j \in [512^2 \cdot (t(\lambda))^6 \cdot \lambda^8 \cdot (u(\lambda))^4 \cdot (q^*(\lambda))^4 \cdot (\ell)^2]$ :
  - 1. Sample a random index ind between 1 and the number of oracle queries made by  $Q_{2,\ell}$ .
  - 2. Simulate  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_4}(V)$  until right before its *ind*-th oracle query is executed and measure the query input register instead of executing the query. Let m, y be the measurement outcome.
  - 3. Check if  $\mathcal{O}_4(m,y)$  is 1. If so, add (m,y) to  $X_4$ .
- 6. Simulate  $Q_{2,\ell}(V)$  with the following oracle  $\mathcal{O}'$ : On input m, y, output 1 if  $(m, y) \in X_4$ , otherwise output 0. Let  $(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}}, S)$  be the output.
- 7. Set  $T_{new} = (T, (V, X_4, S))$ .
- 8. Output  $R'_{internal}$ ,  $(T_{new}, S)$ .

# $\underline{\mathcal{B}_{2,\ell}(T)}$

- 1. Parse  $(T_{prev}, (V, X_4, S)) = T$ .
- 2. Until S' = S:
  - 1. Simulate  $Q_{2,\ell}(V)$  with the following oracle  $\mathcal{O}'$ : On input m, y, output 1 if  $(m, y) \in X_4$ , otherwise output 0. Let  $(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}}, S')$  be the output.
- 3. Output  $R_{internal}$ , S.

C-Adversaries We define  $C_{1,\ell,0,2}$  to be the following algorithm: On input (T,L), output (T,L),  $L,(X_{0,0},X_{1,0},X_{2,0},D_{0,0},D_{1,0},D_{2,0}))$  where  $X_{0,0},X_{1,0},X_{2,0}$  are empty sets and  $D_{0,0},D_{1,0},D_{2,0}$  are empty databases. We define  $C_{2,\ell,0,2}(Y)$  to be the algorithm that runs  $A_{2,\ell}(R,L)$  after parsing (T,L,Y')=Y and executing  $R \leftarrow \mathcal{B}_{2,\ell}(T)$ .

For  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ ,  $j \in [t(\lambda)]$  we define  $C_{1,\ell,j,0}, C_{2,\ell,j,0}$ .

{66}------------------------------------------------

#### C (O0,O1,O2,OOSS.Sign,O3,O4) 1,ℓ,j,0 (T , L)

- 1. Y ← C(O0,O1,O2,OOSS.Sign,O3,O4) 1,ℓ,j−1,2 (T , L).
- 2. Parse (T , L, ((X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1])) = Y .
- 3. Initialize X0,j to be the empty set and D0,j to be an empty set.
- 4. For i ∈ [4194304 · λ 10 · t 2 (λ) · (ℓ) 5 · (u(λ) · q ∗ (λ) · t(λ))<sup>4</sup> ]:
  - 1. Run C2,ℓ,j−1,<sup>2</sup> on input Y until its first query to O<sup>0</sup> but do not execute the query. Instead, measure the query input register and let ivk, isig, z be the measurement result. During this procedure[a](#page-66-0) , C2,ℓ,j−1,<sup>2</sup> makes queries to OOSS.Sign, O3, O<sup>4</sup> which are executed by forwarding them to the corresponding oracles.
  - 2. If O0(ivk, isig, z) ̸= ⊥, add (ivk, isig) to X0,j and set D0,j (ivk||z) = O0(ivk, isig, z) for all z (section query).
- 5. Output (T , L, ((X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1])).

#### C (O0,O1,O2,OOSS.Sign,O3,O4) 2,ℓ,j,0 (Y )

- 1. Parse (T , L, ((X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1])) = Y .
- 2. Set Y ′ = (T , L,((X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1],(X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1],(D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1])).
- 3. Run C2,ℓ,j−1,<sup>2</sup> on input Y ′ with the oracles (O0, O1, O2, OOSS.Sign, O3, O4), but only the first query to O<sup>0</sup> is instead simulated as follows: On input ivk, isig, z, output D0,j (ivk||z) if (ivk, isig) ∈ X0,j and otherwise output ⊥. Let Rinternal, S be the output.
- 4. Output Rinternal, S.

For ℓ ∈ [u(λ) + 1], j ∈ [t(λ)] we define C1,ℓ,j,1,C2,ℓ,j,1.

#### C (O0,O1,O2,OOSS.Sign,O3,O4) 1,ℓ,j,1 (T , L)

- 1. Y ← C(O0,O1,O2,OOSS.Sign,O3,O4) 1,ℓ,j,0 (T , L).
- 2. Parse (T , L, ((X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1])) = Y .
- 3. Initialize X1,j to be the empty set and D1,j to be an empty set.

<span id="page-66-0"></span><sup>a</sup>Note that C1,ℓ,j−1,<sup>2</sup> does not make any queries to O1, O<sup>2</sup> before making its first query to O0.

{67}------------------------------------------------

- 4. For i ∈ [4194304 · λ 10 · t 2 (λ) · (ℓ) 5 · (u(λ) · q ∗ (λ) · t(λ))<sup>4</sup> ]:
  - 1. Run C2,ℓ,j,<sup>0</sup> on input Y until its first query to O<sup>1</sup> but do not execute the query. Instead, measure the query input register and let ivk, isig be the measurement result. During this procedure[a](#page-67-0) , C2,ℓ,j,<sup>0</sup> makes queries to OOSS.Sign, O3, O<sup>4</sup> which are executed by forwarding them to the corresponding oracles.
  - 2. If O1(ivk, isig, z) ̸= ⊥, add (ivk, isig) to X1,j and set D1,j (ivk||z) = O1(ivk, isig, z) for all z (section query).
- 5. Output (T , L,(X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1],(D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1]).

#### C (O0,O1,O2,OOSS.Sign,O3,O4) 2,ℓ,j,1 (Y )

- 1. Parse (T , L, ((X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1])) = Y .
- 2. Y ′ = (T , L, ((X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1], (D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] , (D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1],(D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1])).
- 3. Run C2,ℓ,j,<sup>0</sup> on input Y ′ with the oracles (O0, O1, O2, OOSS.Sign, O3, O4), but only the first query to O<sup>1</sup> is instead simulated as follows: On input ivk, isig, z, output D1,j (ivk||z) if (ivk, isig) ∈ X1,j and otherwise output ⊥. Let Rinternal, S be the output.
- 4. Output Rinternal, S.

For ℓ ∈ [u(λ) + 1], j ∈ [t(λ)] we define C1,ℓ,j,2,C2,ℓ,j,2.

#### C (O0,O1,O2,OOSS.Sign,O3,O4) 1,ℓ,j,2 (T , L)

- 1. Y ← C(O0,O1,O2,OOSS.Sign,O3,O4) 1,ℓ,j,1 (T , L).
- 2. Parse (T , L,((X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1],(D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j−1])) = Y .
- 3. Initialize X2,j to be the empty set and D2,j to be an empty set.
- 4. For i ∈ [512 · λ · (t(λ) · ℓ) · λ 4 · (u(λ) · q ∗ (λ) · t(λ))<sup>2</sup> ]:
  - 1. Run C2,ℓ,j,<sup>1</sup> on input Y until its first query to O<sup>2</sup> but do not execute the query. Instead, measure the query input register and let ivk, y0, y1, z be the measurement result. During this procedure[a](#page-67-1) , C2,ℓ,j,<sup>1</sup> makes queries to OOSS.Sign, O3, O<sup>4</sup> which are executed by forwarding them to the corresponding oracles.
  - 2. If O2(ivk, y0, y1, z) ̸= ⊥, add (ivk, y0, y1, z) to X2,j and set D2,j (z) = O2(ivk, y0, y1, z).
- 5. Output (T , L,(X0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(X1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(X2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(D0,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(D1,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ,(D2,j′)<sup>j</sup> ′∈[j] ).

<span id="page-67-0"></span><sup>a</sup>Note that C1,ℓ,j,<sup>0</sup> does not make any queries to O0, O<sup>2</sup> before making its first query to O1.

<span id="page-67-1"></span><sup>a</sup>Note that C1,ℓ,j,<sup>1</sup> does not make any queries to O0, O<sup>1</sup> before making its first query to O2.

{68}------------------------------------------------

# $\underline{\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell,j,2}^{(\mathcal{O}_0,\mathcal{O}_1,\mathcal{O}_2,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4)}}(Y)$

- 1. Parse  $(T, L, ((X_{0,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (X_{1,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (X_{2,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (D_{0,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (D_{1,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (D_{2,j'})_{j' \in [j]})) = Y.$
- 2.  $Y' = (T, L, ((X_{0,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (X_{1,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (X_{2,j'})_{j' \in [j-1]}, (D_{0,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (D_{1,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (D_{2,j'})_{j' \in [j-1]})).$
- 3. Run  $C_{2,\ell,j,1}$  on input Y' with the oracles  $(\mathcal{O}_0, \mathcal{O}_1, \mathcal{O}_2, \mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}, \mathcal{O}_3, \mathcal{O}_4)$ , but only the first query to  $\mathcal{O}_2$  is instead simulated as follows: On input  $ivk, y_0, y_1, z$ , output  $D_{2,j}(z)$  if  $(ivk, y_0, y_1, z) \in X_{2,j}$  and otherwise output  $\bot$ . Let  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}}, S$  be the output.
- 4. Output  $R_{internal}$ , S.

We define  $C_{1,\ell}, C_{2,\ell}$  to be  $C_{1,\ell,t(\lambda),2}$  and  $C_{2,\ell,t(\lambda),2}$ , respectively. For ease of reference, we write the full description of  $C_{2,\ell}$  with the internal calls unwound.

# $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4}(Y)$

- 1. Parse  $(T, L, ((X_{0,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (X_{1,j'})_{j' \in [t(\lambda)]}, (X_{2,j'})_{j' \in [j]}, (D_{0,j'})_{j' \in [t(\lambda)]}, (D_{1,j'})_{j' \in [t(\lambda)]}, (D_{2,j'})_{j' \in [t(\lambda)]})) = Y.$
- 2. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{2,\ell-1}(T)$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}}$ .
- 3. Simulate  $\mathcal{A}_{2,\ell}^{(\mathcal{O}_0',\mathcal{O}_1',\mathcal{O}_2',\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}}^*,\mathcal{O}_3^*,\mathcal{O}_4^*)}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}},L)$  where
  - The *i*-th (for  $i \in [t(\lambda)]$ ) query-triplet to the oracles  $\mathcal{O}'_0, \mathcal{O}'_1, \mathcal{O}'_2$  is executed with the oracles  $\mathcal{O}^i_0, \mathcal{O}^i_1, \mathcal{O}^i_2$  defined as follows.
    - $-\mathcal{O}_0^i(ivk, isig, z)$ : If  $(ivk, isig) \not\in X_{0,i}$ , output  $\bot$ . Otherwise, output  $(D_{0,i}(ivk||z))$ .
    - $-\mathcal{O}_1^i(ivk, isig, z)$ : If  $(ivk, isig) \not\in X_{1,i}$ , output  $\bot$ . Otherwise, output  $(D_{1,i}(ivk||z))$ .
    - $-\mathcal{O}_2^i(ivk,y_0,y_1,z)$ : If  $(ivk,y_0,y_1,z) \notin X_{2,i}$ , output  $\perp$ . Otherwise, output  $D_{2,i}(z)$ .

Let  $R'_{internal}$ , S be the output.

4. Output  $R'_{internal}$ , S.

 $\mathcal{R}$ -Adversaries For  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ , we define the adversaries  $\mathcal{R}_{1,\ell}, \mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}$ .

# $\mathcal{R}_{1,\ell}^{(\mathcal{O}_0,\mathcal{O}_1,\mathcal{O}_2,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4)}(T,L)$

- 1. Set  $X_{sign}$  to be the empty set.
- 2.  $Y \leftarrow \mathcal{C}_{1,\ell}^{(\mathcal{O}_0,\mathcal{O}_1,\mathcal{O}_2,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4)}(T,L)$ .
- 3. For  $j \in [\lambda^8 \cdot \ell^2 \cdot (t(\lambda))^4 \cdot (n(\lambda))^2 \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2 \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2]$ :
  - 1. Sample a random index ind between 1 and the number of oracle queries by  $C_{2,\ell}$  to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}$ .

{69}------------------------------------------------

- 2. Simulate  $C_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4}(Y)$  until right before its *ind*-th oracle query to  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}$  is executed and measure the query input register instead of executing the query. Let vk, x be the measurement outcome. Check if  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}(vk, x) \neq 0$  and if  $x \notin Span(\{v: (vk, v) \in X_{sign}\})$  and if so add (vk, x) to  $X_{sign}$ .
- 4. Output  $(Y, X_{sign})$ .

# $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4}(G)$

- 1. Parse  $(Y, X_{sign}) = G$ .
- 2. Define the oracle  $\mathcal{O}'_{sign}$ : On input vk, z, output 1 if  $z \notin \mathsf{Span}(\{v : (vk, v) \in X_{sign}\}) \setminus \{0\}$ . Otherwise, output 0.
- 3. Simulate  $C_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}'_{sign},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4}(Y)$  to obtain  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}}, S$ .
- 4. Output Rinternal, S.
- **Q-Adversaries** For  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ , we define the adversaries  $\mathcal{Q}_{1,\ell}, \mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}$ .

$$\mathcal{Q}_{1,\ell}^{(\mathcal{O}_0,\mathcal{O}_1,\mathcal{O}_2,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4)}(T,L)$$

- 1. Set  $X_3$  to be the empty list.
- 2. Set  $D_3$  to be empty database.
- 3.  $G \leftarrow \mathcal{R}_{1,\ell}^{(\mathcal{O}_0,\mathcal{O}_1,\mathcal{O}_2,\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}},\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4)}(T,L).$
- 4. For  $i \in [512 \cdot \lambda \cdot (t^2(\lambda) \cdot \ell) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2]$ :
  - 1. Sample a random index *ind* between 1 and the number of oracle queries by  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}$  to  $\mathcal{O}_3$ .
  - 2. Simulate  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_3,\mathcal{O}_4}(G)$  until right before its ind-th oracle query to  $\mathcal{O}_3$  is executed and measure the query input register instead of executing the query. Let  $ivk, y_0, y_1, m$  be the measurement outcome. If  $\mathcal{O}_3(ivk, y_0, y_1, m) \neq \bot$ , add  $(ivk, y_0, y_1, m)$  to  $X_3$  and set  $D_3(m) = \mathcal{O}_3(ivk, y_0, y_1, m)$ .
- 5. Output  $(G, (X_3, D_3))$ .

# $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_4}(V)$

- 1. Parse  $(G, (X_3, D_3)) = V$ .
- 2. Define the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_3'$ : On input  $ivk, y_0, y_1, m$ , output  $D_3(m)$  if  $ivk, y_0, y_1, m \in X_3$ , otherwise output  $\perp$ .
- 3. Simulate  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_3',\mathcal{O}_4}(G)$  to obtain  $\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{internal}}, S$ .

{70}------------------------------------------------

4. Output R<sub>internal</sub>, S.

## <span id="page-70-0"></span>10.2 Defining the Hybrids

In this section, we define the hybrids for our proof, each of which is constructed by modifying the previous one.

Hyb<sub>0</sub>: The original game LR – SIGN – GAME<sub>A</sub>(1<sup> $\lambda$ </sup>) (Definition 24). For ease of reference, we write it out in full, with the notation introduced above.

### $\mathsf{Hyb}_0$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- 2. Parse  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}} = (\mathcal{O}^*_0, \mathcal{O}^*_1, \mathcal{O}^*_2, \mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}^*_3, \mathcal{O}^*_4) = sn^*.$
- 3. Set  $R_{1,internal}^0 = R_{flame}$  and  $S^0 = \bot$ .
- 4. Set  $R_{2,internal}^0 = \bot$ .
- 5. For  $i \in [u(\lambda)]$ :
  - 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$  and a leakage message  $L^i$ .
  - 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$  and a message  $S^i$ .
- 6. The challenger samples a random message  $m^* \leftarrow \mathcal{M}$ .
- 7. The adversary  $\mathcal{A}_{2,\text{final}}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{u(\lambda)}, m^*$ , and it outputs  $sig^*$ .
- 8. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

Hyb<sub>1</sub>: In this hybrid, we simply convert the challenge phase of the experiment into an additional round by using a special choice of adversaries (that is  $A_{1,\ell+1}$ ,  $A_{2,\ell+1}$ ) for this new round.

### $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- $2. \ \operatorname{Parse} \ \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^* = (\mathcal{O}_0^*, \mathcal{O}_1^*, \mathcal{O}_2^*, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*, \mathcal{O}_3^*, \mathcal{O}_4^*) = sn^*.$
- 3. Set  $R_{1,\text{internal}}^0 = R_{\text{flame}}$  and  $S^0 = \bot$ .
- 4. Set  $R_{2,internal}^0 = \bot$ .
- 5. For  $i \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ :

{71}------------------------------------------------

- 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$  and a leakage message  $L^i$ .
- 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$  and a message  $S^i$ .
- 6. Parse  $(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$ .
- 7. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

For the subhybrids  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,c}$  below, each index  $\ell$  corresponds to a round of the leakage protocol between  $\mathcal{A}_1$  and  $\mathcal{A}_2$ .

Hyb<sub>2, $\ell$ ,0</sub> for  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 2]$ : In this hybrid, the first  $\ell - 1$  rounds of the leakage protocol of  $\mathcal{A}_1, \mathcal{A}_2$  are essentially collapsed into (i.e. simulated by) a single message between the two *new* adversaries  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell-1}, \mathcal{B}_{2,\ell-2}$  (where the new receiver adversary  $\mathcal{B}_{2,\ell-2}$  does not make any oracle calls), and then rounds  $\ell$  through  $u(\lambda) + 1$  are executed as before. The very first hybrid  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,1,0}$  will be equivalent to  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1$ . We also label some parts of the experiment for ease of reference later on.

## $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,0}$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- 2. Parse  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}} = (\mathcal{O}^*_0, \mathcal{O}^*_1, \mathcal{O}^*_2, \mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}^*_3, \mathcal{O}^*_4) = sn^*.$

Round-collapsed Simulation for First  $\ell-1$  Rounds:

- 3. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell-1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $(T^{\ell-1},S^{\ell-1})$ .
- 4. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{2,\ell-1}(T^{\ell-1})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}^{\ell-1}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}$ .

### **Original Protocol Continuation:**

- 5. For  $i \in \{\ell, ..., u(\lambda) + 1\}$ :
  - 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$  and a leakage message  $L^i$ .
  - 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$  and a message  $S^i$ .
- 6. Parse  $(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$ .
- 7. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

Hyb<sub>2, $\ell$ ,1 for  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ : In this hybrid, we remove the oracle calls to  $\mathcal{O}_0^*$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_1^*$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_2^*$  from the receiver adversary during round  $\ell$ , by instead simulating it with a new leakage and a new receiver adversary  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell}$ .</sub>

{72}------------------------------------------------

# $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,\underline{1}}$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- 2. Parse  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^* = (\mathcal{O}_0^*, \mathcal{O}_1^*, \mathcal{O}_2^*, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*, \mathcal{O}_3^*, \mathcal{O}_4^*) = sn^*.$

### Round-collapsed Simulation for First $\ell-1$ Rounds:

3. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell-1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $(T^{\ell-1},S^{\ell-1})$ .

### Round $\ell$ :

- 4.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $S^{\ell-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell}$  and a leakage message  $L^{\ell}$
- 5.  $C_{1,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $T^{\ell-1}, L^{\ell}$  and produces a message  $Y^{\ell}$ .
- 6. Run  $C_{2,\ell}^{(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*, \mathcal{O}_3^*, \mathcal{O}_4^*)}(Y^{\ell})$  to obtain  $(\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell}, S^{\ell})$

### **Original Protocol Continuation:**

- 7. For  $i \in \{\ell + 1, \dots, u(\lambda) + 1\}$ :
  - 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs a leakage message  $L^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
  - 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs a message  $S^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
- 8. Parse  $(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$ .
- 9. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

Hyb<sub>2, $\ell$ ,2</sub> for  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ : We further remove the calls to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*$  made by the receiver adversary during this round, instead simulating it with a new leakage and new receiver adversary  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}$ .

# $\frac{\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2}}{\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2}}$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- $2. \ \operatorname{Parse} \ \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^* = (\mathcal{O}_0^*, \mathcal{O}_1^*, \mathcal{O}_2^*, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*, \mathcal{O}_3^*, \mathcal{O}_4^*) = sn^*.$

### Round-collapsed Simulation for First $\ell-1$ Rounds:

3. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell-1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $(T^{\ell-1},S^{\ell-1})$ .

### Round $\ell$ :

4.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $S^{\ell-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell}$  and a leakage message  $L^{\ell}$ 

{73}------------------------------------------------

- 5.  $\mathcal{R}_{1,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $T^{\ell-1}, L^{\ell}$  and produces a message  $G^{\ell}$ .
- 6. Run  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_3^*,\mathcal{O}_4^*}(G^{\ell})$  to obtain  $(\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell},S^{\ell})$

## **Original Protocol Continuation:**

- 7. For  $i \in \{\ell + 1, \dots, u(\lambda) + 1\}$ :
  - 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs a leakage message  $L^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
  - 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs a message  $S^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
- 8. Parse  $(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$ .
- 9. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

Hyb<sub>2, $\ell$ ,3</sub> for  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ : We further remove the calls to  $\mathcal{O}_3^*$  made by the receiver adversary during this round, instead simulating it with a new leakage and new receiver adversary  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}$ .

# $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,3}$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ .
