- 2. Parse  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^* = (\mathcal{O}_0^*, \mathcal{O}_1^*, \mathcal{O}_2^*, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*, \mathcal{O}_3^*, \mathcal{O}_4^*) = sn^*.$

### Round-collapsed Simulation for First $\ell-1$ Rounds:

3. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell-1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $(T^{\ell-1},S^{\ell-1})$ .

### Round $\ell$ :

- 4.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $S^{\ell-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell}$  and a leakage message  $L^{\ell}$
- 5.  $Q_{1,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^{\mathsf{eq}}}$  receives  $T^{\ell-1}, L^{\ell}$  and produces a message  $V^{\ell}$ .
- 6. Run  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_4^*}(V^{\ell})$  to obtain  $(\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell},S^{\ell})$

### **Original Protocol Continuation:**

- 7. For  $i \in \{\ell + 1, \dots, u(\lambda) + 1\}$ :
  - 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs a leakage message  $L^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
  - 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs a message  $S^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .

{74}------------------------------------------------

- 8. Parse  $(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$ .
- 9. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

Hyb<sub>2, $\ell$ ,4</sub> for  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ : We further remove the calls to  $\mathcal{O}_4^*$  made by the receiver adversary during this round, and instead we simulate it with a new leakage.

# $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,4}$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- 2. Parse  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}} = (\mathcal{O}^*_0, \mathcal{O}^*_1, \mathcal{O}^*_2, \mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}, \mathcal{O}^*_3, \mathcal{O}^*_4) = sn^*.$

### Round-collapsed Simulation for First $\ell-1$ Rounds:

3. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell-1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $(T^{\ell-1},S^{\ell-1})$ .

### Round $\ell$ :

- 4.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $S^{\ell-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell}$  and a leakage message  $L^{\ell}$
- 5.  $\mathcal{Q}_{1,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $T^{\ell-1}, L^{\ell}$  and produces a message  $V^{\ell}$ .
- 6. Set  $X_4^{\ell}$  to be the empty set.
- 7. For  $j \in [512^2 \cdot (t(\lambda))^6 \cdot \lambda^8 \cdot (u(\lambda))^4 \cdot (q^*(\lambda))^4 \cdot (\ell)^2]$ :
  - 1. Sample a random index *ind* between 1 and the number of oracle queries made by  $Q_{2,\ell}$ .
  - 2. Simulate  $Q_{2,\ell}^{\mathcal{O}_4^*}(V^{\ell})$  until right before its ind-th oracle query is executed and measure the query input register instead of executing the query. Let m, y be the measurement outcome.
  - 3. Check if  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m,y)$  is 1. If so, add (m,y) to  $X_4^{\ell}$ .
- 8. Simulate  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}(V^{\ell})$  with the following oracle  $\mathcal{O}'$ : On input m, y, output 1 if  $(m, y) \in X$ , otherwise output 0. Let  $(\mathsf{R}^{\ell}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}, S^{\ell})$  be the output.

### **Original Protocol Continuation:**

- 9. For  $i \in \{\ell + 1, \dots, u(\lambda) + 1\}$ :
  - 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs a leakage message  $L^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
  - 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs a message  $S^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .

{75}------------------------------------------------

10. Parse 
$$(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$$
.

11. Output 
$$\mathcal{O}_{4}^{*}(m^{*}, sig^{*})$$
.

Hyb<sub>3</sub>: We define this hybrid to be the same as  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,u(\lambda)+2,0}$ .

## $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Setup}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- $2. \ \operatorname{Parse} \ \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^* = (\mathcal{O}_0^*, \mathcal{O}_1^*, \mathcal{O}_2^*, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*, \mathcal{O}_3^*, \mathcal{O}_4^*) = sn^*.$
- 3. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{1,u(\lambda)+1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell-1}$  and  $(T^{u(\lambda)+1},S^{u(\lambda)+1})$ .
- 4. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{2,u(\lambda)+1}(T^{u(\lambda)+1})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}^{u(\lambda)+1}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}$ .
- 5. Parse  $(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$ .
- 6. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

## <span id="page-75-0"></span>10.3 Hybrid Indistinguishability (Proof of Theorem 19)

In this section, we prove the indistinguishability of the first and the last hybrid. That is, we prove Theorem 19.

First we give the hybrid indistinguishability lemmata.

**Lemma 5.**  $\mathsf{Hyb}_0 \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_1$ .

*Proof.* This is straightforward by the definition of  $A_{1,u(\lambda)+1}$ ,  $A_{2,u(\lambda)+1}$ .

Lemma 6.  $\mathsf{Hyb}_1 \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,1,0}$ .

*Proof.* This is straightforward by the definition of  $\mathcal{B}_{1,0}, \mathcal{B}_{2,0}$ .

<span id="page-75-4"></span>**Lemma 7.** For all  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ ,  $\left| \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,0} - \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,1} \right| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$ .

We prove this lemma in Section 11.

<span id="page-75-1"></span>**Lemma 8.** For all  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ ,  $\left| \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,1} - \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2} \right| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$ .

We prove this lemma in Section 10.3.1.

<span id="page-75-2"></span>**Lemma 9.** For all  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ ,  $\left| \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2} - \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,3} \right| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$ .

We prove this lemma in Section 10.3.2.

<span id="page-75-3"></span>**Lemma 10.** For all  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ ,  $\left| \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,3} - \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,4} \right| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$ .

We prove this lemma in Section 10.3.3.

**Lemma 11.** For all  $\ell \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,4} \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell+1,0}$ .

*Proof.* Observe that, for the internal state,  $\mathcal{B}_{2,\ell+1}$  produces the exact same mixed state as the one produced by  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}$  in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,4}$  since it is conditioning on the same output message.

{76}------------------------------------------------

Lemma 12.  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,u(\lambda)+2,0} \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_3$ .

*Proof.* By definition.  $\Box$ 

Finally, combining these lemmas gives us

$$|\mathsf{Hyb}_0 - \mathsf{Hyb}_3| \le \frac{1}{4 \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$$

which proves Theorem 19.

### <span id="page-76-0"></span>10.3.1 Proof of Lemma 8

In this section, we prove Lemma 8. That is, we prove that for all  $\ell \in [u(\lambda)+1]$ ,  $\left|\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,1} - \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2}\right| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$ . Throughout the rest of the proof, fix any  $\ell \in [u(\lambda)+1]$ .

Note that the difference between the hybrids  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,1}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2}$  is that in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,1}$  we run  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell}$  with the actual oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*$  whereas in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2}$ , we use  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}$  which simulates  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell}$  with an estimated (by  $\mathcal{R}_{\ell,1}$ ) oracle. We will use the incompressibility property of OSS (Definition 21) to show that this only makes a difference of  $\frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$  statistical difference. In this proof whenever we refer to incompressibility we will be referring to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}$  incompressibility of OSS. We make two notes about this hybrid. First, note that this hybrid is only needed for the LOCC leakage-resilience security: it can be removed in case of non-interactive security. Second, this hybrid indistinguishability can be proven directly using strong  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}$  incompressibility of any OSS (the proof would be essentially the same as Section 11.1), but here we use regular incompressibility and the properties of our actual OSS scheme, rather than strong incompressibility.

Let  $\gamma_{vk,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^\ell}$  be the total query weight of  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell}(Y^\ell)$  to  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*$  in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,1}$  on the input vk,z. We also define the following.

$$\alpha_{vk,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^{\ell}} = \left\{ \begin{array}{c} \sigma_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^{\ell}, \text{ if } \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*(vk,z) \neq 0 \\ 0, \text{ if } \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*(vk,z) = 0 \end{array} \right.$$

We also define  $W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^\ell,X_{sign}}$ . Here, let  $X_{sign}$  denote the values sampled during the execution of  $\mathcal{R}_{1,\ell}$ , and let  $L_{sign}$  denote its projection onto its elements' first components (i.e.  $L_{sign} = \{vk : (vk,z) \in X_{sign}\}$ ). Similarly, for any vk, let S(vk) denote  $\mathsf{Span}(\{v : (vk,v) \in X_{sign}\}) \setminus \{0\}$ .

$$W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^\ell,X_{sign}} := \sum_{\substack{vk,z:\z \notin Sign}} \alpha_{vk,z}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^\ell}$$

We now claim the following.

<span id="page-76-1"></span>Claim 1. For all sufficiently large  $\lambda > 0$ ,

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^\ell, X_{sign}}[W^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^\ell, X_{sign}}] \leq \frac{1}{128 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}.$$

Proof. We will prove this using the incompressibility property of OSS: Consider the following adversaries  $\mathcal{P}_1$  and  $\mathcal{P}_2$  for it.  $\mathcal{P}_1$  simulates the hybrid  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,1}$  until  $\mathcal{C}_{1,\ell}$  produces its output  $Y^{\ell}$ , and then outputs  $Y^{\ell}$ . Then,  $\mathcal{P}_2$  receives this value and runs  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell}$  with it. When considering  $\mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2$  for incompressibility of OSS, we assume that  $\mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2$  are only oracle-adversaries for OSS, and the other oracles are just simulated, e.g. they sample  $H_0$  in advance and both use this sample to simulate

{77}------------------------------------------------

the oracle outputs of  $\mathcal{O}_0^*$ . Observe that both  $\mathcal{P}_1$  and  $\mathcal{P}_2$  can perform their simulations with their respective oracles (e.g.  $\mathcal{P}_2$  only queries  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Sign}}^*$ ,  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Ver}}^*$  and does not query  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS}.\mathsf{GenQKey}}^*$ ).

Let  $\mathcal{L}$  be the incompressibility list for the signing oracle as in Definition 21, and we know  $|\mathcal{L}| = s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda) = 32768 \cdot \lambda^5 \cdot (\ell \cdot t(\lambda))^2 \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2$  since  $\mathcal{P}_1$  makes at most  $s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda)/2$  queries to  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS,GenQKey}^*$ . The list depends on the oracle itself and the leakage  $Y^{\ell}$ , but we will not write this dependence explicitly for conciseness.

$$\begin{split} W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^\ell,X_{sign},\mathfrak{L}} := \sum_{\substack{vk,z:\\z\not\in S(vk)\\vk\not\in \mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_{vk,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^\ell} \\ W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^\ell,X_{sign},\mathfrak{L}} := \sum_{\substack{vk,z:\\z\not\in S(vk)\\vk\in \mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_{vk,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^\ell} \end{split}$$

Now we claim

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^\ell, X_{sign}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^\ell, X_{sign}, \mathfrak{L}}] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

To see this, consider the value

$$A = \sum_{\substack{vk,z:\\vk \not\in \mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_{vk,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^{\ell}}$$

Observe that with probability 1, this is greater than or equal to  $W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell}, X_{sign}, \mathfrak{L}}$ . Then, observe that  $\mathbb{E}[A] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  by the incompressibility property of OSS.

Now we claim that for all sufficiently large  $\lambda > 0$ 

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell}, X_{sign}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell}, X_{sign}, \mathfrak{L}}] \leq \frac{1}{256 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}.$$

To prove this, we first define for  $i \in [s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda)]$ ,

$$Q_i^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^\ell, X_{sign}, \mathfrak{L}} := \sum_{\substack{vk, z:\\z \not\in S(vk)\\vk = \mathsf{Item}_i(\mathfrak{L})}} \alpha_{vk, z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^\ell}$$

We claim  $\mathbb{E}[Q_i] \leq \frac{1}{256 \cdot s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}$  for all  $i \in [s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda)]$ . Observe that with probability 1 we have  $W = W_1 + \sum_{i \in [s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda)]} Q_i$ , thus, proving this claim will complete our proof.

Now fix some  $i^* \in [s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda)]$ . Fix any value  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}, Y^\ell$ . We will prove the above for any such fixed values. Note that fixing these also fixes  $\mathfrak{L}$  and thus  $\mathsf{Item}_{i^*}(\mathfrak{L})$  - denote this as  $vk^*$ . There are  $r_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda) = \lambda^8 \cdot \ell^2 \cdot (t(\lambda))^4 \cdot (n(\lambda))^2 \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2 \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2$  iterations during the run of  $\mathcal{R}_{\ell,1}$ , and we will consider these iterations in  $n(\lambda) + 1$  groups: we have  $\frac{r_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda)}{n(\lambda)+1}$  iterations in each group. Now let GOOD denote the event that  $Q_{i^*} \leq \frac{1}{256 \cdot \lambda \cdot s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}$ . We will prove that  $\mathsf{Pr}[\mathsf{GOOD}] \geq 1 - 2 \exp\{-\lambda\}$ . For each  $j \in [n+1]$ , define the event  $E_j$  to be the event that during the j-th group, a new element is added to  $X_{sign}$ , and define  $E'_j$  to be the event  $\sum_{z \notin S_j(vk^*)} \alpha_{vk^*,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^\ell} > \frac{1}{256 \cdot \lambda \cdot s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}$  where  $S_j$  denotes  $\mathsf{Span}(\{v: (vk,v) \in \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^\ell) > \frac{1}{256 \cdot \lambda \cdot s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}$  where  $S_j$  denotes  $\mathsf{Span}(\{v: (vk,v) \in \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^\ell) > \frac{1}{256 \cdot \lambda \cdot s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}$ 

{78}------------------------------------------------

 $X_{sign}\}$ ) \ {0} for the value of  $X_{sign}$  at the beginning of the j-th group. It is easy to see that  $\left(\bigvee_{j=1}^{n+1}\overline{E_j'}\right) \Longrightarrow \mathsf{GOOD}$ . Similarly, it is easy to see that  $E_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge E_n \Longrightarrow \overline{E_{n+1}'}$ , since the subspace  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_{vk^*})^{\perp}$  is of dimension at most n, so, once n linearly independent elements are added, there cannot be any vectors outside  $\mathsf{Colspan}(A_{vk^*})^{\perp}$ . Note that combining these two, we also get  $E_1 \wedge \cdots \wedge E_n \Longrightarrow \mathsf{GOOD}$ . Finally, we claim that  $\Pr\left[E_j|E_j' \wedge E\right] \geq 1 - \exp\{-\lambda \cdot 2n\}$  for all  $j \in [n]$  and any event E such that  $\Pr[E] > 0$ . For now, we will assume this and complete the proof, and later we will prove it. First, observe that  $\Pr\left[\bigwedge_{j=1}^n E_j|\bigwedge_{j=1}^n E_j'\right] \geq (1 - \exp\{-\lambda \cdot 2n\})^n \geq 1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$  by above. This also means  $\Pr\left[\mathsf{GOOD}|\bigwedge_{j=1}^n E_j'\right] \geq 1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$ . Also recall that  $\overline{\bigwedge_{j=1}^n E_j'} \Longrightarrow \mathsf{GOOD}$ . Combining these two gives us  $\Pr[\mathsf{GOOD}] \geq 1 - 2\exp\{-\lambda\}$ .

Finally, we prove  $\Pr\left[E_j|E_j'\wedge E\right] \geq 1 - \exp\{-\lambda\cdot 2n\}$  for all  $j\in[n]$  and any event E such that  $\Pr[E]>0$ . To see this, observe that during the j-th group, we measure the query of the adversary for  $\frac{r_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda)}{n(\lambda)+1}$  times. Since the weight on  $good\ elements$  (i.e. elements that would be added to our list and thus cause  $E_j$  to occur) is at least  $\frac{1}{256\cdot\lambda\cdot s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda)\cdot t(\lambda)\cdot (\lambda\cdot u(\lambda)\cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}$  when conditioned on  $E_j'$ , we get the desired result since  $r_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda) \geq 1024\cdot (n^2(\lambda)\cdot t(\lambda))\cdot \lambda^2\cdot s_{OSS,\ell}(\lambda)\cdot t(\lambda)\cdot (\lambda\cdot u(\lambda)\cdot q^*(\lambda))^2$ .  $\square$ 

Now we claim that the lemma follows from Claim 1. To see this, observe that the two hybrids only differ on the oracles they use for  $\mathcal{C}_{\ell,2}$ :  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,1}$  uses  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}$  whereas  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2}$  uses the estimated oracle created by  $\mathcal{R}_{\ell,1}$ . Observe that these oracles can differ only on inputs vk, z such that  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}(vk, z) \neq 0$  (i.e.  $z \in \mathsf{Colspan}(A_{vk})^{\perp} \setminus \{0\}$ ) but  $z \notin S(vk)$ . Now observe that  $W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}, Y^{\ell}, X_{sign}}$  is an upper bound on the total weight on the inputs on which the oracles might differ. Thus, the lemma follows by the Jensen's inequality, the fact that  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell}$  makes at most  $t(\lambda)$  queries to  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}$  and Theorem 6.

### <span id="page-78-0"></span>10.3.2 Proof of Lemma 9

In this section, we prove Lemma 9. That is, we prove that for all  $\ell \in [u(\lambda)+1]$ ,  $\left|\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2} - \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,3}\right| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$ . Throughout the rest of the proof, fix any  $\ell \in [u(\lambda)+1]$ .

Observe that the difference between the two hybrids is that in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2}$  we run  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}$  directly, whereas in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,3}$  we instead run  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}$  which simulates  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}$  while using an estimated oracle for its queries to  $\mathcal{O}_3^*$ . We will use the incompressibility property of  $H_0, H_1$  to show that this only makes a difference of  $\frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$  in statistical distance.

Let  $\gamma_{ivk,y_0,y_1,z}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},G^{\ell}}$  denote the total query weight of  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}(G^{\ell})$  to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_2^*$  on input  $ivk,y_0,y_1,z$ . We also define the following.

$$\alpha_{ivk,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,G^\ell} = \sum_{y_0,y_1:\mathcal{O}_2^*(ivk,y_0,y_1,z) \neq \bot} \gamma_{ivk,y_0,y_1,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,G^\ell}$$

<span id="page-78-1"></span>Now let  $(X_{0,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell'\in[\ell],j'\in[t(\lambda)]}$ ,  $(X_{1,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell'\in[\ell],j'\in[t(\lambda)]}$ ,  $(D_{0,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell'\in[\ell^*],j'\in[i^*]}$ ,  $(D_{1,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell'\in[\ell^*],j'\in[i^*]}$  be the estimated lists and databases in  $V^{\ell}$  (or equivalently,  $G^{\ell}$ ) when it is fully unwrapped and parsed. Let  $X_3, D_3$  be the estimated list and database inside  $V^{\ell}$  that is sampled by  $\mathcal{Q}_{1,\ell}$ . With abuse of notation, sometimes we will refer to the projection of the sets  $X_{\cdot,j'}^{\ell'}$  onto their elements' (which are tuples) subcomponents also as  $X_{\cdot,j'}^{\ell'}$  (e.g. we will write  $X_{2,j'}^{\ell'}$  to mean the set of pairs (ivk,z) obtained by projecting each tuple in the actual set  $X_{2,j'}^{\ell'}$  to its first and fourth elements) - however, the meaning will clear from context. Now we claim the following.

{79}------------------------------------------------

### Claim 2.

$$\Pr\left[\left(\bigcup_{\ell'\in[\ell],j'\in[t(\lambda)]}X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right)\bigcap\left(\bigcup_{\ell'\in[\ell],j'\in[t(\lambda)]}X_{1,j'}^{\ell'}\right)=\emptyset\right]\geq 1-\mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Proof. Observe that if this intersection is not empty, then there is ivk such that  $ivk \in X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}$  and  $ivk \in X_{1,j''}^{\ell''}$  for some  $\ell', \ell'', j', j''$ . However, by construction we know that this implies that we can obtain  $isig_0, isig_1$  from  $V^{\ell}$  such that  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}^*}(ivk, 0, isig_0) = \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}^*}(ivk, 1, isig_1) = 1$ . Since  $V^{\ell}$  is obtained by making polynomially many queries to the oracles of OSS, the claim follows by the one-shot security of OSS.

Now we define the following (some dependencies are implicit to keep the notation concise).

$$\begin{split} W_0^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,G^\ell,X_3} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk,z:\\ ivk \not\in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell],j' \in [t(\lambda)]} X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk,z) \not\in X_3}} \alpha_{ivk,z} \\ W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,G^\ell,X_3} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk,z:\\ ivk \not\in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell],j' \in [t(\lambda)]} X_{1,j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk,z) \not\in X_3}} \alpha_{ivk,z} \\ W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,G^\ell,X_3} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk,z:\\ ivk \not\in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell],j' \in [t(\lambda)]} X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right) \cap \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell],j' \in [t(\lambda)]} X_{1,j'}^{\ell'}\right)}} \alpha_{ivk,z} \end{split}$$

Now we make the following claims.

### Claim 3.

$$\mathbb{E}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, G^{\ell}, X_3}] \le \mathsf{negl}(\lambda). \tag{1}$$

*Proof.* This simply follows from the definition of  $W_2$  and Claim 2.

Claim 4. For all sufficiently large  $\lambda > 0$ .

$$\begin{split} \mathbb{E}[W_0^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,G^\ell,X_3}] &\leq \frac{1}{128 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2} \\ \mathbb{E}[W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,G^\ell,X_3}] &\leq \frac{1}{128 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2} \end{split}$$

*Proof.* We will only prove the first one (using incompressibility of the random oracle  $H_0$ ), and the second bound follows by the same argument (but this time relying on the incompressibility of  $H_1$ ).

Now we will use the incompressibility property (Theorem 15) of the random oracle  $H_0$  with the predicate P defined as P(ivk||z) = 1 if  $ivk \in S$ , where  $S = \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell], j' \in [t(\lambda)]} X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right)$ . Note that this set S is exactly the set of prefixes on which our adversary has section queries (otherwise it only makes normal queries and verification queries). In more detail, let  $\mathcal{P}_1$  be the adversary that simulates  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2}$  until the point where  $\mathcal{R}_{1,\ell}$  outputs its message, and it also outputs S as its predicate. Then  $\mathcal{P}_2$  simulates  $\mathcal{R}_{2,\ell}$ . We invoke Theorem 15 for this pair of adversaries, and let  $\mathfrak{L}$ 

{80}------------------------------------------------

denote the incompressibility list that is promised to exist, and we know  $|\mathfrak{L}| = \ell \cdot t(\lambda)$  since  $\mathcal{P}_1$  makes at most  $\ell \cdot t(\lambda)$  normal queries. We then split  $W_0$  into two summands  $U_0, U_1$ :

$$\begin{split} U_0^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,G^\ell,X_3} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk,z:\\ ivk \not\in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell],j' \in [t(\lambda)]} X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk,z) \not\in \mathfrak{L}\\ }} \alpha_{ivk,isig} \\ U_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,G^\ell,X_3} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk,z:\\ ivk,z:\\ ivk \not\in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell],j' \in [t(\lambda)]} X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk,z) \not\in X_3\\ (ivk,z) \in \mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_{ivk,isig} \end{split}$$

By the incompressibility lemma, we get  $\mathbb{E}[U_0] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ . Now, we will focus on bounding  $U_1$ . First we claim that, for all  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}, G^{\ell}$ , with overwhelming probability we have that any ivk, z that satisfies

$$\alpha_{ivk,z} \ge \frac{1}{512 \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot \ell) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

is contained in  $X_3$ . To see this, observe that  $X_3$  is created by measuring a random query of  $\mathcal{R}_{\ell,2}$  to  $\mathcal{O}_3$  for  $512 \cdot \lambda \cdot (t^2(\lambda) \cdot \ell) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2$  times. Thus, for any ivk, z such that  $\alpha_{ivk,z}$  satisfies the above condition, the probability that  $(ivk, z) \notin X_3$  is at most  $\exp\{-\lambda\}$ . Now define GOOD to be the event that all  $(ivk, z) \in \mathfrak{L}$  that satisfies

$$\alpha_{ivk,z} \ge \frac{1}{512 \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot \ell) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

are included in  $X_3$ . Since this is true with probability  $1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$  for each  $ivk, z \in \mathfrak{L}$  individually, and since  $|\mathfrak{L}|$  is polynomial, we have that  $\Pr[\mathsf{GOOD}] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Now we claim

$$\mathbb{E}[U_1 \big| \mathsf{GOOD}] \le \frac{1}{512 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

To see this, first by linearity of expectation we have

$$\mathbb{E}[U_1 | \mathsf{GOOD}]$$

$$= \sum_{\substack{ivk,z:\\ ivk \notin \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell], j' \in [t(\lambda)]} X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk,z) \notin X_3\\ (ivk,z) \in \Omega}} \mathbb{E}[\alpha_{ivk,z} | \mathsf{GOOD}]$$

However, by definition of GOOD, when GOOD occurs, we have

$$ivk, z \in \mathcal{L} \setminus X_3 \implies \alpha_{ivk,z} \le \frac{1}{512 \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot \ell) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

Since  $|\mathfrak{L}| = \ell \cdot t(\lambda)$ , we obtain the desired upper bound on expectation conditioned on GOOD. Since  $\Pr[\mathsf{GOOD}] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , we also get

$$\mathbb{E}[U_1] \le \frac{1}{256 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

as desired.  $\Box$ 

{81}------------------------------------------------

Observe that Lemma 16 follows from the above claims. To see this, observe that  $W_0 + W_1 + W_2$  is an upper bound on the total weight on which the two different oracles in the hybrids might differ. Thus the result follows by the linearity of expectation, Theorem 6 and Jensen's inequality.

### <span id="page-81-0"></span>10.3.3 Proof of Lemma 10

In this section, we prove Lemma 10. That is, we prove that for all  $\ell \in [u(\lambda)+1]$ ,  $\left|\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,3} - \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,4}\right| \le \frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$ . Throughout the rest of the proof, fix any  $\ell \in [u(\lambda)+1]$ .

First, note that the difference between the hybrids  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,3}$ ,  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,4}$  is that in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,3}$  we run  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}$  with the actual oracle  $\mathcal{O}_4^*$  whereas in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,4}$  we use the simulated oracle  $\mathcal{O}'$ . We will use the incompressibility property of the random oracle  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$  (Theorem 15) to show that this only makes a difference of  $\frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$  statistical difference. In this proof whenever we refer to incompressibility we will be referring to that of  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$ .

For the incompressibility property, consider the following adversaries  $\mathcal{P}_1$  and  $\mathcal{P}_2$ .  $\mathcal{P}_1$  simulates the hybrid  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,3}$  until  $\mathcal{Q}_{1,\ell}$  produces its output  $V^{\ell}$ , and then outputs  $V^{\ell}$ . Then,  $\mathcal{P}_2$  receives this value and runs  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}$  with it. When considering  $\mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2$  for incompressibility of  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$ , we assume that  $\mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2$  are only oracle-adversaries for  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$  and the verifier (as in Theorem 15) of  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$  respectively, and the other oracles are just simulated, e.g. they sample  $H_0$  in advance and both use this sample to simulate the oracle calls to  $\mathcal{O}_0^*$ . Observe that both  $\mathcal{P}_1$  and  $\mathcal{P}_2$  can perform their simulations with their respective oracles, e.g.,  $\mathcal{O}_4^*$  is simply the verification oracle of  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$  and  $\mathcal{P}_2$  does not query  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$ .

Let  $\mathcal{L}$  be the incompressibility list as in Theorem 15, and we know  $|\mathcal{L}| = s_{4,\ell}(\lambda) = 512 \cdot \lambda \cdot (t^2(\lambda) \cdot \ell^2(\lambda)) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2$  since that many queries to  $H_{\text{sig}}$  are made by  $\mathcal{P}_1$ . The list depends on the oracle itself and the *leakage*  $V^{\ell}$ , but we will not write this dependence explicitly for conciseness.

Let  $\gamma_{m,y}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^{\ell}}$  be the total query weight of  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}(V^{\ell})$  to  $\mathcal{O}_4^*$  in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell,2}$  on the input m,y. Define  $\alpha_m$  as

$$\alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell} = \sum_{y:\mathcal{O}_4^*(m,y)=1} \gamma_{m,y}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell}.$$

Now define  $W^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell,X_4^\ell},W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell,X_4^\ell,\mathfrak{L}},W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell,X_4^\ell,\mathfrak{L}}$  as

$$W^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell,X_4^\ell} := \sum_{\substack{m:\\ m \not\in X_4^\ell}} \alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell} \\ W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell,X_4^\ell,\mathfrak{L}} := \sum_{\substack{\alpha \\ m \not\in X_4^\ell}} \alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell}$$

$$W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell, \mathfrak{L}} := \sum_{\substack{m:\\ m \not \in X_4^\ell\\ m \not \in \mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell}$$

$$W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell,X_4^\ell,\mathfrak{L}} := \sum_{\substack{m:\\ m\not\in X_4^\ell\\ m\in\mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell}$$

In the definition above, and in the rest of the proof, by abuse of notation, we write  $m \in X_4^{\ell}$  to denote that there exists a pair  $(m, y) \in X_4^{\ell}$  for some y.

We claim the following.

<span id="page-81-1"></span>Claim 5. For all sufficiently large  $\lambda > 0$ ,

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell, \mathfrak{L}}[W^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell}] \leq \frac{1}{128 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}.$$

{82}------------------------------------------------

Observe that once we prove this, the lemma follows by Theorem 6 and by the Jensen's inequality since the oracles  $\mathcal{O}_4^*$  and  $\mathcal{O}'$  in these hybrids can possibly differ only on inputs (m, y) such that  $(m, y) \notin X_4^\ell$  and  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m, y) = 1$ , and  $W^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell}$  is an upper bound on the total weight on such inputs and  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}$  makes at most  $t(\lambda)$  queries to the oracle  $\mathcal{O}_4^*$ .

To prove Claim 5, we make the following two other claims.

### <span id="page-82-0"></span>Claim 6.

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKevFireSign}}^*, V^{\ell}, X_{4}^{\ell}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_{1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^{\ell}, X_{4}^{\ell}, \mathfrak{L}}] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* Consider the value.

$$A = \sum_{\substack{m:\\ m \not\in \mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell}$$

Observe that this value is always greater than or equal to  $W_1^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},V^\ell,X_4^\ell,\mathfrak{L}}$ . Also observe that  $\mathbb{E}[A] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  by the incompressibility of  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$ .

<span id="page-82-1"></span>Claim 7. For all sufficiently large  $\lambda > 0$ :

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell, \mathfrak{L}}] \leq \frac{1}{256 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}.$$

*Proof.* First we claim that, for all  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}, V^{\ell}$ , with overwhelming probability we have that any  $m \in \mathcal{M}$  that satisfies

$$\alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell} \geq \frac{1}{512 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2 \cdot s_{4,\ell}(\lambda)}$$

is contained in  $X_4^\ell$ . To see this, observe that  $X_4^\ell$  is obtained by measuring a random query of  $\mathcal{Q}_{2,\ell}(V^\ell)$  to  $\mathcal{O}_4^*$  for  $r_{4,\ell}(\lambda) = 512^2 \cdot (t(\lambda))^6 \cdot \lambda^8 \cdot (u(\lambda))^4 \cdot (q^*(\lambda))^4 \cdot (\ell)^2$  times and adding to the set if the pair m,y obtained from the measurement is valid (i.e.  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m,y)=1$ ). Thus, for any  $m \in \mathcal{M}$  that satisfies the above condition, the probability that  $m \not\in X_4^\ell$  is at most  $\exp\left\{-r_{4,\ell}(\lambda) \cdot \frac{\alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,V^\ell}{t(\lambda)}\right\}$ . Since we have

$$1 - \exp\left\{r_{4,\ell}(\lambda) \cdot \frac{1}{t(\lambda) \cdot 512 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2 \cdot s_{4,\ell}(\lambda)}\right\} = 1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$$

this claim follows.

Now define GOOD to be the event that all  $m \in \mathfrak{L}$  that satisfies

$$\alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^{\ell}} \ge \frac{1}{512 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2 \cdot s_{4,\ell}(\lambda)}$$

are included in  $X_4^{\ell}$ . Since this is true with probability  $1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$  for each  $m \in \mathfrak{L}$  and since  $\mathfrak{L}$  is of polynomial size, we have that  $\Pr[\mathsf{GOOD}] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Now we claim

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell, \mathfrak{L}}\big|\mathsf{GOOD}] \leq \frac{1}{512 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}.$$

{83}------------------------------------------------

To see this, first by linearity of expectation we have

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^{\ell}, X_4^{\ell}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^{\ell}, X_4^{\ell}, \mathfrak{L}}|\mathsf{GOOD}] = \sum_{\substack{m:\\ m \not \in X_4^{\ell}\\ m \in \mathfrak{L}}} \mathbb{E}[\alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^{\ell}}|\mathsf{GOOD}].$$

However, by definition of GOOD, when GOOD occurs, we have

$$m \in \mathfrak{L} \setminus X_4^{\ell} \implies \alpha_m^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},V^{\ell}} \leq \frac{1}{512 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2 \cdot s_{4,\ell}(\lambda)}$$

Since  $|\mathfrak{L}| = s_{4,\ell}(\lambda)$ , we obtain the desired upper bound on  $\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^{\ell}, X_4^{\ell}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^{\ell}, X_4^{\ell}, \mathfrak{L}}]$  GOOD]. Since  $\Pr[\mathsf{GOOD}] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , we get

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, V^\ell, X_4^\ell, \mathfrak{L}}] \leq \frac{1}{256 \cdot t(\lambda) \cdot (\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda))^2}.$$

Now observe that Claim 5 follows immediately from Claim 6 and Claim 7 since  $W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},V^\ell,X_4^\ell} = W_1^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},V^\ell,X_4^\ell,\mathfrak{L}} + W_2^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},V^\ell,X_4^\ell,\mathfrak{L}}$  for all  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},V^\ell,X_4^\ell,\mathfrak{L}$  (i.e. with probability 1). This completes the proof of Claim 5, and then the lemma follows as discussed above.

# <span id="page-83-0"></span>10.4 Proof of Theorem 20

In this section, we prove security in the last hybrid. That is, we prove Theorem 20, which says  $\Pr[\mathsf{Hyb}_3 = 1] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

First we prove the following lemma.

<span id="page-83-1"></span>**Theorem 21.** Let  $H: \{0,1\}^{v(\lambda)} \to \{0,1\}^{\lambda}$  be modeled as a quantum random oracle, and let  $v(\lambda)$  be a superlogarithmic function.

For any adversaries  $(A_1, A_2)$ , consider the following experiment.

# $\mathsf{Exp}_{\mathcal{A}_1,\mathcal{A}_2}(\lambda)$

- 1. Sample a random function  $H: \{0,1\}^{v(\lambda)} \to \{0,1\}^{\lambda}$ .
- 2.  $A_1$  is given quantum oracle access to H and outputs a message register R.
- 3. Sample  $m^* \leftarrow \{0,1\}^{v(\lambda)}$ .
- 4.  $A_2$  does not have access to H, and it receives  $(R, m^*)$  and outputs  $y^*$ .
- 5. Output 1 if  $y^* = H(m^*)$ , and 0 otherwise.

Then, for any query-bounded  $A_1$ ,

$$\Pr[\mathsf{Exp}_{\mathcal{A}_1,\mathcal{A}_2}(\lambda) = 1] \le \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* Since  $m^*$  is unpredictable to  $A_1$ , the result follows by Theorem 7.

{84}------------------------------------------------

Observe that in  $\mathsf{Hyb}_3$ , to win the game, the adversary needs to output a value  $sig^*$  such that  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}(m^*) = sig^*$ . Also observe that in this hybrid, the receiver adversary  $\mathcal{B}_{2,u(\lambda)+1}$  does not have access to any oracles, and the sender adversary  $\mathcal{B}_{1,u(\lambda)+1}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}}$  makes polynomially many queries to the random oracle  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$  and to  $\mathcal{O}_4^*$  (which can be simulated by querying  $H_{\mathsf{sig}}$ ). Thus the result follows by Theorem 21.

{85}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-85-0"></span>11 Proof of Lemma 7

In this section, we prove Lemma 7. Throughout this section, fix any  $\ell^* \in [u(\lambda) + 1]$ . Therefore, we will prove  $|\mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell^*,0} - \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell^*,1}| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda)}$ . The proof will be done through a sequence of hybrids, each of which is constructed by modifying the previous one. We will denote our hybrids as  $\mathsf{Hyb}'_i$  (hybrid prime), and their indices will be independent of the indices of the hybrids  $\mathsf{Hyb}_j$  from Section 10.

We first define our hybrids.

# $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{j,0}$ for $j \in [t(\lambda)]$ :

# $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{j,0}$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Spark}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- 2. Parse  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKevFireSign}}^* = (\mathcal{O}_0^*, \mathcal{O}_1^*, \mathcal{O}_2^*, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*, \mathcal{O}_3^*, \mathcal{O}_4^*) = sn^*.$

### Round-collapsed Simulation for First $\ell^* - 1$ Rounds:

3. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell^*-1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*-1}$  and  $(T^{\ell^*-1},S^{\ell^*-1})$ .

## Round $\ell^*$ :

- 4.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,\ell^*}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*-1}$  and  $S^{\ell^*-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*}$  and a leakage message  $L^{\ell^*}$
- 5.  $C_{1,\ell^*,j,0}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $T^{\ell^*-1}, L^{\ell^*}$  and produces a message  $Y^{\ell^*,j,0}$ .
- 6. Run  $C_{2,\ell^*,j,0}^{(\mathcal{O}_{OSS,Sign}^*,\mathcal{O}_3^*,\mathcal{O}_4^*)}(Y^{\ell^*,j,0})$  to obtain  $(\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*},S^{\ell^*})$

### Original Protocol Continuation:

- 7. For  $i \in \{\ell^* + 1, \dots, u(\lambda) + 1\}$ :
  - 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs a leakage message  $L^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
  - 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs a message  $S^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
- 8. Parse  $(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$ .
- 9. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

# $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{j,1} \ \mathbf{for} \ j \in [t(\lambda)]$ :

# $\underline{\mathsf{Hyb}'_{j,1}}$

1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Spark}(1^{\lambda})$ .

{86}------------------------------------------------

2. Parse  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^* = (\mathcal{O}_0^*, \mathcal{O}_1^*, \mathcal{O}_2^*, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*, \mathcal{O}_3^*, \mathcal{O}_4^*) = sn^*.$ 

### Round-collapsed Simulation for First $\ell^* - 1$ Rounds:

3. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell^*-1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*-1}$  and  $(T^{\ell^*-1},S^{\ell^*-1})$ .

### Round $\ell^*$ :

- 4.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,\ell^*}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*-1}$  and  $S^{\ell^*-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*}$  and a leakage message  $L^{\ell^*}$
- 5.  $C_{1,\ell^*,j,1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $T^{\ell^*-1}, L^{\ell^*}$  and produces a message  $Y^{\ell^*,j,1}$ .
- 6. Run  $C_{2,\ell^*,j,1}^{(\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign}^*,\mathcal{O}_3^*,\mathcal{O}_4^*)}(Y^{\ell^*,j,1})$  to obtain  $(\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*},S^{\ell^*})$

### **Original Protocol Continuation:**

- 7. For  $i \in \{\ell^* + 1, \dots, u(\lambda) + 1\}$ :
  - 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs a leakage message  $L^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
  - 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs a message  $S^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
- 8. Parse  $(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$ .
- 9. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

# $\mathsf{Hyb}_{j,2}' \ \mathbf{for} \ i \in \{0,\dots,t(\lambda)\}:$

# $\operatorname{\mathsf{Hyb}}'_{j,2}$

- 1. The challenger samples  $sn^*$ ,  $R_{\mathsf{flame}} \leftarrow \mathsf{QKeyFireSign.Spark}(1^{\lambda})$ .
- 2. Parse  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^* = (\mathcal{O}_0^*, \mathcal{O}_1^*, \mathcal{O}_2^*, \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*, \mathcal{O}_3^*, \mathcal{O}_4^*) = sn^*.$

# Round-collapsed Simulation for First $\ell^* - 1$ Rounds:

3. Run  $\mathcal{B}_{1,\ell^*-1}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}(\mathsf{R}_{\mathsf{flame}})$  to get  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*-1}$  and  $(T^{\ell^*-1},S^{\ell^*-1})$ .

### Round $\ell^*$ :

- 4.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,\ell^*}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*-1}$  and  $S^{\ell^*-1}$ , and it outputs an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*}$  and a leakage message  $L^{\ell^*}$
- 5.  $C_{1,\ell^*,j,2}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $T^{\ell^*-1}, L^{\ell^*}$  and produces a message  $Y^{\ell^*,j,2}$ .
- 6. Run  $C_{2,\ell^*,j,2}^{(\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Sign}}^*,\mathcal{O}_3^*,\mathcal{O}_4^*)}(Y^{\ell^*,j,2})$  to obtain  $(\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{\ell^*},S^{\ell^*})$

{87}------------------------------------------------

### **Original Protocol Continuation:**

- 7. For  $i \in \{\ell^* + 1, \dots, u(\lambda) + 1\}$ :
  - 1.  $\mathcal{A}_{1,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $S^{i-1}$ , and it outputs a leakage message  $L^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{1,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
  - 2.  $\mathcal{A}_{2,i}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*}$  receives  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^{i-1}$  and  $L^i$ , and it outputs a message  $S^i$  and an internal state register  $\mathsf{R}_{2,\mathsf{internal}}^i$ .
- 8. Parse  $(m^*, sig^*) = S^{u(\lambda)+1}$ .
- 9. Output  $\mathcal{O}_4^*(m^*, sig^*)$ .

Lemma 13.  $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{0,2} \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell^*,0}$ 

*Proof.* This follows by the definition of the adversaries  $\mathcal{C}_{1,\ell,0,2},\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell,0,2}$ .

Lemma 14.  $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{t(\lambda),2} \equiv \mathsf{Hyb}_{2,\ell^*,1}$ .

*Proof.* Follows by the definition of the adversary  $C_{1,\ell}$ ,  $C_{2,\ell}$  which are defined to be  $C_{1,\ell,t(\lambda),2}$ ,  $C_{2,\ell,t(\lambda),2}$ .

<span id="page-87-1"></span>**Lemma 15.** For  $i \in [t(\lambda)]$ ,  $\left|\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i-1,2} - \mathsf{Hyb}'_{i,0}\right| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda^2 \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda)} \ and \left|\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i,0} - \mathsf{Hyb}'_{i,1}\right| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda^2 \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda)}$ .

We prove this lemma in Section 11.1.

<span id="page-87-2"></span>**Lemma 16.** For  $i \in [t(\lambda)]$ ,  $\left| \mathsf{Hyb}'_{i,1} - \mathsf{Hyb}'_{i,2} \right| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda^2 \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda)}$ 

We prove this lemma in Section 11.2.

Finally, Lemma 7 follows by simply combining these lemmata.

### <span id="page-87-0"></span>11.1 Proof of Lemma 15

In this section, we prove Lemma 15. We will only explicitly prove the first part, and the second part follows similarly.

Fix any  $i^* \in \{1, \ldots, t(\lambda)\}$ . Thus, we will prove  $|\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*-1,2} - \mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*,0}| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda^2 \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda)}$ . Observe that the difference between the two hybrids is that in  $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*-1,2}$  we run  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell^*,i^*-1,2}$  directly, whereas in  $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*,0}$  we instead run  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell^*,i^*,0}$  which simulates  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell^*,i^*-1,2}$  while using an estimated oracle for its first query to  $\mathcal{O}_0^*$ . We will use the strong incompressibility property of OSS to show that this only makes a difference of  $\frac{1}{\lambda^2 \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda)}$  in statistical distance. In this proof, whenever we refer to incompressibility, we will be referring to the strong incompressibility of OSS. For the strong incompressibility property of OSS, consider the following adversaries  $\mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2$ .  $\mathcal{P}_1$  simulates  $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*-1,2}$  until  $Y^{\ell^*,i^*,1}$  is produced, and outputs  $Y^{\ell^*,i^*,1}$ . Then,  $\mathcal{P}_2$  receives this value and runs  $\mathcal{C}_{\ell^*,2,i^*-1,2}$  with it until right after first query to  $\mathcal{O}_0^*$ . When considering  $\mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2$  for incompressibility of OSS, we assume that  $\mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2$  are only oracle-adversaries for OSS, and the other oracles are just simulated, e.g. they sample  $H_0, H_1, H_{\mathsf{sig}}$  in advance and both use this sample to simulate the oracle calls to relevant oracles.

Now let  $\mathfrak{L}$  denote the strong incompressibility list for these adversaries, and we know  $|\mathfrak{L}| = s_{OSS,\ell^*}(\lambda) = 2048 \cdot \lambda \cdot (t^2(\lambda) \cdot \ell^*) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2 \cdot (\ell^* - 1) + 2 \cdot i^*$  since  $\mathcal{P}_1$  makes at most

{88}------------------------------------------------

 $\frac{s_{OSS,\ell^*}(\lambda)}{2}$  calls to  $\mathcal{O}_{OSS,GenQKey}^*$ . The list depends on the oracle itself and the leakage  $Y^{\ell^*,i^*,1}$ , but we will not write this dependence explicitly for conciseness.

Let  $\gamma_{ivk,isig,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}}$  denote the query amplitude of  $\mathcal{C}_{\ell^*,2,i^*-1,2}(Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2})$  on input ivk,isig,z during its first query to  $\mathcal{O}_0^*$ . We also define the following. Here,  $X_{0,i^*}^{\ell^*}$  is the list sampled during execution of  $\mathcal{C}_{1,\ell^*,i^*,0}$ .

$$\begin{split} \alpha_{ivk,isig}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}} &= \begin{cases} &|\gamma_{ivk,isig}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}}|^2, \text{ if } \mathcal{O}^*_{\text{OSS.Ver}}(ivk,0,isig) = 1\\ 0, \text{ if } \mathcal{O}^*_{\text{OSS.Ver}}(ivk,0,isig) = 0 \end{cases} \\ W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2},X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk,isig:\\ (ivk,isig) \notin X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}}} \alpha_{ivk,isig}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}} \\ W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2},X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*},\mathfrak{L}} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk,isig:\\ (ivk,isig) \notin X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}\\ (ivk,isig) \notin \mathcal{L}^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}}} \alpha_{ivk,isig}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}} \\ W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2},X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*},\mathfrak{L}} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk,isig:\\ (ivk,isig) \notin \mathcal{L}^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}\\ (ivk,isig) \notin \mathcal{L}^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}}} \alpha_{ivk,isig}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}} \\ W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2},X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*},\mathfrak{L}} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk,isig:\\ (ivk,isig) \notin \mathcal{L}^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}\\ (ivk,isig) \notin \mathcal{L}^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}}} \alpha_{ivk,isig}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\text{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}} \end{aligned}$$

Now we make the following claims.

### Claim 8.

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

*Proof.* Observe that with probability 1, we have

$$W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}} \leq \sum_{\substack{ivk, isig:\\ (ivk, isig) \not\in \mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_{ivk, isig}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}}$$

However, expectation of the value on the right is negligible by incompressibility of OSS (with the adversaries  $\mathcal{P}_1, \mathcal{P}_2$ ).

Claim 9. For all sufficiently large  $\lambda > 0$ .

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}] \leq \frac{1}{256 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

*Proof.* First we claim that, for all  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}$ ,  $Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}$ , with overwhelming probability all ivk, isig that satisfies

$$\alpha_{ivk,isig}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}} \geq \frac{1}{512 \cdot s_{OSS,\ell^*}(\lambda) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

is contained in  $X_{0,i^*}^{\ell^*}$ . To see this, observe that  $X_{0,i^*}^{\ell^*}$  is created by measuring the first query of  $\mathcal{C}_{\ell^*,2,i^*-1,2}$  to  $\mathcal{O}_0$  for  $r_{OSS,\ell^*}(\lambda) = 4194304 \cdot \lambda^{10} \cdot t^2(\lambda) \cdot (\ell^*)^5 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^4$  times. Thus, for

{89}------------------------------------------------

any ivk, isig, the probability that  $(ivk, isig) \notin X_{0,i^*}^{\ell^*}$  is at most  $\exp\{-r_{OSS,\ell^*}(\lambda) \cdot \alpha_{ivk,isig}\}$ . Since we have

$$1 - \exp\{-r_{OSS,\ell^*}(\lambda) \cdot \frac{1}{512 \cdot s_{OSS,\ell^*}(\lambda) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}\} = 1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$$

the claim follows. Now define GOOD to be the event that all  $(ivk, isig) \in \mathfrak{L}$  that satisfies

$$\alpha_{ivk,isig}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2}} \geq \frac{1}{512 \cdot s_{OSS,\ell^*}(\lambda) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

are included in  $X_{0,i^*}^{\ell^*}$ . Since this is true with probability  $1 - \exp\{-\lambda\}$  for each  $ivk, isig \in \mathfrak{L}$  individually, and since  $|\mathfrak{L}|$  is polynomial, we have that  $\Pr[\mathsf{GOOD}] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Now we claim

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}\big| \mathsf{GOOD}] \leq \frac{1}{512 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

To see this, first by linearity of expectation we have

$$\begin{split} &\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}\big| \mathsf{GOOD}] \\ &= \sum_{\substack{ivk, isig:\\ (ivk, isig) \not\in X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}\\ (ivk. isig) \in \mathfrak{L}}} \mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}} \left[ \alpha_{ivk, isig}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}} \big| \mathsf{GOOD} \right]. \end{split}$$

However, by definition of GOOD, when GOOD occurs, we have

$$ivk, isig \in \mathfrak{L} \setminus X_{0,i^*}^{\ell^*} \implies \alpha_{ivk, isig}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^* - 1, 2}} \leq \frac{1}{512 \cdot s_{OSS, \ell^*}(\lambda) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

Since  $|\mathfrak{L}| = s_{OSS,\ell^*}(\lambda)$ , we obtain the desired upper bound on

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKevFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKevFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}|\mathsf{GOOD}].$$

Since  $Pr[\mathsf{GOOD}] \ge 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , we get

$$\mathbb{E}_{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*-1, 2}, X_{0, i^*}^{\ell^*}, \mathfrak{L}}] \leq \frac{1}{256 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

Now, observe that Lemma 15 follows from these two lemmata. To see this, observe that  $W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2},X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}}$  is an upper bound on the total weight on inputs at which the two oracles might differ. Since we have  $W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2},X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*}} = W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2},X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*},\mathfrak{L}} + W^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*-1,2},X^{\ell^*}_{0,i^*},\mathfrak{L}}$  with probability 1, the result follows by the linearity of expectation, Theorem 6 and Jensen's inequality.

{90}------------------------------------------------

### <span id="page-90-0"></span>11.2 Proof of Lemma 16

Fix any  $i^* \in \{1, \ldots, t(\lambda)\}$ . Thus, we will prove  $|\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*,1} - \mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*,2}| \leq \frac{1}{\lambda^2 \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda)}$ . The proof will follow similarly to Lemma 9.

Observe that the difference between the two hybrids is that in  $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*,1}$  we run  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell^*,i^*,1}$  directly, whereas in  $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*,2}$  we instead run  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell^*,i^*,2}$  which simulates  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell^*,i^*,1}$  while using an estimated oracle for its first query to  $\mathcal{O}_2^*$ . We will use the incompressibility property of  $H_0, H_1$  to show that this only makes a difference of  $\frac{1}{\lambda^2 \cdot u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda)}$  in statistical distance.

Let  $\gamma_{ivk,y_0,y_1,z}^{\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}},Y^{\ell^*,i^*,1}}$  denote the query amplitude of  $\mathcal{C}_{\ell^*,2,i^*,1}(Y^{\ell^*,i^*,1})$  on input  $ivk,y_0,y_1,z$  during its first query to  $\mathcal{O}^*_2$ . We also define the following.

$$\alpha_{ivk,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^{\ell^*,i^*,1}} = \sum_{y_0,y_1:\mathcal{O}_2^*(ivk,y_0,y_1,z) \neq \bot} |\gamma_{ivk,y_0,y_1,z}^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*,Y^{\ell^*,i^*,1}}|^2$$

Now let  $(X_{0,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]}$ ,  $(X_{1,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]}$ ,  $(X_{2,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]-1}$ ,  $(D_{0,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]}$ ,  $(D_{1,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]}$ ,  $(D_{2,j'}^{\ell'})_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]-1}$  be the estimated lists and databases in  $Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}$  when it is parsed and fully unwrapped. With abuse of notation, sometimes we will refer to the projection of the sets  $X_{\cdot,j'}^{\ell'}$  onto their elements' (which are tuples) subcomponents also as  $X_{\cdot,j'}^{\ell'}$  (e.g. we will write  $X_{2,j'}^{\ell'}$  to mean the set of pairs (ivk,z) obtained by projecting each tuple in the actual set  $X_{2,j'}^{\ell'}$  to its first and fourth elements) - however, the meaning will clear from context. Now we claim the following.

### <span id="page-90-1"></span>Claim 10.

$$\Pr\left[\left(\bigcup_{\ell'\in[\ell^*],j'\in[i^*]}X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right)\bigcap\left(\bigcup_{\ell'\in[\ell^*],j'\in[i^*]}X_{1,j'}^{\ell'}\right)=\emptyset\right]\geq 1-\mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Proof. Observe that if this intersection is not empty, then there is ivk such that  $ivk \in X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}$  and  $ivk \in X_{1,j''}^{\ell''}$  for some  $\ell', \ell'', j', j''$ . However, by construction we know that this implies that we can obtain  $isig_0, isig_1$  from  $Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}$  such that  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}^*}(ivk, 0, isig_0) = \mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{OSS.Ver}^*}(ivk, 1, isig_1) = 1$ . Since  $Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}$  is obtained by making polynomially many queries to the oracles of OSS, the claim follows by the one-shot security of OSS.

Now we define the following (some dependencies are implicit to keep the notation concise).

$$\begin{split} W_0^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}, X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk, z:\\ ivk \not\in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]} X_{0, j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk, z) \not\in X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}}} \alpha_{ivk, z} \\ W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}, X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk, z:\\ ivk \not\in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]} X_{1, j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk, z) \not\in X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}}} \alpha_{ivk, z} \\ W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}, X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}} &= \sum_{\substack{ivk, z:\\ ivk \in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]} X_{0, j'}^{\ell'}\right) \cap \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]} X_{1, j'}^{\ell'}\right)}} \alpha_{ivk, z} \end{split}$$

{91}------------------------------------------------

Now we make the following claims.

### Claim 11.

$$\mathbb{E}[W_2^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}, X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}}] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda). \tag{2}$$

*Proof.* This simply follows from the definition of  $W_2$  and Claim 10.

Claim 12. For all sufficiently large  $\lambda > 0$ .

$$\begin{split} \mathbb{E}[W_0^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}, X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}}] &\leq \frac{1}{128 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2} \\ \mathbb{E}[W_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}, X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}}] &\leq \frac{1}{128 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2} \end{split}$$

*Proof.* We will only prove the first one (using incompressibility of the random oracle  $H_0$ ), and the second bound follows by the same argument (but this time relying on the incompressibility of  $H_1$ ).

Now we will use the incompressibility property (Theorem 15) of the random oracle  $H_0$  with the predicate P defined as P(ivk||z) = 1 if  $ivk \in S$ , where  $S = \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]} X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right)$ . Note that this set S is exactly the set of prefixes on which our adversary has section queries (otherwise it only makes normal queries and verification queries). In more detail, let  $\mathcal{P}_1$  be the adversary that simulates  $\mathsf{Hyb}'_{i^*,1}$  until the point where  $\mathcal{C}_{1,\ell^*,i^*,2}$  outputs its message, and it also outputs S as its predicate. Then  $\mathcal{P}_2$  simulates  $\mathcal{C}_{2,\ell^*,i^*,1}$  until right after its first query to  $\mathcal{O}_2^*$ . We invoke Theorem 15 for this pair of adversaries, and let  $\mathfrak{L}$  denote the incompressibility list that is promised to exist, and we know  $|\mathfrak{L}| = \ell^* \cdot t(\lambda)$  since  $\mathcal{P}_1$  makes at most  $\ell^* \cdot t(\lambda)$  normal queries. We then split  $W_0$  into two summands  $U_0, U_1$ :

$$U_0^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}, X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}} = \sum_{\substack{ivk, z:\\ ivk \not\in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]} X_{0, j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk, z) \not\in X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}\\ (ivk, z) \not\in \mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_{ivk, z}$$

$$U_1^{\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}^*, Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}, X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}} = \sum_{\substack{ivk, z:\\ ivk \not\in \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]} X_{0, j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk, z) \not\in X_{2, i^*}^{\ell^*}\\ (ivk, z) \in \mathfrak{L}}} \alpha_{ivk, z}$$

It is easy to see that  $\mathbb{E}[U_0] \leq \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$  by the incompressibility of  $H_0$ , thus, we will focus on bounding  $U_1$ .

First we claim that, for all  $\mathcal{O}^*_{\mathsf{QKeyFireSign}}, Y^{\ell^*, i^*, 1}$ , with overwhelming probability we have that any ivk, z that satisfies

$$\alpha_{ivk,z} \ge \frac{1}{512 \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot \ell^*) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

is contained in  $X_{2,i^*}^{\ell^*}$ . To see this, observe that  $X_{2,i^*}^{\ell^*}$  is created by measuring the first query of  $\mathcal{C}_{\ell^*,2,i^*,1}$  to  $\mathcal{O}_2$  for  $512 \cdot \lambda \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot \ell^*) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2$  times. Thus, for any ivk, z such that

{92}------------------------------------------------

 $\alpha_{ivk,z}$  satisfies the above condition, the probability that  $(ivk,z) \notin X_{2,i^*}^{\ell^*}$  is at most  $\exp\{-\lambda\}$ . Now define GOOD to be the event that all  $(ivk,z) \in \mathfrak{L}$  that satisfies

$$\alpha_{ivk,z} \ge \frac{1}{512 \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot \ell^*) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

are included in  $X_{2,i^*}^{\ell^*}$ . Since this is true with probability  $1-\exp\{-\lambda\}$  for each  $ivk, z \in \mathfrak{L}$  individually, and since  $|\mathfrak{L}|$  is polynomial, we have that  $\Pr[\mathsf{GOOD}] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ .

Now we claim

$$\mathbb{E}[U_1 \big| \mathsf{GOOD}] \le \frac{1}{512 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

To see this, first by linearity of expectation we have

$$\mathbb{E}[U_1|\mathsf{GOOD}]$$

$$= \sum_{\substack{ivk,z:\\ ivk \notin \left(\bigcup_{\ell' \in [\ell^*], j' \in [i^*]} X_{0,j'}^{\ell'}\right)\\ (ivk,z) \notin X_{2,i^*}^{\ell^*}\\ (ivk,z) \in \mathfrak{L}}} \mathbb{E}[\alpha_{ivk,z}|\mathsf{GOOD}]$$

However, by definition of GOOD, when GOOD occurs, we have

$$ivk, z \in \mathfrak{L} \setminus X_{2,i^*}^{\ell^*} \implies \alpha_{ivk,z} \leq \frac{1}{512 \cdot (t(\lambda) \cdot \ell^*) \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

Since  $|\mathfrak{L}| = \ell^* \cdot t(\lambda)$ , we obtain the desired upper bound on expectation conditioned on GOOD. Since  $\Pr[\mathsf{GOOD}] \geq 1 - \mathsf{negl}(\lambda)$ , we also get

$$\mathbb{E}[U_1] \le \frac{1}{256 \cdot \lambda^4 \cdot (u(\lambda) \cdot q^*(\lambda) \cdot t(\lambda))^2}$$

which completes the proof.

Observe that Lemma 16 follows from the above claims. To see this, observe that  $W_0 + W_1 + W_2$  is an upper bound on the total weight on inputs at which the two different oracles in the hybrids might differ. Thus the result follows by the linearity of expectation, Theorem 6 and Jensen's inequality.

{93}------------------------------------------------

# Appendix

# <span id="page-97-0"></span>A Alternative Equivalent Definitions for Quantum Protection Notions

We recall the definition of LOCC leakage-resilience for the case of signing and decryption. Note that this is a special case of the general definition [\(Definition 8\)](#page-26-1), and we write the specialized version explicitly for ease of exposition.

Definition 25 (Signature Scheme with LOCC Leakage-Resilience [\[C¸ GLZR24,](#page-94-1) [C¸ G24\]](#page-93-8)). Consider the following game between the challenger and an adversary A.

#### LR − SIGN − GAMEA(1<sup>λ</sup> )

- 1. The challenger samples vk, Rkey ← SIG.Setup(1<sup>λ</sup> ) and submits vk to A.
- 2. The adversary obtains leakage on Rkey adaptively over any number of rounds as in [Definition 8.](#page-26-1)
- 3. The challenger samples m<sup>∗</sup> ← M and submits m<sup>∗</sup> to A.
- 4. A outputs a forged signature sig.
- 5. The challenger outputs 1 if and only if SIG.Ver(vk, m<sup>∗</sup> , sig).

A digital signature scheme SIG is said to satisfy LOCC leakage-resilience if for any QPT adversary A,

$$\Pr \Big[\mathsf{LR} - \mathsf{SIGN} - \mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda}) = 1 \Big] \leq \frac{1}{|\mathcal{M}|} + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

Definition 26 (Public-Key Encryption with LOCC Leakage-Resilience [\[C¸ GLZR24,](#page-94-1) [C¸ G24\]](#page-93-8)). Consider the following game between the challenger and an adversary A.

#### LR − PKE − GAMEA(1<sup>λ</sup> )

- 1. The challenger samples pk, Rkey ← PKE.Setup(1<sup>λ</sup> ) and submits pk to A.
- 2. The adversary obtains leakage on Rkey adaptively over any number of rounds as in [Definition 8.](#page-26-1)
- 3. The adversary A outputs two messages m0, m1.
- 4. The challenger samples b ← {0, 1} and ct ← PKE.Enc(pk, mb) and submits ct to A.
- 5. A outputs a guess b ′ ∈ {0, 1}.
- 6. The challenger outputs 1 if and only if b ′ = b.

A public-key encryption scheme PKE is said to satisfy LOCC leakage-resilience if for any QPT adversary A,

$$\Pr\Bigl[\mathsf{LR}-\mathsf{PKE}-\mathsf{GAME}_{\mathcal{A}}(1^{\lambda})=1\Bigr] \leq \frac{1}{2} + \mathsf{negl}(\lambda).$$

{98}------------------------------------------------

# <span id="page-98-0"></span>B On [HV25]

The initial version (v1) of our paper on arXiV contained a small gap in last hybrid of our quantum key-fire proof, which was communicated to us by the authors of [HV25] and at the same time they put their paper online. Within a day of receiving their communication, we fixed the small gap in our proof and let them know. Current version of our paper does not have this gap (and it has additional results, such as LOCC leakage-resilience security for key-fire and unbounded-message-length incompressibility for OSS) however, we include a discussion here for historical reference.

In [HV25], the authors claimed the following (about the first version of our paper).

- 1. They claimed that the oracles  $\mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0$  that we set to be the signing oracle  $(\mathcal{O}_{OSS.Sign})$  in our incompressible one-shot signature (OSS) scheme construction are not sufficient for signing, and they claimed that thus our claim about existence of 1-bit incompressible OSS was incorrect.
- 2. They claimed that incompressible OSS for multi-bit messages does not follow directly from incompressible OSS for 1-bit messages.

In the following sections we address both of these points in detail. However, a quick summary is given below:

- The first point mentioned was a misunderstanding by the authors of [HV25] regarding the prior work of [SZ25] and our construction. [HV25] claimed that the oracles  $\mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0$  are not sufficient for our signing algorithm, then proceeded to change our signing algorithm (they did not ask us for a clarification) by giving additional access to  $\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}$ , and finally, claimed that our argument is flawed since incompressibility cannot hold given access to oracles  $\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}$ . However, this is incorrect: It is indeed possible to sign using only the oracles  $\mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0$  as shown by various works ([AGKZ20, Shm22, SZ25]).
- The second point was correct and indeed pointed to a small gap in the first version of our key-fire proof: We had implicitly assumed incompressible OSS for multi-bit messages follows in a straightforward manner from incompressible OSS for 1-bit messages, thus we had only given a 1-bit incompressible OSS scheme explicitly.
  - However, first, our quantum fire security proof (as opposed to key-fire, which is a slightly stronger primitive) had already relied on only incompressible OSS for 1-bit messages, and thus this gap did not effect our original quantum fire security proof. Second, for proving key-fire, we had relied on incompressible OSS for multi-bit messages only in the last hybrid of the proof. Thus, this was a localized gap and can be fixed it with a small change to make it rely on only 1-bit incompressible OSS. Overall, it did not affect the main ideas and techniques of our paper. We communicated this small fix to them within a day of receiving their email.

More details now follow.

### **B.1** Signing Oracle

In our incompressible OSS scheme, we have four oracles  $\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}, \mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0$ . We set  $\mathcal{D}$  and  $\mathcal{D}_0$  as the signing and signature verification oracles. We proved that in the presence of the signing and verification oracle (that is  $\mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0$ ), our scheme satisfies an incompressibility property.

The authors of [HV25] claimed that  $\mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0$  are not sufficient for signing, and they claimed that we must include  $\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}$  to the signing oracle  $\mathcal{O}_{\mathsf{Sign}}$ . Then they point out that given  $\mathcal{P}, \mathcal{P}^{-1}$ , the incompressibility property is broken. However, indeed the oracles  $\mathcal{D}, \mathcal{D}_0$  are sufficient for signing

{99}------------------------------------------------

and we do not need to include P,P −1 . In this version, we added a part that recalls the details of the signing algorithm (which is entirely from the previous work) to prevent any future confusion.

To explain in more detail, in the one-shot signature literature, there are two main/well-known signing algorithms, the so-called Grover-style signing algorithm (from [\[AGKZ20\]](#page-93-9)), and the generic signing algorithm from [\[DS23\]](#page-94-12). The confusion from [\[HV25\]](#page-94-8) might be due to the fact that we said that our signing algorithm is as in [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3), however [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3) does not explicitly write out its signing algorithm but rather it is implicit that the signing algorithm of [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3) is the Grover-style signing algorithm. In the one-shot signature literature, it is well-known that the Grover style signing algorithm is used when the quantum signature token takes the specific form of a coset state (i.e., a uniform superposition over vectors from some coset), which is the case for [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3). This algorithm (with small modifications) has been used in many OSS works such as [\[AGKZ20\]](#page-93-9) and [\[Shm22\]](#page-95-11), and it is well understood that this is the signing algorithm for coset based one-shot signature schemes like [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3). Indeed, another follow-up work to [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3) also mentions this Grover-style signing algorithm as the signing algorithm of the [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3) construction: See Section 2.3, Page 11 in [\[BGMS25\]](#page-93-11) where it is also clear that the only oracle being used for signing is D. Note that [\[BGMS25\]](#page-93-11) was put on arXiv on October 10th, which is prior to the publication of [\[HV25\]](#page-94-8).

Perhaps another point of the confusion from [\[HV25\]](#page-94-8) is because [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3) essentially constructs both a one-shot signature scheme and a stronger primitive called a non-collapsing collision-resistant hash (non-collapsing CRH). Specifically, [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3) cites a known result by [\[DS23\]](#page-94-12), which says that a non-collapsing CRH generically implies an OSS. However, the context is to claim a stronger primitive (non-collapsing CRH over OSS), and they do not not mean that the specific construction at hand needs to use this generic transformation to get an OSS. Indeed, in the specific case of the construction from [\[SZ25\]](#page-95-3), their construction is both an OSS directly and a non-collapsing CRH, and the well-known Grover-style signing is to be used for signing when the goal is to obtain OSS directly.

### B.2 Multi-bit Incompressible OSS

We showed the existence of incompressible OSS for 1-bit messages. 1-bit OSS is sufficient for most of our proof, but in the first version of our paper, in the proof of our last hybrid in key-fire security, we had invoked incompressible OSS for multi-bit messages. We had implicitly assumed incompressible OSS for multi-bit messages follow in a straightforward manner from incompressible OSS for 1-bit messages, thus we had only given a 1-bit incompressible OSS scheme explicitly. However in a nice observation, [\[HV25\]](#page-94-8) point out that parallel repetition of a 1-bit OSS scheme to obtain multi-bit OSS scheme, does not preserve incompressibility.

This was a localized issue, and did not affect the rest of our paper. Moreover, this affected only key-fire: Without any changes, our quantum fire security (as opposed to key-fire, which is a slightly stronger primitive) in the first version of our paper still holds using only 1-bit OSS. For key-fire security, by making a small change to our construction and to the last hybrid, we made the proof work using only 1-bit incompressible OSS. When the gap was first pointed out to us by the authors of [\[HV25\]](#page-94-8), we communicated this fix to them within a day of receiving their email.
